Introduction
It depends on all of us.
It depends on you
The Bundestag elections will decide how all of us will fare in the coming years.
We stand up for your concerns, wishes and dreams to finally be taken seriously in this country.
We stand for a policy of reliability and honesty, but also of courage - we want to change.
The Corona crisis clearly revealed the injustices of capitalism: while some people had to fear for their jobs, their children's education and their health, large corporations increased their profits.
We are not resigned to these conditions and are ready to take on the profiteers.
Together, we can all make Germany more democratic.
and socially fairer.
We have it in our hands together.
Our economy must be transformed in Germany, Europe and worldwide in a more social, democratic and environmentally compatible way.
Our democracy will only be stronger if all people can participate in it.
Our future can only be one of solidarity if we begin to shape it in the here and now.
That's what this election is about.
A strong LEFT party is essential for this.
You have the choice.
In our program we show what proposals we have.
We invite you to be part of the change.
And it's a promise to you: DIE LINKE makes the difference.
We have the courage to dare to make the necessary changes.
For more justice, for
peace
and a secure future.
For you.
With you.
We leave no one behind
We leave no one behind.
It is about the realization of fundamental social and democratic rights and human dignity for all.
It is about all people, about their dreams and their right to a good life,
about the realization of the ancient human dream of a world of peace
and social justice, for which so many have fought and are fighting.
We want security and a future for all of our fellow human beings who become anxious and fearful when they think about their wages, rent, electricity bills or old age.
We want trust and social security for all those who have long been overlooked, disregarded and hurt because their concerns and needs count for too little.
We insist that things change because they can be changed.
We leave no one behind in overcoming the corona crisis.
We want to make society and democracy more crisis-proof.
We are concerned with justice and security.
People need recognition and social support again.
In everyday life, at work, in the community and in culture!
We are leaving no one behind in our efforts to combat climate catastrophe.
Climate change continues to indicate, at an accelerated pace, that the capitalist economy is associated with resource consumption and pollutant emissions, with sustained warming of the global climate, with incurable threats to biodiversity and the entire biosphere that can endanger life on Earth even in the short term.
We want a society that is equipped for a change for the better - socially and in terms of solidarity.
Because change needs hope that it can succeed, that everyone can participate and that no one feels excluded.
Change needs social security in a peaceful world.
But change also requires trust.
That's what we're promoting.
We can do it in solidarity.
What moves us
For more than a year, the Corona crisis has dominated our daily lives.
People are worried about their loved ones and their health.
While the pandemic affects everyone, it does not affect everyone equally.
Millions of people work hard and a lot - and get little in return.
This is especially true in the Corona crisis.
People at risk of poverty are at higher risk of losing income or becoming ill.
Even faster than before, social inequality between the global North and South has worsened.
Supported by the private disposal of pharmaceutical patents, the central industrialized countries have created a kind of vaccination nationalism towards economically disadvantaged countries.
We are concerned about all those who are suffering from this crisis of the century due to a virus, but we are also particularly concerned about all those who are now giving everything and getting very little.
Those who hold the store together and earn little have to work even harder.
Recognition must also be expressed on the pay slip!
This applies just as much to employees in retail, catering, daycare centers and social work, to cleaners and delivery staff.
But it's also about art and culture.
It's about all those who are trying to fulfill their dream of self-employment and are having trouble making ends meet.
Millions have been hit by this crisis of the century and they all now need a secure foundation and a social perspective for their livelihoods and their life dreams.
We need to change that.
We can only achieve this together.
For more than a year, people have known what it would take to get a handle on the pandemic, to protect lives and allow people to return to their daily lives.
But the federal government has failed to lead this country out of the crisis: in vaccine procurement, in test supply, in economic assistance.
The grand coalition has helped large corporations, but many people have fallen through the cracks of the rescue nets.
The cultural industry is down.
The government has failed in its pandemic response by putting the profit interests of business above health protection.
It has even already passed on some of the costs of the pandemic to employees.
Those insured by the public health insurance funds bear the bulk of the costs of health care in the pandemic.
To be sure, she was anxious to keep the infection numbers within a range that would not cause the broken health care system to collapse.
But the virus continues to circulate, more and more people fall ill and die.
The country lurches from one half-hearted lockdown to the next.
Sixteen years of Angela Merkel have put a veil over the social differences that so fissure our society, that cause unrest, that divide and have led to anger and powerlessness.
We address these differences and to criticize them.
And we want to overcome them.
It is about more social justice and it is about a fairer distribution of wealth in this rich country and in the world.
We can change that.
The coronavirus pandemic has exacerbated the crisis in our infrastructure
and public services of general interest.
For decades, savings have been made on what is now so urgently needed.
Rightly so, health has never had such a high priority as it does today.
All those who now work in the hospitals, every day, hour after hour, to ensure that no more people fall victim to the pandemic, need better working hours, and they need more pay.
Better salaries in nursing and hospitals not only help employees in concrete terms,
but are an investment in the well-being of society as a whole.
Staff shortages and permanent stress in the health and education systems, for example, must not be allowed to continue.
There is a shortage of caregivers in the health care system,
burdens are increasing, and incomes are not increasing with them.
It has been politically driven decisions that have led to such an unequal distribution of work and burdens in this society.
We are going to change that.
We together with you.
We want to fight with you to strengthen the common good and push back capital interests.
We are fighting for a new economic and social model.
Our alternative is ecological and democratic socialism.
A new policy for all who have long deserved it
Our goal: a new policy for a majority that has long deserved it.
We fight for a strong social infrastructure.
We want public services and administration in a rich country to be truly prepared for crises.
We want everyone to be able to count on receiving protection and help in a crisis.
We want recognition for those who keep society running, and in their wallets too: wages that are enough for a good life.
Our goal: a society of the good life for all.
We want work for everyone that is well paid, covered by collective agreements and fairly distributed.
We want a strong democratic and future-proof welfare state that is financed fairly and protects everyone.
We want a new public service for all, which organizes health, care, education, housing, local transport and energy supply publicly, so that they serve the common good and everyone has the chance to live their dreams.
We propose a left-wing program that leaves no one behind: a plan for rebooting from the pandemic.
A plan for a socially and climate-compatible transformation of the economy and infrastructure.
A plan for a renewed welfare state.
An offer for a crisis-proof society in which people feel safe and secure again.
A policy that would benefit the vast majority of people in this country.
Compliance with fundamental social rights is an indispensable prerequisite for a dignified life in a socially just society.
We are committed to upholding fundamental social rights at all levels of society.
Defend jobs in the crisis and create well-paid, climate-just work: As a result of the pandemic, many industries are facing layoffs and clear-cutting in inner cities.
We want to tie state support to guarantees for jobs and collective agreements - and at the same time set the course for a better future, for secure jobs and a functioning public infrastructure.
We want to significantly expand the equipment for education, training, health and care with an investment program and hire more personnel.
invest in broadband network expansion.
We want to provide investment funds for municipalities to invest in solar roofs, energy-efficient buildings and affordable housing, affordable mobility, culture, sports and attractive city centers.
In this way, we can prevent a clear-cut as a result of the lockdown - and at the same time set the course for the future.
We propose a public transformation fund that secures climate-just jobs for the future
and promotes an ecological change of course.
Our investment program for the future will enable us to create one million well-paid jobs by 2025,
helping to make the economy and infrastructure climate-neutral by 2035.
Good work, fair pay: The many people who keep the store running and yet barely make ends meet at the end of the month urgently need higher wages.
We want to raise the statutory minimum wage to 13 euros so that income from work really does protect against poverty.
Salaries for normal and low-wage earners must increase significantly.
To this end, we want to strengthen trade unions and make it easier to declare collective agreements generally binding.
Temporary work and permanent contracts, mini- and midi-jobs are depressing wages and weakening social security.
As far as possible, we want to transform these jobs into regular, fully socially secure employment relationships.
Stress and overload, while others are left without a job - that doesn't have to be.
Reducing working hours secures jobs in industry and in sectors transformed by digitization - it enables new prosperity for all.
We support the trade unions in their fight for a significant reduction in working hours towards a 30-hour week with full pay and necessary staff compensation.
We want to support this process by limiting overtime and reducing the statutory maximum working hours.
Good health care and dignified care for all: the corona crisis is also the result of neglecting important pillars of a functioning society.
It is wrong that hospitals have to operate according to flat rates per case and with a profit orientation.
Hospitals and nursing facilities each lack100,000 nurses to provide good care.
We want to take hospitals and care groups off the stock market.
We want to transfer private hospitals and care operations that do not operate on a non-profit basis to common ownership.
They must be organized according to need and common good.
We want to replace the system of flat rates per case with needs-based financing.
We want to increase salaries in the nursing sector, which will also help to combat the shortage of skilled workers.
We want to replace two-tier medicine with a solidarity-based health insurance system into which everyone pays.
We want to transform long-term care insurance into full insurance that covers all benefits.
The co-payments for the insured or their relatives, which today drive many people into poverty and despair, will be eliminated.
People must not be excluded from access to medicines and vaccines through patents just to keep pharmaceutical companies' profits high.
The pandemic in particular shows that pharmaceutical research is a public good.
Corona vaccine licenses need to be released to accelerate vaccine production.
For educational equity: Corona highlights the failures in education policy - in staffing ratios, digital equipment and inadequate safeguards.
Equally good education for all children is only possible with a development program for more educators, teachers and social pedagogues.
A legal right to a daycare place also means: the right to good care, small groups, well-paid and trained educators and no fees.
It should go without saying that it doesn't rain through the school roof, the toilets are clean and every child has a mobile device and access to data volume.
A new welfare state: A society that creates security and enables change is only feasible with sufficient and crisis-proof social security.
The pandemic has shown that benefits are far too scarce.
We want to ensure that no one has less than1,200 euros a month at their disposal.
That is our limit for a fair minimum income.
We want unemployment insurance that also covers solo self-employed workers.
The time of Hartz IV has expired.
We are fighting for a minimum income that is free of sanctions, i.e. cannot be reduced.
Away with old-age poverty: In 2000, the pension level was still 53 percent; if the German government has its way, it will drop to 43 percent.
This is a retirement poverty program!
We advocate a statutory pension that approximates the standard of living again - in East and West alike.
To achieve this, we want to reverse the pension cuts and lower the standard retirement age again.
We want to raise the pension level to 53 percent immediately.
Those who currently receive the current average pension of1,048 euros (net) will then receive just under 100 euros more per month.
We want to upgrade the pensions of women and all people who work for low wages so that their life's work finally counts as well.
And no one should have to live on less than1,200 euros net in old age.
Civil servants, members of parliament, freelancers and the self-employed should also pay into the statutory pension in the future.
We want new legal regulations to recognize lifetime work achievements.
Various former GDR citizens have had their pensions arbitrarily limited; we want to abolish this.
Gender justice - time for a self-determined, secure and just life: As LINKE, we stand for a feminism that goes to the roots.
First and foremost, this means distributing work and time fairly between the sexes.
We want a society in which everyone can live freely, safely and self-determined,
have time for family and friends and
at the same time pursue meaningful and well-paid work.
We want a society in which women can participate in political decision-making in the same way as men,
and in which life is not just about paid work.
No return on rent: Corona has forced many people to stay home or work there.
But fewer and fewer can afford their homes.
Rents have exploded in recent years, real estate capital is waltzing through cities promising returns.
We want to make rent caps possible throughout Germany.
Our aim is not only to slow down the explosion in rents, but to put an end to it and reverse it.
Particularly high rents must be lowered.
We want to take real estate groups off the stock market.
It is necessary to create at least 250000 additional housing units per year that are permanently affordable.
Reduce inequality: New Social Security, a fresh start out of the pandemic, and a climate-smart rebuilding program should be funded equitably.
We want to tax high wealth and inheritances more heavily.
Instead of a cheap tax on corporate profits, we want to tax profits like all income.
Our Basic Law provides for the possibility of a wealth tax; we want to levy it again and include multimillionaires and billionaires in the financing of a fair society with a progressive tax rate of up to five percent.
The revenues will enable the states to make urgently needed investments in education, health and housing.
Together with many experts, we consider the debt brake to be economically harmful and want to abolish it.
We propose to raise the tax allowances in the income tax:1,200 euros per month will be exempt from taxes.
This provides noticeable relief for low and middle incomes.
A new start for the East:
We want to finally make good on the Basic Law's promise of equal living conditions.
We are fighting for uniform collective bargaining areas and equal wages in this country.
The pension value for the East must be raised to the West level immediately.
As long as there are still strong wage differences between East and West, the conversion of East salaries should be maintained for pensions.
The equalization of eastern pensions must not be a disadvantage for current employees.
We want to strengthen people's stubbornness, spirit of optimism and solidarity in the East.
No more restructuring of the regions over the heads of the local people!
We propose social and economic councils that give people co-determination.
Digital can also be social: The Corona crisis shows what we have known for some time: Anyone who does not have fast digital access is effectively excluded from a large part of social participation today.
The digital divide in our society not only deepens the existing poverty, but also deprives all those where the Internet is too slow or where there is not enough money for a good connection.
Just as our schools and public authorities need to be made digitally fit,
all citizens, whether in urban or rural areas, have the right to fast Internet access.
Data sovereignty and digital access are part of a basic service guaranteed by the state.
We say: They must become enforceable basic social rights.
For us, this also means that digital participation must never replace social encounters without digital devices.
Social and climate-friendly economic policy: We must achieve the transformation to a largely carbon dioxide-free, energy- and resource-saving economy and infrastructure as quickly as possible if we are to have any chance at all of still achieving the1.5 degree target for limiting global warming.
LEFT economic policy is based on higher wages and secure working conditions as well as democratic decision-making on investments, with which we want to launch a public welfare-oriented and climate-neutral economy.
The industrial structure must become more regional, more crisis-resistant and less dependent on exports.
We want to support the necessary ecological transformation in industry, in particular the automotive supply industry, with a state industry transformation fund worth 20 billion euros per year.
This fund benefits companies that secure jobs, have good wages and nationwide collective agreements.
Decisions on public funding are to be made by regional economic and transformation councils, in which trade unions, environmental and social associations have equal voting rights alongside politicians and companies.
We particularly want to promote cooperatives.
Supporting the retail trade: Online retail, large supermarkets and delivery services have been jeopardizing the retail sector in cities for some time, and not just since the pandemic.
We want to create a legal regulation at the federal level so that states and municipalities can introduce rent caps for small businesses, crafts, cultural institutions, and social and non-profit organizations with legal certainty.
Working conditions in the retail sector are often characterized by poor pay, overtime and, temporary, precarious employment.
Collective bargaining coverage is declining.
Therefore, DIE LINKE demands good wages and working conditions for employees in the retail sector.
Secure jobs and co-determination: We want guarantees for jobs and incomes for employees.
In the crisis and when companies switch to climate-friendly production, a reduction in working hours with a further training offensive can safeguard jobs.
The training is paid for proportionally from a solidarity fund by the companies and the employment agency.
We want to introduce a continuing education allowance.
We want state funds that go to companies as aid payments or subsidies to be linked to long-term job guarantees,
Collective agreements
and binding investment plans for ecological conversion.
We tie public contracts to compliance with collective bargaining agreements.
We want veto rights for employees against cutbacks in companies and effective co-determination in decisions on site closures, mass layoffs and investments in the future.
Consistent climate protection and more quality of life, mobility, agriculture and energy turnaround: We want to expand local public transport, increase the frequency and improve the service - also in rural areas.
We want to reduce ticket prices to zero.
We create good jobs in the production of buses, trains and rails and for employees in public transport.
We are starting with model projects in 15 cities most polluted by exhaust fumes.
We are shifting short-haul flights and freight traffic to rail.
The railroads must be expanded and made affordable for all.
Our traffic turnaround ensures more mobility, but with less traffic.
We want to orient the energy supply to the common good and organize it in municipal utilities and cooperatives.
All energy should come from renewable sources as soon as possible.
We want to help municipalities with climate-neutral conversion
and the creation of good work.
This requires a training and qualification offensive in the skilled trades to meet the demand for skilled personnel in all areas.
We want to ensure good nutrition for all people
and transform the agricultural industry into crisis-proof ecological agriculture.
This is the only way we can guarantee long-term access to enough water and food.
Protecting farmland: We want to strengthen public ownership of agricultural and forestry land and effectively prevent land grabbing.
Among other things, we propose a public land fund that leases to sustainable, local farms on fair terms.
We want to promote cooperative and non-profit use and cap land prices.
In this way, we secure regional food production,
ecological restructuring
and the future of farmers.
Anti-fascism is a foundation of our politics, which is directed not least against the structures that breed fascism:
We oppose all forms of misanthropy and defend democracy - on the streets, in everyday life, in parliament.
We want to strengthen the forces in civil society that are committed to fighting racism, anti-Semitism, antiziganism and neo-Nazis with a Democracy Promotion Act.
The so-called protection of the constitution does not protect democracy, but often right-wing structures.
We want to dissolve the constitutional protection agencies in this form.
We want to promote anti-fascist work in civil society and establish an independent observatory.
We want to set up a committee of inquiry into right-wing terrorism and create investigative focal points against militant neo-Nazis.
We stand up for an anti-fascist culture of remembrance.
Against armament and war: Every weapon finds its war.
We want to ban the export of weapons and weapons factories.
Arms exports to countries that are involved in wars and disregard human rights must be stopped immediately.
DIE LINKE is committed to peace and détente policies.
We want to strengthen civil conflict resolution.
We will end Bundeswehr missions abroad and prevent new ones.
We want to support people from war zones in finding a legal and safe way to escape and advocate for a dignified life outside the war zone.
Especially in a pandemic, the money should go to health care - also internationally - and a fairer global economy,
not to tanks or drones.
Instead of upgrading the Bundeswehr with reference to NATO's 2-percent target, we advocate disarmament and détente
and rational, peaceful international relations; this includes Russia and China.
For us, humanity is indivisible: many people are discriminated against, excluded from social and political participation because of their physical condition, their origin, their poverty, their gender, their age, faith or sexual orientation.
Often they are exposed to psychological and physical violence.
But we want a country in which everyone lives together on an equal footing
and participates in democratic decision-making.
We oppose exclusion, discrimination and violence with our model of an inclusive and socialist society.
That is why we advocate for the right to stay and equal rights.
We want to fight the causes of flight, not refugees.
Misery and death at Europe's external borders must come to an end: Rescue at sea and compliance with the United Nations Refugee Convention must be a matter of course.
We want to evacuate the camps where refugees are locked up in inhumane conditions and fight together for the full restoration of the right to asylum.
Fighting for more democracy:
The Corona crisis has highlighted the shortcomings of existing parliamentary democracy at all levels.
We want crisis management with more democracy, not less.
Parliamentary rights must be strengthened.
All restrictions must be democratically decided, controlled, transparent and regularly reviewed.
Courage to change
Our program for a socio-ecological turnaround that leaves no one behind is not modest.
We stand for a social development in which the domination of capital is overcome by democratic, social and ecological forces and the society of democratic socialism is created.
This federal election is about the future.
It is about deciding the path this country is taking and beginning to take.
This requires big ideas and the courage to change.
We want to have a say.
Our proposals are feasible.
Because things cannot go on as they are.
This election will be about who ends up paying for the cost of the pandemic.
We want a wealth levy and fair taxation of multimillionaires and billionaires to address the costs of the crisis.
We want wages that are enough for a good life.
We want to cap rents
and increase pensions so that pensioners and future generations can live well in old age.
We want everyone to be able to afford good nutrition.
It is about equal living conditions and equal life chances for all children, about justice in education and good schools and daycare centers in all parts of the city.
We are concerned with equal rights for all.
Everyone who lives and works in this country - and who often has a hard time finding a place to live.
Who are affected by racism in everyday life and social structures.
It's about social security for all and being
able to be different without fear.
We are facing major upheavals.
We see this as an opportunity.
We know that the majorities in this country are in favor of more justice,
for social security
and for climate justice.
Here lies a responsibility for us LINKE in the class struggles to be expected: to also use the potential of changes.
We stand for a social awakening after the pandemic - after years of cutback policies and decades of ecological destruction: common good before profits.
Solidarity worthy of the name,
instead of enrichment and corruption.
We need a social awakening.
A new dawn for social security
and a functioning infrastructure,
for peace,
for social
and for climate justice.
The necessary transformation of our economy must not take place at the expense of employees and the population at large.
Neither in this country nor elsewhere.
We want an economy where no worker has to choose between their job and the future of their children.
We want a society in which workers and employees can afford climate protection.
The protection of livelihoods needs a foundation: social security.
Without security and trust, we cannot make our society climate neutral.
A socio-ecological transformation therefore needs just transitions.
We want to create job and income guarantees and one million well-paying and meaningful carbon-neutral jobs.
We can tackle the climate catastrophe together if we do it radically, realistically and justly.
We want to set the course so that our infrastructure and economy, municipalities and industry become climate-neutral by the middle of the next decade.
We no longer have time to just wait for better times.
More than ever, it is about left-wing politics in the here and now,
about a departure for more social democracy
and more climate justice.
We stand for the realization of long overdue social, democratic and ecological changes.
We don't just say how things could be done better.
We also want to do things differently.
Change needs experimentation.
We are focusing on a new culture in political action.
Those who always think they alone are right cannot change the world.
This is especially true for democratic parties and for progressive majorities.
We therefore rely on social alliances and movements.
We trust in more democracy through open dialogue with civil society initiatives and citizens' councils.
We want more participation through referendums.
For us, living democracy means learning from contradictions and criticism.
We ourselves want to remain self-critical as we move forward and change, and become more adaptive, more willing and more determined when it comes to taking up demands from current movements and working them out further.
Pressure from the street needs addressees and multipliers in parliament.
Politics in institutions needs the fuel of social awakening to move forward.
We stand alongside trade unions, social movements, tenants' initiatives, Fridays for Future, Black Lives Matter, Seebrücke, anti-fascist groups, queer initiatives, social associations and the peace movements.
We stand for indivisible solidarity with majorities who keep this society running every day with their paid and unpaid work, with heart and hope.
We take an unequivocal stand against racism, anti-Semitism, anti-gypsyism and any form of misanthropy, against agitation and violence from the right.
We want a socio-ecological
and peace policy change.
We want a new political beginning in our country.
That's what we stand ready to do, and that's what we want to do.
DIE LINKE is willing to compromise when it comes to stride length.
But the direction of the step must be right.
We will not take a step in the direction of social cuts,
rearmament,
privatization
or combat missions of the Bundeswehr.
Our direction is social justice,
Peace
and environmental protection.
Let's walk this path together.
We don't want to talk about people, we want to achieve something together with them.
We want to awaken curiosity and a desire for change in those whose lives are made better by left-wing politics.
We want to win over those who have long since stopped expecting anything from elections.
We want change today.
We make the difference.
That is THE LEFT.
Join in, it's worth it.
Good work, good wages - democracy also applies in the workplace!
DIE LINKE fights to ensure that all working people can live well and securely from their work.
Working conditions must be geared to people and their families, not to the profit interests of entrepreneurs.
The business associations are using the crisis to restrict workers' rights, further depress wages and impose overtime.
When companies get huge economic aid in the Corona crisis and then lay off workers or close sites, we say no!
DIE LINKE stands by the side of the employees and their unions.
We want to defend jobs and collective agreements and expand collective bargaining coverage, abolish the Hartz IV system as an instrument of pressure on wages, stop layoffs and turn the world of work upside down:
Good work that fits in with life must be the rule for everyone, rather than the exception.
To achieve this, we want to implement the following key demands: Wages that are enough for a good life!
We are abolishing the low-wage sector and strengthening collective agreements.
We create a legal right to a full-time position for all employees.
Social security in all employment relationships!
We are pushing back temporary employment and safeguarding all activities through social insurance.
This includes employees through platforms, solo self-employed, and seasonal employees.
Working hours that fit life!
More staff instead of permanent stress.
We support the trade unions in their struggle for a significant reduction in working hours in the direction of a new normal working relationship with 30 hours per week.
We advocate for a right of co-determination in staffing levels and an anti-stress ordinance.
Right to further qualification
with social security!
We create a further training entitlement for all and secure income during further training periods with a further training allowance.
Expanding workforce and public participation in economic issues.
Companies that receive public aid may not at the same time pay dividends to their shareholders or bonuses to their board members.
Wages that are enough for a good life.
An end to low wages
The statutory minimum wage is increased to 13 euros.
Supplements for Sunday, shift or overtime work as well as special payments may not be offset against the minimum wage.
All exceptions to the minimum wage must be eliminated.
Compliance with the minimum wage must be enforced through the obligation to record working hours electronically and more frequent checks.
The number of inspectors at the Customs' Financial Control of Clandestine Employment must be doubled to15,000.
The federal government should establish an official reporting portal against minimum wage fraud.
Collective bargaining agreements must apply to all companies and industries.
To achieve this, the unions' bargaining power must be strengthened and it must be easier to declare collective agreements generally binding.
The latter must be possible at the request of a party to the collective agreement.
The employers' veto right in the collective bargaining committee must be abolished, and it must be considered a "public interest" to strengthen the scope of collective agreements and prevent undercutting competition to the detriment of wages and working conditions.
In addition, it should be possible to extend complete pay scales regulated in collective agreements to companies not bound by collective agreements by means of a legal ordinance in accordance with the Employee Assignment Act.
All collective agreements that have been declared generally binding - even if only for a regional area - must also apply to employees temporarily posted to Germany.
End wage dumping through work contracts and temporary employment.
We want to ban temporary work.
Until temporary work is banned, temporary workers must receive the same wages as permanent employees from day one, plus a flexibility allowance of10 percent.
The awarding of contracts for work and services and the use of temporary labor must be tied to the approval of the works council and compliance with the collective agreements in force in the core company.
To prevent the abuse of work contracts, the burden of proof must lie with employers in future.
The Employee Leasing Act must be tied to the workplace rather than the person of the employee.
It must come to an end that employment agencies and job centers force the unemployed into such undignified working conditions.
We want a legal right to a full-time position.
In order to enforce equal pay for women and men, the right to information in the Pay Transparency Act must be supplemented by a right of action for associations.
Unions must be able to sue for equal pay for their members.
In the event of transfers to companies not bound by collective agreements and in the event of outsourcing, the existing collective agreements in their current version must remain protected indefinitely and also apply to new employees.
A federal collective bargaining law must make compliance with collective bargaining agreements a mandatory requirement for public contracts and also include subcontractors used by contracted firms.
We want binding upper limits for managers' and board members' salaries: they may not be more than twenty times the lowest salary in the company.
Managers' salaries can rise if the lowest wage groups are raised.
Annual salaries in excess of half a million euros may no longer be tax-deductible.
Social security in every employment relationship
All employees are entitled to social security, regardless of their origin and type of employment relationship:
Stop time limits!
Non-cash fixed-term contracts must be deleted from the Part-Time Working and Fixed-Term Contracts Act without replacement, and permissible non-cash reasons must be strictly limited.
In the case of public funding, the temporary nature of budgetary or project funds should no longer be a permissible reason for the temporary nature of employment contracts.
The third employment contract with the same employer must be for an indefinite period.
We want to transform mini- and midi-jobs into jobs that are subject to social insurance contributions.
From the first euro, companies must be subject to a full social security obligation.
Platforms must fulfill employer obligations and pay social security contributions for employees working through them.
The concept of a company and the concept of an employee must be updated and adapted to today's employment relationships and company structures so that labor rights and the works constitution apply to all economically dependent employees.
Clients must also pay social security contributions for solo self-employed persons who work as small entrepreneurs, freelancers, craftsmen, showmen and tradesmen.
To this end, we are creating nationwide industry-specific minimum fee regulations that counteract ruinous price competition and protect solo self-employed workers.
Qualification and further training offers especially for solo self-employed persons must be improved.
All social security exemptions must be eliminated for foreign seasonal workers.
Working hours that fit life
Good life consists of more than work.
Many workers are getting sick from too much work and overtime, while millions are excluded from gainful employment or involuntarily pushed into part-time work.
It is time for a new normal employment relationship.
We want to distribute work fairly in society and between the sexes.
If work were distributed more equitably, instead of overtime and constant stress, more than a million jobs could be created in short full-time 30-hour work weeks.
Such a redistribution of working time increases the quality of life for all.
We want to limit the statutory maximum working time to a maximum of 40 hours per week.
We want to impose stricter limits on exceptions to the maximum daily working time of 8 hours.
We reject a reduction of the required rest periods of11 hours.
Employers must record the beginning, end and duration of the daily working time as well as the duration of the granted rest breaks on the day of work performance.
Business trips and work performed during free time must be fully counted as working time.
Stronger controls by occupational health and safety authorities must be required by law.
Work on call is removed from the Part-Time and Fixed-term Employment Act.
Works and staff councils need a mandatory right of co-determination in staffing levels to prevent regular overtime and performance compression.
We want a right to a temporary reduction in working hours for all employees.
There needs to be a legal entitlement to family-friendly working hours for all those who take on responsibility for raising and caring for children (see chapter "Supporting families where they need it").
We need a legal right for all employees to a six-week caregiver leave with continued payment of wages by the employers (see chapter "For a Left Feminism").
We want to gradually increase the minimum vacation entitlement in the Federal Vacation Act from 24 to 36 working days (including Saturdays).
Each and every employee shall be entitled to at least six weeks of vacation.
Holidays that fall on a weekend shall be made up by substitute holidays during the week.
All employees should be able to do part of their work at home through a right to home office, provided the nature of their work permits this.
The conditions for home office must be regulated by collective agreement or by company/service agreement.
Occupational safety and statutory accident insurance must also apply without restriction in the home office.
There must also be a right to breaks and a right to end working hours in the home office!
However, employees may not be required to work from home.
Right to sabbaticals: Employees should have the opportunity to take a sabbatical year twice in their working lives, combined with a right to return.
Good working conditions, fewer burdens
Work must not make you ill.
The level of performance in companies must be such that health is maintained throughout a person's working life.
The Occupational Health and Safety Act obliges companies to design work in such a way that the risk to mental and physical health is avoided as far as possible.
However, it often fails to be enforced.
We want to create protection against permanent stress and overwork:
We need a regulation to protect against hazards caused by mental stress at work (anti-stress regulation).
Works councils must be able to more easily enforce the rules of the Occupational Health and Safety Act on the prevention of mental stress as well as holistic risk assessments and, above all, remedial measures.
The co-determination rights of works councils must also extend to the prevention of stress.
Employees need an individual "right of veto" in the event of overwork that poses a health risk, in order to also protect employees in companies without a works council.
The occupational health and safety authorities must be better equipped in terms of funding and personnel and be better integrated with minimum wage monitoring in order to enable effective and regular monitoring.
Controls need to be more frequent.
It should be mandatory that they take place on the store floor and not on the record.
Fines for violations of employee health protection must be increased significantly.
It must be made clear in the Occupational Health and Safety Act that it is a criminal offense to continue to endanger the health of employees despite prior warning from the authorities.
Workforces must be given two hours of consultation time per month during working hours to exchange information on work design, working hours, co-determination and occupational health and safety, for contacting occupational health and safety authorities and for developing co-determination initiatives.
The recognition of occupational diseases must be facilitated.
This includes mental illness.
We call for a rebuttable presumption rule in favor of the insured to facilitate the presentation of evidence in occupational disease proceedings.
Independent counseling centers must be set up to support insured persons in asserting their claims.
Disability pensions need to be improved.
Employees with heavy workloads must be able to retire earlier (see chapter "Good pension, good life").
Good work and income to live on, also for people with disabilities.
People with disabilities are disproportionately affected by unemployment - due to lack of accessibility and other discrimination.
We fight for an inclusive labor market without special structures.
No restructuring on the backs of employees: further training entitlement for all
Companies use the introduction of new technologies and products, climate protection and digitization as an opportunity to restructure on the backs of employees, lay off workers or blackmail the workforce.
At the same time, the ecological transformation and digitization are leading to new fields of activity and changing the demands on employees.
Companies must not shift responsibility for training and continuing education onto employees and the general public.
Training measures that are in the interest of the companies must also be financed by them.
Employees whose jobs are eliminated must be protected.
We want a social and ecological transformation with job and income guarantees for employees.
Veto right against clear-cutting, co-determination on the future.
Employees and works councils also need co-determination on economic issues.
This applies in particular to operational changes, site changes and redundancies.
Mandatory co-determination rights are also required in matters relating to occupational health and safety, in-house environmental protection, the planning and design of activities and working conditions, changes to workplaces and the intensity of work.
The right of works councils to negotiate with the actual decision-makers must also be clarified in international corporations.
It must not be the case that companies undermine democratic co-determination rights through holding structures in which the local management acts only as a recipient of orders.
Works councils need an enforceable right of co-determination and initiative for in-company training and further education - and in the realignment of companies.
Companies with more than100 employees are required to carry out qualified personnel planning, which includes further training planning for employees.
All employees must have a legal right to temporarily reduce or temporarily suspend their working hours for the purpose of further training.
Employers must pay partial wage compensation of at least 70 percent of net salary and social security contributions during part-time educational leave.
The state must support educational part-time work for employees by taking greater account of pension entitlements and the amount of entitlements to ALG I.
For low-wage earners, full wage compensation must be guaranteed through government subsidies.
To ensure that all companies contribute equally to the financing of further vocational training, DIE LINKE proposes a further training fund into which all companies in a sector would pay.
Vocational schools and universities must be required by law and enabled to provide continuing vocational education offerings that
are open to all employees, regardless of previous educational attainment.
Further training programs offered by the employment agency and job center must be expanded.
The goal of rapid placement of the unemployed must be eliminated; instead, priority must be given to maintaining qualifications and continuing education.
For the period of further training, a further training allowance amounting to 90 percent of the last net salary is paid.
The period of further training is not counted towards the entitlement to unemployment benefits (cf. chapter "Social guarantees").
Companies that do not provide training must pay a training levy (see chapter "Well trained").
Equal rights for seasonal employees and employees in private households
Violations of occupational health and safety and good working conditions are particularly serious for mobile workers from abroad.
By linking the right of residence to the employment contract, they are particularly at risk of extreme exploitation and find it more difficult to assert their rights.
We want equal protection rights for all and equal pay for equal work.
Equal pay for equal work from the first day must also apply to seasonal workers and employees posted from abroad.
To prevent wage fraud, companies must be required to keep electronic time records that employees can view.
At the same time, we need legal residence status for all workers here, so that controls serve to protect workers and do not become a disadvantage to them.
Termination of employment shall not result in the loss of the right of residence.
Access to information about existing labor rights must be facilitated, and initiatives that advise mobile workers in their native languages must be more strongly promoted.
There must be a clear limit on allowable costs for employer-provided or arranged accommodations.
These are to be based on the applicable non-cash remuneration values from social security law.
Deductions for room and board must be transparently presented on the pay stub to allow employees to verify.
Compliance with hygiene standards in the accommodations must be regularly checked by the supervisory authorities.
All statutory exemptions from social security coverage for foreign employees must be eliminated.
We want to put an end to social dumping when employees are posted to Germany: In the future, social security contributions should be paid in the destination country and registration should have to be applied for one week before the assignment begins.
DIE LINKE wants to strengthen the rights of employees in private households.
Work in private households (including cleaning, care, childcare) is to be organized primarily through certified agencies, public welfare or municipal providers.
They must guarantee collective agreements, permanent employment, the right to a contractual minimum number of hours, occupational health and safety, and continuing education for employees.
In order to reduce exploitation, workers in private households without the right to work and reside must be given the opportunity to legalize.
The exploitation of mostly Eastern European workers in 24-hour care must end.
Care must be organized in accordance with labor law.
Stop Union Busting, Strengthen Resistance, Expand Co-determination
DIE LINKE wants to strengthen democracy in society, in the workplace and in the economy.
The last significant reform of the Works Constitution Act was in 1972, when
there was no temporary work, no outsourcing and no relocation abroad.
There were no permanent contracts, mini-jobs or on-call work.
Forms of employment such as crowd- and clickwork were unknown and employers could not avoid socio-political responsibility disguised as platforms.
Our working world today is characterized by digitalization, globalization, deregulation
and the need for ecological restructuring.
We want to facilitate works council elections and safeguard the ability of works councils to work.
We want to create special prosecutor's offices with sufficient staff for criminal offenses in labor law and works constitution law,
as well as tougher sanctions against employers and law firms that specialize in preventing union organizing.
We want the possibility of direct establishment of works councils by the labor court in cases of union busting in first-time works council elections.
We want to adapt the concept of a company and expand the concept of an employee.
Additional employee representation structures should be able to be determined by collective agreement or works agreement.
We want to extend mandatory co-determination to questions of work organization, staffing levels, precarious employment and qualification.
The transformation of the world of work is a comprehensive societal restructuring with serious implications for labor relations.
It does not take place in a class-neutral way, but as a distributional dispute, inseparably linked to the property question.
Therefore, the extension of mandatory co-determination to economic issues is central.
Employees and their works councils should be able to take the initiative in investment decisions, production depths, relocations, closures of plants and parts of plants, rationalization projects and new working methods and control mechanisms.
This is the only way to get employees on board with the upcoming transformation,
This is the only way to curb precarious work,
This is the only way to realize climate and environmental protection in the companies
and digitalization in the interests of employees and the common good.
DIE LINKE is committed to making it easier to elect works councils.
Protection against dismissal must be extended to all organs of the works constitution and prolonged.
The same co-determination rights must apply to employees in the public sector.
We want to introduce genuine codetermination on a parity basis in the supervisory board of all private, public and public-sector companies with 500 or more employees.
In these companies, the owners and the employees must be equally represented.
The chairmanship is assumed by another person on whom both sides must agree.
Issues of significant importance to the workforce - such as relocations - must be confirmed by employee vote.
Strengthen trade unions
Trade unions must be given a comprehensive right of collective action to ensure compliance with collective agreements and statutory provisions, as well as the right to collective complaints in accordance with the protocol of the European Social Charter.
In defense of the right to strike, the anti-strike paragraph160 of SGB III must be abolished.
The Collective Bargaining Unity Act must be withdrawn, as it entails a restriction of the right to strike.
Solidarity strikes with workers in other companies and industries and political strikes to achieve social improvements and to defend democracy and peace must be included in the right to strike.
The right to strike must also apply to civil servants.
OT memberships ("without tariff") in employers' associations must be abolished.
Workplace co-determination rights and the right to strike must also apply without restriction to church, diaconal and Caritas employees.
Section 118 of the Works Constitution Act must be deleted.
The work of store stewards must be regulated in a similar way to the work of works councils.
Good pension, good life: Solidarity-based employment insurance
We want a statutory pension that restores the standard of living and protects against poverty.
For many people, this is the basis for a carefree and self-determined life.
We reject demands that those who live longer should retire later.
Pensions must not be "secured" via capital markets - then they are insecure.
Old-age provision must be financed equally by companies and employees.
As recently as 2000, the pension level was 53 percent; now it is set to drop to 43 percent.
This is a federal government program for old-age poverty!
We want to end the pension cuts and restore the guarantee promise of the statutory pension insurance.
Three central measures are the starting point: We want to raise the pension level back to 53 percent.
In monetary terms, this means that anyone who currently receives the current average pension of 1,048 euros will then receive 1,148 euros, or just under 100 euros more per month.
The pension level of currently 48.4 percent (without revision effect) can easily be raised to 53 percent within one election period.
With average earnings of 3,462 euros, this costs employees and employers only about 33 euros more per month.
The contribution for a private Riester pension (124 euros) can be waived for this.
Average earners would therefore have 90.50 euros more in their pockets.
We are restoring wage-relatedness in the pension adjustment.
As a LEFT core project, we include all employed persons in the statutory pension insurance.
To this end, we have developed a concept that combines solidarity and social justice with financial solidity and stability.
We are thus strengthening the statutory pension insurance and preventing poverty in old age and in the event of reduced earning capacity.
Our concept of solidarity-based employment insurance offers statutory old-age insurance for the self-employed, freelancers, civil servants, managers and politicians who have not been insured up to now.
We want all employed persons to pay contributions to the statutory pension insurance.
As a guarantee, we are introducing a Solidarity Minimum Pension of 1,200 euros for all those who, despite the pension reform measures, have too low a retirement income to live on.
For those who today have to look back on long periods of poor wages, unemployment or illness are nevertheless entitled to a dignified life in old age.
The Solidarity Minimum Pension is therefore paid by the pension insurance scheme to all people of retirement age - in the case of reduced earning capacity as a supplement, in individual cases also as a full amount - who have a net income of less than 1,200 euros in old age.
The solidarity-based minimum pension is income and asset-tested.
It is financed from taxes.
Maintenance claims in accordance with the BGB are taken into account.
With asset allowances, we ensure that social hardship is avoided and that normal, owner-occupied residential property remains untouched.
Our promise is: No one should have to live on less than 1,200 euros in old age.
The Solidarity Minimum Pension is regularly increased on July1 of each year to the same extent as all other statutory pensions.
With our concept of solidarity-based employment insurance, we are setting the course for a fair, stable and inclusive old-age pension system of the future that is there for all working people.
It will be flanked by the following individual measures: The contribution assessment ceiling (for general and miners' pension insurance and for the old and new federal states) will first be standardized and then drastically increased in several steps.
The level of pension entitlements above twice the average is to be flattened (to the maximum extent permitted by the constitution).
Therefore, a "contribution equivalence limit" is to be introduced.
The private Riester pension has failed.
It cannot close the gaps in the statutory pension.
The contributions and subsidies go into the coffers of the insurance companies instead of into the wallets of the pensioners.
Millions of people with normal and low incomes cannot afford private pension insurance.
We are transferring the Riester pension to the statutory pension on a voluntary basis.
Those who have paid in should be able to keep their entitlements and transfer them to the statutory pension.
We will end the state subsidies of almost 4 billion euros per year and thus increase the subsidies to the statutory pension insurance.
In addition, it is to be made easier for insured persons and their employers to pay additional contributions into the statutory pension insurance scheme on a voluntary basis up to a certain limit.
Employees must not be exposed to risks on the capital market.
We reject the idea of releasing employers from liability in the context of funded occupational pension schemes and so-called target pensions.
This also applies to the waiver of pension guarantees in favor of a pure contribution commitment.
Instead of a company pension scheme financed primarily by employees, we want a company pension scheme financed primarily by employers (as a company social benefit).
Binding collective bargaining agreements are to form the basis for this.
We call for an immediate end to the double contribution of health insurance and long-term care insurance contributions for company pension plans.
One thing is clear: occupational pensions must not be free of social security contributions.
But they are to be paid in the accumulation phase, not in the retirement phase.
However, deferred compensation weakens the finances of the statutory pension scheme and reduces the pension entitlements of all insured persons - regardless of whether they make provision via the company or not.
Inequality is thus exacerbated.
That is why we want to abolish deferred compensation for the future.
We want to abolish the double taxation of pensions.
We want to raise the tax-free subsistence minimum to14,400 euros a year - small to medium pensions would thus be tax-free.
DIE LINKE demands an extension of the transition period until 2070, an extraordinary pension increase and a recalculation of the individual pension allowance.
After all, after decades of contributions, the pension must again secure the net standard of living.
Our neighbor Austria shows that a statutory pension system can protect against poverty, secure living standards and be affordable at the same time.
Instead of making part of the old-age provision dependent on the capital market, the statutory pension system in Austria was expanded into an employment insurance scheme.
We want to achieve the same in Germany.
We want to swiftly implement further improvements in pensions.
Our pension concept provides for: Solidarity compensation for low wages: We want to compensate for periods of low wages.
The so-called basic pension adopted by the grand coalition does not go far enough here.
We want to introduce and improve the "pension according to minimum earning points" for periods after1992 as well.
Full-time employees earning13 euros per hour would then generally receive a pension of around1,200 euros.
With a pension level of 53 percent, for example, a retail saleswoman with a salary of
2,200 euros gross after 45 years of work, almost198 euros more per month than under current law with the so-called basic pension - without an income test!
This would benefit women and those employed in eastern Germany in particular.
Training periods are better recognized and lead to higher pensions.
We value periods of unemployment, child-rearing and caregiving more highly so that they do not lead to poverty pensions.
For each child, three pay points - currently there are over102 euros of so-called maternity pension - are credited to the pension account.
It doesn't matter whether a child was born in 1960 or 2010, whether he or she was born in Frankfurt am Main or Frankfurt an der Oder.
This improvement must be financed entirely from taxes as a task for society as a whole.
All family caregivers acquire additional pension entitlements from their care activities for the entire duration of the care situation, even in care degree1, after reaching the standard retirement age and without reduction if professional care services are also used.
The benefit amounts will be increased.
For regularly performed voluntary and unpaid work of citizens in the organized recognized rescue service, fire protection, disaster control and technical relief organization (THW), appropriate contributions are paid by the state into the statutory pension insurance.
The pension only from 67 must be withdrawn.
Demands for an even higher standard retirement age are unrealistic and irresponsible.
We want to prevent working until you drop.
Everyone must be able to retire without deductions from the age of 65 at the latest.
That can be financed.
If people have paid contributions for 40 years, they should be able to retire without deductions from the age of 60.
People who fall ill should not have to fear another low pension: Access to reduced earning capacity pensions must be made easier.
The decided increase in the bonus period (the time that is "added on" because the insured person was unable to pay into the pension due to reduced earning capacity) for pensioners starting in 2019 must also apply to people who already received a reduced earning capacity pension in 2018 and earlier.
We demand that the unsocial deductions on reduced earning capacity pensions be abolished or compensated by a measure with the same effect.
Contributions must finally be paid into the pension fund again for the long-term unemployed.
We want to finally put an end to the discrimination of East German pensioners.
We demand the immediate adjustment of the "current pension value (East)" to the West level without disadvantaging future pensioners (see chapter "Justice for the people in East Germany").
We are fighting for the Jewish contingent refugees and ethnic German repatriates who have been living in this country for decades and who retired by 2012 to receive at least a one-time payment of10,000 euros per person from the hardship fund that is currently being created, which will not be offset against the "basic security in old age" and other social benefits.
We want to abolish the retroactive inclusion of GDR old-timers in the pension transition legislation and ensure that they receive their pensions promised by the federal government under the Foreign Pensions Act.
Social security for all
We want a strong, democratic welfare state that effectively protects all people against the life risks of illness, accident, old age, need for care and unemployment.
Corona has shown the gaps in our social security systems: For Hartz IV recipients, additional expenses for homeschooling and security masks, for example, are not affordable; the standard amounts alone do not protect against poverty.
Freelancers remain without social security.
Homeless people in collective shelters are at high risk of infection.
Social inequality has increased.
We want a democratic welfare state that gives social rights, strengthens social life through social services and public infrastructures, and provides good and predictable gainful employment that is secure and fits life.
We will not participate in a government that privatizes services of general interest or cuts social services, whose policies worsen the performance of public services.
These are the three pillars of our welfare state of the future: social rights for all that protect against poverty and enable social participation:
We strengthen the welfare state through social guarantees based on solidarity-based pay-as-you-go systems that effectively protect everyone against life's risks.
We guarantee a good standard of living for everyone in all phases and situations of life - including retirement.
We want guaranteed protection against poverty.
We are abolishing sanctions and degrading application procedures.
In summary, we want a guaranteed minimum income of 1,200 euros in every life situation where it is needed.
Social services and public infrastructures that provide access for all: Social services - for example, in health, care, education and social services - and public infrastructures - for example, libraries, theaters, swimming pools, roads, local transport - are therefore central to social cohesion in society.
As part of society's wealth, they are public goods that benefit all members of society and should therefore be designed with the common good in mind.
We understand these services and infrastructures as social property of all citizens.
A "new normal employment relationship" for good and plannable gainful employment that is secure and fits in with life: Meaningful gainful employment, shorter working hours and wages that are sufficient for a good, predictable and secure life.
In this way, we can also push back gender inequality.
Good work also secures tax revenues and insurance contributions for the expansion of the democratic welfare state.
Social rights: A fair insurance against unemployment
Unemployment in Germany has risen again as a result of the Corona crisis.
The increase was higher in the new federal states than in the old ones.
For many unemployed people, this means falling into Hartz IV.
Those who have paid into unemployment insurance for years are still at risk of poverty.
Long-acquired insurance claims are destroyed.
We want unemployment insurance that approximates the standard of living previously achieved.
Employees and employers pay into the insurance.
The goal of our improvements to unemployment insurance is to provide good coverage for as many people as possible.
This also includes employees who have so far been excluded from statutory unemployment insurance (for example, the self-employed and freelancers).
To this end, we are expanding the existing unemployment benefit and introducing a new unemployment benefit plus.
We want a right to gainful employment with an enforceable individual legal entitlement.
This also includes the right to refuse a specific gainful employment.
DIE LINKE is committed to strengthening unemployment insurance: All people - especially career starters - should receive a longer entitlement to unemployment benefit more quickly and long-term employees should be protected from having to switch to the Hartz IV system after a short time.
Reasonable job offers must be based on the principle of "good work".
Blocking periods and sanctions are abolished without exception.
In particular, employees should not be threatened with lock-up periods if they themselves give notice or reject specific job offers.
Qualification and further training are to be strengthened,
unemployment benefits are to be increased to a uniform 68 percent and an unemployment benefit plus (58 percent) is to be introduced, also financed by contributions, the duration of which is to be as long as the previous unemployment benefit, and permanent for those insured for many years.
Annual inflation compensation is intended to prevent a lowering of the standard of living due to price increases.
We want to permanently expand short-time work as a fast-acting means of securing jobs.
Short-time allowance is paid at 90 percent of the last income, and social security contributions are paid in full without interruption.
Companies that receive short-time working benefits from the German Labor Agency are not allowed to make redundancies
or pay dividends to their shareholders.
The employed, who are still excluded from the statutory unemployment insurance (e.g. solo self-employed and freelancers), will also be included in it.
Contributions and benefits are based on actual income; employers are required to make contributions in the same way as employers.
We want to give new perspectives to people who are currently unable to pursue regular employment.
To this end, we are creating a publicly subsidized employment sector with additional jobs that provide a livelihood, are subject to social insurance contributions and are covered by collective agreements.
The offers are voluntary for the unemployed.
Needs-covering and sanction-free individual minimum benefits
We want to abolish the Hartz IV system and replace it with good work (see "Good work" section),
better unemployment insurance (see above)
and a needs-based individual minimum income without sanctions.
To safely protect against poverty, it must currently be1,200 euros.
It applies to the unemployed, those in supplementary employment, the long-term unemployed and those unable to work without sufficient income or assets.
Special needs, for example for the chronically ill or people with disabilities, are granted under the Solidarity Health Insurance or the Federal Participation Act.
In areas with a tight housing market, higher housing costs are also covered in addition to the minimum benefit.
The amount of the sanction-free minimum benefit must be increased annually in line with the cost of living (inflation compensation).
Once during the legislative period, the level of the minimum income is reviewed, ensuring that social participation and protection against poverty are guaranteed.
We want to introduce an independent basic benefit for children (see below).
All persons currently residing in Germany have a right to social benefits that ensure their livelihood.
The Asylum Seekers' Benefits Act (AsylbLG) is abolished.
Asylum seekers and EU citizens living here are included in the individual minimum income.
Immediate measures: Increase the standard rates and abolish sanctions
As an interim step until the introduction of a sanction-free minimum income, we want an immediate increase in the current basic security benefits to 658 euros plus the assumption of housing and electricity costs in the actual amount.
In addition, we demand a flat-rate supplement of 100 euros per month for the duration of the corona pandemic for all recipients of Hartz IV and basic benefits.
We share this demand with many social associations and trade unions.
Durable consumer goods such as refrigerators and washing machines (so-called white goods) are not covered by standard needs.
Their acquisition must be fully covered if necessary.
The funds for mobility must correspond to real prices.
We advocate a social ticket for local public transport.
In the long term, we want free public transport for everyone.
All previous federal governments have deliberately reduced what people need to live.
This must stop.
We agree with many social and professional associations on this.
The costs of housing and heating must be covered to an extent that corresponds to the actual supply of housing on site (and not just that deemed "appropriate" by the Job Center).
Currently, municipalities often set reasonable housing costs far too low.
The contributions for memberships in tenants' associations are to be taken over by the Jobcenter.
The previous principle of so-called "need communities" is no longer up to date.
We want to replace it with individual claims (respecting the legal maintenance claims).
Digital connectivity has become a mandatory requirement for social participation in our society.
That's why we're calling for one-time benefits for the digital equipment of adults.
The ongoing actual costs for digital must be included in the standard rates.
School-age children on benefits are to receive a one-time subsidy for computers, printers and other IT equipment as an immediate measure.
The subsidy is to amount to 500 euros and is to be granted unbureaucratically.
We will transfer the IT supplement to our stand-alone basic child allowance as soon as it is established (see below).
Freedom from sanctions!
All sanctions, i.e. reductions of the subsistence level, must be excluded.
With its ruling of November 5, 2019, the Federal Constitutional Court has already drawn a necessary red line against the previous sanctions practice.
The basic right to social participation must also be implemented for recipients of basic social security benefits.
The current sanction regulations in SGB II and the benefit restrictions in SGB XII must be abolished.
The socio-cultural subsistence minimum is a fundamental right and must not be undercut by sanctions.
To ensure that legal assistance is also available to people with low incomes, we call for the expansion of legal costs and counseling assistance.
We want to abolish the co-payment for counseling assistance.
We want to change the criteria for approval and for the use of income and assets in favor of amounts that actually cover needs.
We want to abolish the four-year downstream review of the granting of legal aid.
We are also committed to free and independent advice centers.
A nationwide network of self-organized social counseling centers is needed to ensure that no one has to go to the office alone and to facilitate the exchange of information among those affected.
Their operation must be financed by federal grants.
Precarious employment and unemployment, high rents and illness drive people into the poverty trap and thus inevitably into the debt trap.
The 2020 reform of consumer insolvency proceedings is not sufficient.
We say: Get out of the debt and poverty trap!
People who have already been consistently registered in the "debtors' tower" (public debtors' register) for at least 72 months are to receive a shortened full discharge of residual debt of 12 months.
Schufa and other private information files should no longer be allowed to provide information about applicants' debts and current loans when they apply for housing.
For landlords, the declaration of freedom from rent debts must be sufficient as a control instrument.
We want to prevent debt before it arises.
To this end, we want to strengthen debt counseling centers and introduce mobile debt counseling in rural areas.
We want free legal help for every affected consumer without conditions.
Everyone in DIE LINKE is committed to the fundamental goal of safely protecting all people from poverty
and guaranteeing social participation.
This guarantee makes the idea of a basic income attractive to many.
Many others, however, consider this idea unsuitable.
For us, this goal is the reason to advocate for a sanction-free minimum income of1,200 euros for everyone who needs it: whether retired, on short-time work, unemployed or studying - no adult should have less.
We are conducting controversial social discussions on an unconditional basic income and will decide next year in a membership vote whether to change our stance on this.
Overcoming child poverty: Child Basic Security
Child poverty is always income poverty of the parents.
Good social infrastructure, good wages and social guarantees are important components in the fight against child poverty.
In addition, there is a strong child and youth welfare system and a poverty-proof basic child benefit system.
We eliminate child and youth poverty with two approaches:
financial support for material and monetary poverty,
infrastructural services (public transport, children's and youth recreational facilities, music schools, libraries, etc.) open doors and create participation in social life - low-threshold, barrier-free, close to home and, if possible, free of charge.
Together with social associations, trade unions and other social actors, we are calling for an independent basic child benefit.
It must be easy to understand, transparent and fair.
We are basing the design on the model of the Bündnis Kindergrundsicherung.
The height is graduated.
Starting at 630 euros for the poorest children, it is reduced to 328 euros depending on their income situation.
This corresponds to the increased child benefit that we are demanding for all children as an immediate measure.
It is paid monthly to all families regardless of income.
As an immediate measure, we are increasing child benefits for all children to 328 euros per month.
It is paid to all families regardless of income.
Children from poor families additionally receive a supplement of up to 302 euros, staggered according to age, as an immediate measure in addition to child benefit.
In addition, the actual accommodation costs as well as one-off and special needs (school trips, IT equipment, etc.) should also be taken into account for children.
The basic child allowance applies to all children and young people up to the age of 18 and to young adults up to the completion of their first school education (including high school graduation).
With our basic child allowance, we are replacing the existing bureaucratic, restrictive and non-transparent social security systems for children of low-income families.
The advance on maintenance payments remains in place.
The basic child benefit is a benefit exclusively for the child.
It is not counted as income of parents or other household members when receiving social benefits or within tax law.
We want to expand the offers for children and young people for participation in social life and for personal development - barrier-free, close to life and as free of charge as possible.
The municipalities must be given appropriate financial support to provide child and youth welfare services, sports facilities, indoor and outdoor swimming pools, cultural and educational facilities, and public transport services that are geared more closely to the needs of young people.
We want a real participation law for children and young people.
The current provisions in Paragraph13 SGB VIII are mere declarations of intent.
We want to make it a legal right to social participation.
Supporting families where they need it
Low wages and unemployment result in family, child and youth poverty.
The situation is particularly dramatic for single mothers and fathers who are on Hartz IV benefits.
LEFT family policy aims to enable all people to live a good, predictable life without fear of the future - for all family forms, regardless of origin, sexual orientation and gender identity (see chapter "Reproductive Justice").
To this end, we want to expand social and public infrastructures and services and introduce good social safeguards to make family and career more compatible.
