Fee-free public childcare for children of all ages: Parents need childcare facilities that have flexible opening hours to ensure a work-life balance.
At the same time, employees need good working conditions, good wages and better care ratios.
Public childcare services, especially for children from the age of one, must be expanded so that their legal entitlement to educational support can be met (see the chapter on "Education").
Minimum parental allowance, longer duration: In order to better reconcile family and career, we want to extend the parental allowance to 12 months per parent (or 24 months for single parents).
The parental allowance applies individually and is not transferable to the other parent.
It is valid until the child is seven years old.
We also want to raise the minimum amount of parental allowance to 400 euros and, in the case of parental allowance plus, to 200 euros accordingly.
No offsetting of parental allowance against transfer benefits: Since 2011, parental allowance has been offset against Hartz IV benefits, for example.
In particular, families with little or no income who rely on government assistance have since been excluded from the benefit.
Working time models that enable mothers and fathers to reconcile their careers with family and private life.
Instead of a flexibilization of working time that is oriented only to operational requirements, employees need time autonomy and gainful employment that fits in with life and can adapt to the requirements of the different phases of life (cf. chapter "Work, family-friendly working hours").
Parents need special protection against dismissal until the child reaches the age of six.
More sick days for children: Due to the corona pandemic, sick days for children were extended by ten additional days per child for parents with statutory health insurance until the end of 2021 and by an additional twenty days per child for single parents.
We want a permanent extension of pediatric sick days.
This must also apply to employees in mini- and midi-jobs, the self-employed and freelancers!
Additional parental protection: We want additional parental protection of ten days paid time off for the second parent after the birth of the child.
Gender-equitable tax models instead of spousal splitting.
The unused taxable minimum income should be transferable between spouses or partners.
In custody and access rights, the focus must be on the best interests of the child and must continue to be examined on a case-by-case basis.
We want to anchor children's rights in the Basic Law.
More staff in youth welfare offices: Parents need expert advice and support.
These are tasks of the youth welfare offices that they are often unable to perform due to a lack of staff and under-resourcing.
We demand that youth welfare offices be adequately staffed and equipped.
This applies in particular to psychological personnel and mediators.
Self-determined in old age
How people want to live in old age, in well-deserved rest, active and socially engaged, involved in the family or in other relationships of solidarity, must be their free decision.
Older people must be involved in all areas of life that affect them - as experts in their own lives.
The ability of older people to participate in society must be guaranteed without restriction, taking into account the special features of this stage of life.
Communication, administrative and community services should be available in an age-appropriate and barrier-free manner.
We are fighting for a society based on solidarity in which the young and the old are not played off against each other.
A society in which people can age with dignity (see the chapter on "Pensions").
Create age-appropriate, non-profit (for example, cooperative), inclusive, and diverse housing and care options.
They should enable the coexistence of different generations, nationalities, religions, genders, people of different sexual orientation or empowerment.
Older people should be able to remain in their own homes and familiar living environment for as long as they wish.
Effective aids and concepts against social isolation and loneliness in old age.
Community outreach services for seniors and community meeting places are public and must be funded.
Good and age-appropriate health care, outreach and education without violating patient self-determination.
Individual decision-making authority through health care proxies and living wills is to be promoted regardless of social status.
Health and nursing care must be professional, close to the patient's home and made a mandatory municipal task.
We want to strengthen co-determination rights for seniors at the federal, state, district and local levels.
In particular, the rights of senior citizens' representatives are to be expanded and strengthened on a nationwide basis.
We want an independent participation law for seniors that establishes the legal right to full social participation, for example, the right to barrier-free housing and health care close to home in old age, and makes the municipalities responsible for this.
It is intended to take up the existing services and offerings from Section 71 of the Social Code XII and develop them further under the aspects of self-determination and self-empowerment.
Good infrastructure: Even in rural areas and in nursing homes, people must have access to public administration, retail and utilities.
Public transportation, on-call buses, and mobile utility services are to be expanded.
Fast Internet and hardware for digital participation are a prerequisite for a self-determined life in old age and should be expanded with public funding in line with the needs of the elderly.
Stop the nursing crisis!
System change in health and care
The Corona crisis made it clear to everyone that the health care system was organized incorrectly:
the hastily established emergency hospitals could not be operated in many places because there were not enough staff.
Due to the lack of sufficient protective clothing, many nurses and medical staff became infected.
This exacerbated the care shortage,
and in some cases violated basic rights of people in need of care.
The federal government could have known better after the spring.
But it has not increased hospital and nursing staff, it has not given the pharmaceutical companies clear guidelines for the production of the vaccine.
Even before Corona, the normal state of affairs in German hospitals was: hardly any time for attention, poor hygiene, more accidents and avoidable deaths.
The federal government has not presented a strategy on how to stop the nursing shortage in hospitals and care facilities.
The policies of federal governments that ensure private corporations and investors can make big money off our insurance premiums, co-pays, copays and exploitation of health care workers are endangering our health!
That must be an end to it!
We are all potential patients and people with care needs.
We expect to be well cared for in nursing homes, hospitals and in the outpatient sector.
DIE LINKE stands by the side of the employees who have been fighting for these goals for years.
The nursing emergency must finally be stopped!
100000 nursing staff more in the hospitals and 100000 nursing staff more in the nursing homes and 500 euros more basic salary!
The many trainees who have left the profession are to be won back with attractive working conditions.
We need a statutory staffing level for all professions in hospitals and in outpatient and inpatient care facilities!
In hospitals, we want to stop and reverse staff cuts and outsourcing.
We support workers' struggles for the reversal of outsourcing and privatization (for example, of kitchen and cleaning services or logistics).
It must apply: One house, one tariff!
The current financing of hospitals via the system of so-called flat rates per case (DRG) creates false incentives: diagnoses that are worthwhile are made more often.
Hospitals are being put under competitive pressure.
Individual health needs are no longer the focus.
We demand the abolition of flat rates per case!
The operating costs must be fully refinanced by the health insurance funds.
We want to transfer hospitals into municipal, public or non-profit ownership.
Profits from hospital operations must not flow into the pockets of owners and shareholders.
That is why we need a ban on taking profits.
Possible surpluses must remain in the company.
If profit withdrawals are no longer possible, private corporations lose the incentive to operate hospitals.
We call for a federal remunicipalization fund to prevent further privatization and support deprivatization efforts.
The planning rights of the federal states must be strengthened vis-à-vis hospital operators.
We facilitate and promote the creation of municipal hospital associations.
We want to enforce good working conditions in the care facilities.
To this end, the Long-Term Care Provident Fund is to be converted into a Long-Term Care Workforce Fund.
Medical treatment care, must also be fully covered by the statutory health insurance in inpatient care facilities and facilities for the disabled.
Additional nursing staff can thus be employed on a regular basis and better paid.
The basis for this must be a generally binding area-wide collective agreement, at least at the level of the collective agreements for the public sector (TVÖD/TV-L), for all employees, which also applies to private and church sponsors such as Caritas and Diakonie.
DIE LINKE calls for a needs-based, high level of skilled labor, including on the night shift in nursing facilities, to be implemented on a binding basis throughout Germany and to be effectively monitored for compliance.
Until the introduction of scientific staffing levels in nursing care for the elderly, a specialist staffing ratio of at least 50 percent applies.
Decent care cannot and must not be geared towards profit.
Currently, the majority of nursing home places and outpatient care services are privately organized.
The statutory entitlement to profit, the so-called risk surcharge, for which the state pays in case of doubt, must be abolished without replacement.
The cost spiral of ever-increasing co-payments must be broken.
Until full long-term care insurance is introduced, co-payments must be significantly reduced and capped immediately.
No transnational care corporations: we need licensing controls that include a domestic tax credit.
Care facilities must operate on a non-profit basis.
Good care is provided locally: local authorities must be enabled to bring care facilities under public or non-profit responsibility and democratic control.
DIE LINKE rejects the introduction of nursing chambers.
The federal and state governments must fulfill their obligation to invest and ensure the necessary infrastructure.
For comprehensive planning of the care landscape, we want to introduce care demand planning analogous to hospital demand planning.
We want to secure outpatient care services and solo self-employed caregivers by organizing them on non-profit platforms and enforcing employment relationships that are subject to social security contributions.
DIE LINKE is committed to strengthening qualifications
and improving pay in the health and medical professions.
Education and training in health professions must be free of charge and work performance during training must be remunerated.
In the case of continuing education, employees should be paid according to their basic occupation.
For psychotherapists in training and continuing education, this must apply throughout their practical work.
DIE LINKE supports the union's commitment to nationwide training regulations and apprenticeship pay in the healthcare industry.
We demand nationwide regulations for the recognition of curative education nurses as specialists in the care of the disabled.
A new solidarity-based health insurance!
The general welfare must be the priority in health and care - not the profit opportunities of individual corporations.
The actual need must be the decisive factor in planning our health and care landscape, not whether investors expect a return on investment.
Funding needs to be put on a new footing.
We need a solidarity-based comprehensive health insurance.
Everyone pays in, contributions are levied on all incomes, everyone is well taken care of.
Co-payments and co-payments will be eliminated in the future.
With the abolition of the income threshold, the contribution for health insurance will fall from around15 percent to around12 percent of gross wages.
Until the introduction of a solidarity-based health insurance system, contributions for the self-employed and others voluntarily insured in the statutory health insurance system (SHI) must be more closely aligned with real income.
For people with a monthly income of less than 6,200 euros, contributions will fall in absolute terms.
This concept will relieve the financial burden on the vast majority of the population, including many self-employed and pensioners.
Employers and insured persons each pay half, i.e. less than six percent.
An end to two-tier medicine: We want to abolish the separation between statutory and private health insurance.
Everyone pays into the solidary health insurance according to their total income (earned income, capital income and other income) and receives all medically necessary benefits, including full medication, glasses, dentures or physiotherapy.
Medically unnecessary treatment of privately insured patients for profit is a thing of the past.
Several hundred thousand people still have no health insurance coverage - almost fourteen years after the introduction of compulsory health insurance!
That is why we demand that all people living in Germany receive necessary health services without restriction.
People without health insurance must be able to be admitted without going into debt.
Contributions for the self-employed and others voluntarily insured in the SHI system must be based much more closely on real income.
We call for an end to the reimbursement of non-evidence-based treatments by SHI.
A solidarity-based comprehensive nursing care insurance
Long-term care insurance does not cover the cost of care; it is a partial benefit insurance.
More and more people cannot afford good care, have to go into debt or end up on welfare.
We want to fundamentally restructure long-term care insurance: With reliable, fair and future-proof funding, we can provide good working conditions
and ensure good care according to scientific standards.
The municipalities are relieved because fewer people become dependent on social welfare as a result of care costs.
We stand by the participation-oriented concept of care: there must be time for activating care and listening, for attention and support.
Care services include assistance for people with disabilities.
Assistance services should ensure participation in public life for as long as possible.
Our solidary comprehensive nursing care insurance covers all nursing care benefits.
People with care needs and their families do not have to pay a co-payment.
No care service may be refused for cost reasons.
Care services should be provided in high quality by well-paid professionals.
Family care and neighborhood involvement can be complementary and should not be provided out of necessity.
People who are dependent on social assistance receive the same benefits as all other people with care needs.
Private long-term care insurance must be transferred to the statutory system.
The financial burden must be shared fairly among all shoulders.
Civil servants, members of parliament and the self-employed must also pay into the solidarity-based health and long-term care insurance scheme in proportion to their incomes: even on income from capital gains and without an assessment ceiling that spares millionaires.
In this way, we are creating the financial basis for solidarity-based comprehensive long-term care insurance.
Against exploitation, workers in private households without the right to work and reside must be given the possibility of legalization.
Preference should be given to organizing care work in private households as regular employment through public agencies, care platforms, public welfare or community providers.
These must guarantee collectively agreed pay, permanent employment, the right to a contractual minimum number of hours, occupational health and safety, and further training for employees (see the chapter on "Labor").
For a vacation in EU countries, the costs of foreign nursing care benefits are to be covered by the German nursing care insurance.
Relieve the burden on family caregivers!
The gaps in our care system are filled by unpaid work of family members.
Most often it is the women - spouses and partners, daughters and daughters-in-law.
In everyday life, many carers struggle with constant stress, exhaustion and money worries.
Many limit their professional activities or give them up.
This reduces their income and their own pension entitlements and leads caregivers into old-age poverty.
The relief budget announced in the CDU/CSU and SPD coalition agreement was not introduced.
The greatest relief for both people with care needs and their family caregivers is professional day and short-term care that is close to home, non-commercial, and covered by a solidarity-based comprehensive care insurance, as well as relief services that are accessible without red tape.
They need to be expanded and brought together.
People with care needs and family caregivers should be able to decide for themselves which form of care and which support services they need and want in which mix in their lifestyle.
The interest groups of care-giving relatives and people with care needs need a seat with voting rights in all care committees at the federal level - such as the quality committee - and in all regional care conferences.
As part of the solidarity-based long-term care insurance system, we want to create an advisory council for people with care needs and family caregivers, which is to be consulted on all projects affecting them and is to be given the right to propose legislative initiatives.
Local care initiatives must be publicly funded on a permanent basis as part of self-help.
For more transparency, networking and self-determination, we need care platforms that employ care workers with social insurance and collective wage agreements.
The widespread 24-hour care provided by only one caregiver living in the household of the person with care needs is based on systematic violation of the Working Hours Act.
We reject current proposals to make this form of care subject to social insurance contributions through the employment model of quasi-employee self-employment.
They do not fix the fundamental problem, but perpetuate it and do not change the system of organized exploitation.
Eastern European caregivers must not be allowed to relieve the financial burden on family caregivers and cushion the German care crisis by foregoing minimum wages and social benefits!
DIE LINKE expressly recognizes the desire of older people for autonomy in old age and living in their own homes.
Support in managing everyday life through home care, which is necessary for this purpose, must be repositioned on the ground of the current labor law.
Currently, there are no true wage replacement benefits for family caregivers who are still working.
We want all employees to be given six weeks' leave with full employer-financed wage compensation the first time a family care case arises.
It must also be possible to reconcile care and work and prevent poverty when taking over home care for a longer period of time.
Together with the interest groups of caring relatives, social associations and trade unions, DIE LINKE is developing a concept for a leave of absence for working carers and relatives with wage replacement.
We want to abolish the thresholds in the Caregiver Leave and Family Caregiver Leave Act.
There needs to be a nationwide legal entitlement to family-friendly working hours for all those who take on responsibility for raising and caring for children, including a right to return to one's own job or an equivalent job (cf. chapter "Supporting families where they need it").
Strengthen public health service!
For years, savings have been made in the staffing and equipment of the public health service (ÖGD).
In the course of the corona pandemic, it became apparent how irresponsible this was: important tasks, such as school enrollment examinations for all children in a given year, were no longer being performed.
The capacity limits were quickly reached.
Instead of calling on the Bundeswehr for helpers, the German Federal Agency for Technical Relief (THW) must be better equipped to deal with extreme emergencies.
DIE LINKE wants a financial strengthening of the ÖGD and better coordination.
The work of the ÖGD must focus on the social component of health.
Pandemic and disaster preparedness plans must be updated and regularly reviewed for functionality at the municipal level by the ÖGD.
The social component of health must be at the center of the work of the ÖGD.
It must be given a leading role in prevention issues.
The federal government must provide funding for the creation of state health departments in the states.
The federal government must ensure that advance costs for materials and treatment capacity are fully covered.
We want the ÖGD to play a leading role in providing low-threshold vaccination services and in prophylaxis against infections in daycare centers, schools and companies.
In all federal states, a legal regulation is needed for a mandatory invitation and reporting system for participation in preventive medical checkups for children.
Menstrual hygiene products should be provided free of charge by public health departments (see chapter on "Feminism").
Fighting health inequality!
Health is a central prerequisite for the social participation
and self-determination of every individual.
It is well known that the social situation has a decisive influence on health: People who are poor get sick more often and die earlier.
The gap between rich and poor is widening particularly rapidly in Germany, with the result that inequality in health opportunities continues to rise.
Health is largely determined by people's living and working conditions.
This development was exacerbated by the corona pandemic and the federal government's handling of it.
Medical research and treatment of disease are driven by a gender data gap, with the male body as the norm.
As a result, women often receive, for example, a treatment and dosage of medication that is harmful or even life-threatening for them.
The link between social situation and health must be the focus of health policy.
On the one hand, this concerns access to good nursing and health care.
Even more important, however, is to see the promotion of health opportunities as a task for all policy areas, from education and transport to the environment, consumer protection and foreign policy.
We therefore want any legislative initiative to be examined by an independent body for its impact on health inequities.
We demand the introduction of the anonymous health card, which allows illegalized people to access health care.
We want to consistently remove barriers from the healthcare system.
This means not only removing barriers to accessing doctors' offices, hospitals and healthcare facilities, but also adapting examination techniques and communication to the special needs of older patients and people with disabilities.
Easy-to-use language, legible and understandable patient information, and appropriate counseling services must become a matter of course.
In order to give medical and nursing staff more confidence in dealing with people with disabilities in a natural, needs-oriented and non-discriminatory way, we are committed to implementing special modules in education, training and continuing education.
They are to be carried out by expert peer workers.
The self-determination rights of people with disabilities in care and in (partially) inpatient facilities must be guaranteed.
This also includes taking personal assistance to medical examinations and inpatient hospital stays as well as to visit preventive care and rehabilitation facilities, even if it is not organized through the employer model.
Patients must be at the center of healthcare.
What is a phrase for many, we want to fill with life.
No decision about health and care provision should be made without the active participation of patient representatives.
In order for self-help to secure its independence and meet the large associations and companies in the healthcare sector on an equal footing, it must be adequately funded.
The funding procedures must be transparent and unbureaucratic.
We strengthen the living will: Comprehensive self-determination must also be possible in extreme situations, and all young people should be informed of their rights in this regard at an early stage.
We want to place people with mental impairments on an equal footing before the law and in social insurance schemes, and give them access to an inclusive labor market.
We want a non-violent psychiatry and the abolition of special laws in this regard.
The spatial conditions and staffing must enable treatment without coercion and violence.
We want to promote a gender-sensitive view of health and illness in research and continuing education.
Patient data protection must also apply to privately insured young people
POC and people with a migration history are entitled to treatment free of discrimination and violence.
Outpatient care: Good local, urban and rural care
On average, Germany has a high physician density, but long distances and long waiting times have to be accepted in some cases, and not only in rural regions.
DIE LINKE advocates good, comprehensive, barrier-free and needs-based health care in cities and rural areas.
Criteria for good health care must be: Proximity to home and accessibility by public transport, short waiting times for an appointment and good emergency care, accessibility and age appropriateness.
In the medium term, regional care centers are to become the backbone of health care close to home.
They should coordinate outpatient as well as acute inpatient, emergency medical, psychotherapeutic, (community) nursing and other therapeutic treatments in a region and serve as a central point of contact for all patients*.
In this way, we want to provide care from a single source
and promote cross-professional working with family-friendly working hours.
The regional health centers form important interfaces with other areas of care such as youth welfare, integration assistance, addiction assistance and other services.
They should also work in a preventive and community-oriented way, especially with regard to the social, economic and ecological prerequisites of health.
We want inpatient and outpatient care to be planned and designed together according to the interests of the common good.
Psychotherapists, physical and occupational therapists, speech therapists, podiatrists, midwives and pharmacies must also be accessible everywhere.
We want to establish joint planning committees at the state level with the participation of patient representatives, states and municipalities, physicians, hospitals and health insurance companies.
We want to examine the possibility of limiting purchase prices for "cash seats" for physicians and psychotherapists.
We support model projects for new forms of care, such as the existing and emerging district health centers and polyclinics.
To enable them to fulfill their claim to integrated, multiprofessional and social-space-oriented care, we advocate the introduction of a new form of service provision in the Social Code.
We want a public liability fund to make midwives independent of private insurance.
Midwives should be the first point of contact for pregnant women and prenatal and postnatal care - as in the Netherlands.
Midwives are the accompanying and caring professionals during childbirth.
We support the midwives' association's call for an obstetric care strengthening law with the goal of one-to-one care during childbirth.
The cost of day-to-day operations in obstetrics departments must be funded by health insurers in a way that allows these departments to cover their holding costs and pay midwives based on performance with good staffing ratios.
In many regions, psychotherapeutic care falls far short of demand.
Demand planning urgently needs to be revised in this area in particular.
The financing of the therapy must also cover the need.
In this way, we want to make the questionable reimbursement practice of the health insurance companies obsolete.
By operating medical care centers, corporations are trying to create profit opportunities for themselves in the outpatient sector.
We want to reverse this development.
Break the power of the pharmaceutical industry!
Democratize health research!
The statutory health insurance funds in Germany spend over 41 billion euros on pharmaceuticals - with a rapidly rising trend.
For cancer, rheumatism and multiple sclerosis drugs, fantasy prices are paid in the first year after approval.
Drug prices must be effectively capped by law.
Patients are burdened by high co-payments.
They must pay for most non-prescription medications entirely out of pocket, even if they are prescribed by a doctor.
We want all patients to be provided with safe and effective medicines based on the latest scientific knowledge - regardless of their income or disease.
All drugs with proven benefits must be fully reimbursed.
A positive list must be introduced for this purpose.
Drug research not only determines whether drugs are developed that are really needed,
but also who owns the property rights,
which prices are called,
whether the research results are made transparent
and, last but not least, whether people in the Global South can gain access to innovations.
For DIE LINKE, pharmaceutical research is a public task.
We want to push back the influence of the pharmaceutical companies.
This concerns advertising and influencing of physicians, science and patient organizations.
We demand a transparent, legal regulation of donations from the pharmaceutical industry to medical professionals.
We want to fight corruption in the healthcare sector.
Results of drug studies must be published.
Negative study results must not be suppressed.
The production of medicines and medical devices must not be subject to the profit interests of shareholders.
The pharmaceutical industry must be committed to the common good and placed under democratic control.
Patents can be lethal.
The fact that an internationally unequal distribution of the Covid 19 vaccine was pushed through under the German EU Council Presidency is a scandal.
We want publicly funded research to be transferred to poorer countries and generic producers on social terms through equitable licensing (the socially responsible exploitation of patents).
Product development partnerships must be sustained and supported across the full breadth of the disease spectrum.
We want to expand WHO's competencies in this area.
All drugs must receive their approvals only through scientific studies.
Special paths without a scientific basis must be abolished.
We want to abolish discount agreements and other selective contracts.
In the future, research programs should be developed in a transparent and participatory process that involves the general public in addition to expert knowledge.
This is the only way to improve care and strengthen patient-oriented and interdisciplinary research.
Sovereignty for good health care instead of dependence on Big Pharma!
Corona has shown: Given the market failure in the global supply of much-needed Covid 19 vaccines and the threat of future pandemics, we can no longer leave the production of vaccines to corporations.
Therefore, we propose the establishment of public vaccine manufacturing (in the sense of Regional Vaccine Manufacturing Hubs),
globally coordinated by WHO and UN.
The cost of building production capacity for a rapid and sufficient supply of vaccines, amounts to a fraction of the cost of rearmament projects such as the Eurofighter.
We want to target funds to strengthen health sciences (public health) and non-commercial clinical research.
DIE LINKE demands that research on the therapy of long-term symptoms of a covid-19 infection ("long covid") be supported financially and according to need.
No profits with rent and land: Home for all!
Stop rent madness and displacement.
Reduce high rents and develop the non-profit housing sector.
End speculation with land.
Having an apartment where you can live well should be a given.
But land prices and rents have exploded in many cities, and are now rising sharply even in smaller towns.
This applies to apartments as well as small business premises.
Corona has exacerbated this situation.
The lockdown has shown that many apartments are too cramped and rents are often too high, even more so with unemployment and short-time work.
Moving into a suitable apartment is out of the question for many people:
Rents have doubled in many places within a decade.
Over 11 million people are overburdened by housing costs.
They have to spend more and more money on rent, which is then lacking elsewhere, in education, children, leisure time or necessary purchases.
50,000 people are already homeless and living on the streets in this country, and at least 650,000 people are homeless.
Even places of everyday cohesion such as daycare centers, cultural spaces and pubs are being displaced in many places as owners and investors try to squeeze more money out of their properties.
Public space is being commercialized and privatized.
High earners and large chains are turning more and more people into extras in an environment that is geared towards consumption, tourism and as much turnover as possible.
The reason for housing crisis, displacement and rent explosion is not simply that there is too "little housing" and the solution is not "build, build, build" - the population has not grown by leaps and bounds.
Nearly 2 million homes are vacant as financial capital searches for lucrative investment opportunities due to the unequal distribution of wealth and bubbles in the financial markets.
That's where the "concrete gold" comes in handy.
Construction is mainly in the luxury segment.
Where there is no profit to be made, however, there is no investment at all - in many places in the countryside, residential and commercial space is falling into disrepair.
Also for ecological reasons, smart mechanisms of redistributing existing housing and converting old stock into social housing would be preferable to new construction.
But the last federal governments have done nothing to counter this development.
What's more, they have systematically scaled down social housing, privatized public housing, and opened up cities and communities to speculation.
The rights of tenants are still far too weak.
The German government's "rent brake" is not working.
Construction Minister Horst Seehofer is spending three times as much money from tax revenues on "Baukindergeld" to help high-income earners buy property as he is on social housing.
Berlin, on the other hand, where DIE LINKE is in government, shows how it can be done: Cap rents with hard caps, bring apartments back into public ownership, promote social housing construction and make the real estate industry non-profit!
Rents in Berlin fell for the first time in years.
But the lobby of the real estate industry is trying to undermine effective tenant protection in the states and municipalities.
This shows that a change of policy is needed in the federal government so that people with lower incomes are no longer marginalized,
so that cities and communities do not become more deserted and are not misused as profit centers for the real estate industry.
Our cities and towns are meant to be homes and places for people to live, not extortion tools in the hands of realtors and real estate lobbies.
DIE LINKE is fighting in broad alliances for a reorientation of rent and urban development policy.
We stand by the tenants
and the many initiatives that campaign against displacement and for a right to housing.
We stand for livable cities and villages for all.
Our goal is clear: to stop the rent explosion and displacement, to
reduce rents again
and to build up a non-profit housing industry in the long term
- for a good home for everyone.
Cap rents nationwide!
We want to make rent caps possible throughout Germany.
Our aim is not only to slow down the explosion in rents, but to put an end to it and reverse it.
Particularly high rents must be lowered.
The government's rent brake is not working.
We support the "Rent Freeze" campaign and call for a rent freeze for existing leases throughout Germany wherever there is a tight housing market.
Rents must be frozen there.
Municipalities are to be authorized to determine that a housing market is tight.
We also want to simplify the conditions for small businesses:
The federal government must ensure that the states and municipalities can introduce legally secure rent caps for small businesses, crafts, cultural institutions, and social and non-profit organizations.
Create social and non-profit housing!
There is currently a shortage of more than five million homes for low-income people, many of whom live in single-person households.
Over the past 15 years, the number of public housing units has almost halved.
This is because subsidized social housing may in some cases be rented out again at a high price after just 15 years.
We want to counter this with 15 billion euros a year - by saving social housing construction, boosting municipal and cooperative housing construction, converting the existing housing stock to make it more energy-efficient and demographically stable, using subsidies and occupancy rights to make social housing more available, and building up a non-profit housing sector.
By reforming the Building Code, we will enable the public sector to actually enforce the construction of social housing against investors.
Convert former barracks into social housing: Since these buildings are in public hands, we do not want to leave them to the private sector, but to convert them into affordable housing and commercial space.
With the introduction of a new non-profit housing organization, we are tying subsidies and tax benefits permanently to rent caps,
an obligation to reinvest profits,
and democratic co-determination rights for tenants.
This will allow the creation of up to 250,000 social housing units and additional municipal and cooperative housing units per year.
For them, the rule is: once promoted, always bound.
In this way, we want to promote and democratize cooperatives more strongly.
We want to promote new forms of housing such as tenement syndicates and tenants' communities.
The federal government should support new rental housing syndicates with grants and interest-free loans.
Subsidies should be targeted to build housing that is affordable to low-income people.
Affordable and safe housing must be created for single women living in (old-age) poverty, for single parents and for women exposed to domestic violence.
We want a minimum percentage of social housing everywhere to ensure a mix of neighborhoods and to stop the trend toward the formation of parallel societies of the rich in inner cities and villa districts.
50 percent of the housing stock in public and non-profit ownership.
The Vienna model shows: Affordable housing in good condition and with high housing quality for the majority of people is possible.
In the long term, we want to take the housing stock completely off the market.
The protection against termination of commercial leases must be fundamentally changed.
There is a need for public commercial space providers to secure non-profit tenants*.
We want to abolish the general fixed-term nature of commercial leases.
We want to legally limit the termination by the landlord side.
We want to create affordable housing primarily in existing buildings.
Building codes need to be realigned for this purpose so that building in existing stock is made easier.
When making decisions on the permissibility of demolition and new construction measures, social objectives must be
and energy sustainability goals are becoming more important.
Housing is not a commodity.
Strengthen tenants' rights!
We want a broad ban on the conversion of rental apartments into condominiums.
The desire for homeownership must not come at the expense of those already living in the apartments.
Rental housing in communities with tight housing markets may not be offered as vacation rentals.
We want to create a Fairbnb alternative to providers such as Airbnb for non-commercial, private-to-private home exchanges that misappropriate living space, aim solely at profits and are listed on stock exchanges.
We want to cap the rents of micro-apartments and furnished apartments, which are used to circumvent the Mietpreisbremse and squeeze even more profit out of real estate.
The right to terminate for personal need may only apply to the immediate family.
Pretended own use is punished.
People who have lived in their apartment for a long time or are over 70 years old or suffer from a serious illness, as well as single parents, should no longer be allowed to terminate their lease because of their own needs.
We want to improve protection against termination: Once rent arrears have been paid, notice of termination may not be given.
Milieu protection must be expanded.
Effective controls, a public complaints office and significantly more staff are needed to effectively enforce the rights of tenants against rent-seeking, de-renting and other forms of abuse.
Landlords who violate the rent cap must be punished.
We want to make it easier to prosecute usurious rents.
Tenants should also be given a right of first refusal on their houses as a community and in commercial law.
Democratic tenant councils are needed in all public companies.
Nationwide, we want a new tenant co-determination law.
Collective tenants' rights and the right to strike are needed.
Climate justice instead of displacement!
Climate protection in buildings is crucial: this is where a large proportion of greenhouse gases are produced.
But up to now, energy-efficient refurbishment has all too often been used to increase rents and then also leads to displacement.
This damages the acceptance of climate protection.
Climate protection without rent increase!
We want to abolish the modernization levy, which serves to increase rents - not to protect the climate.
Surcharges on the rent are to be permitted only to the extent of the savings achieved in heating and hot water.
Poor people also have a right to energy-efficient housing.
In the short term, we want to introduce a climate component in the costs of housing and heating and increase housing benefit appropriately.
We want a nationwide climate check of all buildings by 2025.
With binding building-specific step-by-step plans that include energy efficiency levels to be achieved flexibly by a certain date, we want to guarantee a climate-neutral building stock by 2035
and create many new jobs.
This requires a comprehensive build-up of production capacities and qualifications.
This must include targeted support for training in the skilled trades, the creation and expansion of specialized courses of study, state-created production capacities and price controls to prevent deadweight and blockade effects.
The CO2 tax may not be passed on to the rent.
The renovation rate must be at least tripled
in a socially acceptable way, i.e. virtually neutral in terms of warm rents and protected by tenancy law.
Landlords who are unable to bear the costs of an energy-efficient refurbishment can come under the umbrella of the housing non-profit.
This gives them access to the full public subsidy for the cost of renovation and, in return, commits them to the non-profit management of their apartments.
We want to gear the funding backdrop to an immediate program of climate-friendly and socially responsible renovation of post-war housing developments (built between 1949 and 1978).
In addition to increasing the current programs of the Kreditanstalt für Wiederaufbau (KfW) to at least10 billion euros per year on a permanent basis, another5 billion euros per year are to be made available for this purpose.
Redevelopment consultants are to act in an advisory capacity (protecting tenants) within a social plan procedure in accordance with Section 180 of the German Building Code (BauGB) at climate support points and coordinate socially compatible neighborhood redevelopment concepts.
We want to set up further training and certification programs for craftsmen and construction companies in order to achieve good-quality, low-cost energy refurbishments.
We want to raise the standards for new buildings to the KfW 40 efficiency standard by law.
Subsidies that are currently still flowing into new construction efficiency subsidies must be completely redirected into socially responsible energy-efficient refurbishment.
In addition to increasing building efficiency, the residual energy demand must be covered gradually - but at a much faster pace - by renewable energy.
The central role for us is played by the heat pump.
The installation of fossil heating systems must be stopped as quickly as possible.
We want to make the use of geothermal energy possible even in densely populated areas: through geothermal plants operated by the state and local authorities, each supplying several residential blocks.
We will remove obstacles for ecological building materials in the building law.
At the same time, there is a need for a life cycle assessment for new construction projects in order to build more in existing buildings and save resources.
Stop demolishing affordable housing with structures worth preserving in favor of expensive new construction!
We will make ecological building materials (e.g. timber construction) mandatory in building law where it makes sense and is possible.
When awarding subsidies for energy refurbishment, consideration must be given not only to reducing energy loss per square meter, but also to reducing energy consumption in the production and processing of building materials throughout their entire life cycle.
The promotion of energy-efficient refurbishment must be expanded to include the use of sustainable building materials.
Building materials used must be clearly and traceably documented to facilitate remediation.
Building land in community hands!
One of the central causes of rising rents is the explosion in land prices.
Since1964 , land prices have risen by an average of more than1,800 percent.
In the past few years alone, prices in major cities have almost tripled.
In contrast, urgent measures are needed to stop the increasingly rapid speculation merry-go-round with land and to finally make affordable housing construction possible again.
Land prices for social housing must be capped for a specific purpose in the cities and for family housing in the countryside.
Only with affordable land are affordable rents possible.
We want to rule out the privatization of public land with a Land Security Act.
We only want to grant ground leases for public land.
In order to increase the share of public ownership of land, we are calling for a purchase program worth two billion euros a year, from which the federal government, states and municipalities will receive funds for the acquisition of land.
Real estate policy must be decoupled from fiscal policy so that the public sector can also stockpile land.
We want to commit the Bundesanstalt für Immobilienaufgaben (BImA) and the Bundeseisenbahnvermögen (BEV), which have hitherto been committed to the financial exploitation of public real estate, to social, ecological and charitable purposes.
We want to strengthen the municipalities' right of first refusal: It should be possible to exercise it everywhere without exception and within up to six months.
We need a price-limited right of first refusal that is not based on the speculative "market price" but on affordable rents (social income value) for the residents.
Stop speculation - skim off profits!
At the latest since the financial crisis, cities and municipalities have been massively targeted by speculators.
The price for the ever faster carousel of real estate purchases and sales is ultimately paid by tenants and the public sector.
We want to break the speculative cycle, in which the few enrich themselves at the expense of the many, with an anti-speculation law: Housing must no longer be an object of speculation on the stock exchange, and we want to withdraw the authorization of real estate and hedge funds.
We want to stop speculation with building land.
That is why we want to skim off non-performing gains from the increase in the value of land via a land value appreciation tax.
We want to put a stop to tax dodges in the mass purchase and sale of apartments, such as so-called share deals.
We will tax and skim off profits from speculation, company shareholdings and real estate sales more heavily.
In the future, we will prevent balance sheet tricks by, among other things, aligning the balance sheets.
Private real estate sales may not be tax-free even after ten years, except for an individual allowance.
We also call for a real estate register that can be viewed by the public.
The lack of transparency in the ownership structure must finally come to an end.
The misuse of residential and commercial space must be prohibited; we want to confiscate vacant residential and commercial space and put it to interim use.
We want to legalize the civil society reappropriation of misappropriated spaces ("squats").
We strive to ensure that, in principle, the occupation of housing that has been vacant for at least one year leads to a permanent right to live there, unless the owners undertake to make the housing available at socially acceptable rents.
Real estate groups are among the winners of the crisis.
They must therefore be given a higher-than-average share of the costs.
That is why we are calling for a one-time special levy on real estate income, which should primarily hit large corporations with more than 3,000 apartments.
Put real estate corporations on the chain!
We want to put a stop to large housing corporations like Vonovia and Deutsche Wohnen, which systematically practice rent profiteering.
DIE LINKE is therefore part of the campaign "Expropriate Deutsche Wohnen& Co".
With a socialization law, we want to improve the possibility of transferring apartments, land and property of large housing companies into public ownership.
To this end, we want to set up a remunicipalization fund.
With new housing legislation, we want to put an end to the business model of real estate funds that collect rents, distribute returns, hardly invest, and only bet on the increase of real estate prices.
A substantial portion of the rent is then available as a building renewal reserve not for financial market speculation, but for necessary maintenance.
Housing is a basic right - housing first!
No one should be without shelter.
As a short-term emergency aid until affordable rents are enforced, we want to increase and restructure housing subsidies.
The Corona crisis is not over: the moratorium on layoffs and evictions must be extended.
Rent arrears must be waived.
We will significantly raise the appropriateness thresholds for housing costs.
We want to ban evictions into homelessness as a matter of principle, and
we want to include the right to housing in the Basic Law.
We will put an end to the undignified accommodation of refugees, homeless people or seasonal and migrant workers in mass housing.
Every person has the right to their own apartment!
We want to embed the Housing First approach in addressing homelessness.
It means housing the homeless quickly and as a first step.
This also requires the further institutionalization of low-threshold counseling services and structures.
Making cities fit for the future - bringing life to the villages!
While rents are exploding in many places, apartments and houses are standing empty in some rural regions.
There is too little investment, and rental housing in structurally weak regions is less and less in line with demand.
It's not just since corona that stores have been dying in the countryside and in cities
and cultural desolation.
For socio-ecological restructuring and the revitalization of inner cities and village centers, we need a new orientation of regional policy and urban development funding from the federal government.
Investments are to focus on tasks for the future, such as building refurbishment, improvement of the living environment, age-appropriate and barrier-free conversion of buildings, and promotion of sustainable mobility.
We want to develop an infrastructure that is suitable for women and families in central and local locations with good accessibility.
Future-proof cities also means more beautiful cities without advertising.
We will advocate for a ban on commercial outdoor advertising in city centers.
We want to eliminate the municipal contribution to upgrading measures.
In order to ensure local supply in residential areas, we want to transfer vacant businesses into municipal or cooperative ownership and develop them into social centers.
The federal government is to provide financial backing for this through a remunicipalization fund.
Counties, cities and municipalities must be supported in building digital infrastructures.
Smart City must not remain a business model for large corporations.
New technologies belong in the hands of citizens to improve their participation in the development of their living environment.
We oppose the displacement of allotment gardens with an allotment garden protection program.
We want to build in a space-saving and ecological way.
We want to promote urban green spaces such as parks, allotments and community gardens (urban gardening) through investment.
We want to plan differently, away from land grabbing and urban sprawl and toward village and city planning that focuses on quality of life for all.
We reject a policy that promotes large shopping centers and malls in the interest of investors (see chapter "Mobility for all with less traffic").
We want to abolish the land-grabbing paragraph13b BauGB.
We want to finally cancel the unjustified old debts from GDR housing construction.
Companies in structurally weak regions in particular find themselves in economic difficulties and are unable to invest.
In this context, rental housing and an acceptable living environment must be secured in line with demand and the climate, especially in basic centers and settlement focal points in rural areas.
We want to strengthen the preservation of rental opportunities in rural areas through nationwide support programs.
This stops people moving away and relieves conurbations and cities with housing shortages.
City or village development is more than housing, it needs public spaces and places to meet as well as social and cultural facilities.
Residents must have a say in this.
This enables exchange, from which joint action and solidarity can grow.
An investment program for urban redevelopment is needed to overcome the one-sided focus on automobility and to improve the quality of life, for example through play streets.
Good education: fair, tuition-free, for life
We oppose social division in education, pressure to perform and underfunding with a different idea.
Access to education should reduce social disadvantages, not exacerbate them.
We want learning together in a spirit of solidarity instead of competition and grade pressure.
DIE LINKE is committed to an inclusive education system in which people receive individual support.
We want education and science that does justice to individuals and helps answer societal questions.
How do we stop the climate crisis?
How can we live and produce in such a way that everyone has enough to live on and the environment is protected?
With new challenges come new demands on education.
We want to open up universities,
strengthen continuing education and the legal right to vocational training,
and set up programs so that everyone has career prospects for the future.
We have known this for decades: Access to education in Germany is strongly dependent on social background.
The Corona crisis exacerbated problems that existed before.
While some children have their own room and a laptop for studying, others have to share both with siblings or solve tasks on their cell phones and hope that the data volume is sufficient for downloading.
The German education system reinforces the social division of society instead of counteracting it.
Those with wealthy parents have a better chance of graduating from high school and going to university.
74 percent of the children of academics go on to study, but only 21 percent of children without academic parents.
The proportion of Bachelor's graduates is15 percent, and only 8 percent of Master's graduates.
For many children, the decision as to which type of secondary school they will attend is already made after elementary school, and thus also which doors will remain closed to them in the future.
And far too little money is invested in education.
Unrenovated schools with poor facilities are a visible sign of this.
This particularly affects poorer neighborhoods, where families can hardly compensate for this through private spending on equipment or tutoring.
The debt brake has exacerbated these problems.
The need for refurbishment of schools alone is now estimated at almost 50 billion euros nationwide.
Around 35 billion euros would have to be invested in universities between 2017 and 2025 to reduce the modernization backlog.
Lecture halls and seminar rooms are often overcrowded and there are not enough staff.
And like other services, school cleaning has been outsourced in many places.
As a result, cleaning is outsourced to the cheapest suppliers, cleaners work under pressure and do not manage to finish in the allotted time.
Toilets and classrooms are dirty, students and teachers suffer.
We are fighting for more staff in education and training.
DIE LINKE demands a federal offensive for more teachers, educators and school social workers.
We need 100,000 additional teachers and 200,000 additional educators and school social work at every school!
We want to renovate and expand the buildings and
adapt them to the needs for inclusive education.
The education system is part of the public service and must be adequately funded by the state.
Privatizations - including of public educational institutions - must be stopped and reversed.
Education is more than preparation for the labor market.
The trend toward ever greater economization of education must be stopped
We want the federal, state and local governments to be able to work together on education.
The ban on cooperation means that this is only possible to a limited extent.
We want to lift the ban completely
and anchor education as a joint task in the Basic Law so that educational justice can be established for all children and young people.
We want a federal education framework law for all areas of education so that the same legal entitlements, social and personnel conditions can be ensured in all states and degrees are recognized everywhere, regardless of where they were earned.
DIE LINKE stands for good education that does not depend on one's wallet and origin.
We want real freedom of teaching and learning materials, free meals in daycare centers and schools, and free transportation for students.
Good Kitas
All children must be able to live and learn together with other children in day-care centers all day from the very beginning.
Regardless of whether and for how long the parents work.
Children need a legal right to a full-day place in a daycare center.
Especially during the corona-related daycare closures, it became clear how valuable early childhood education is for everyone.
The legal entitlement to a daycare place is still not being implemented everywhere.
This can lead to disadvantages that continue throughout the educational biography.
There is currently a shortage of 342,000 places for under-threes and soon up to 740,000 places for all children until they start school.
The groups are often too large.
Educators continue to be paid far too little.
With a narrow-track training of often only a few weeks, educational assistants are trained to retouch the massive shortage of skilled workers.
The federal government must make more money available to ensure the quality of the facilities and for the further expansion of daycare places.
We need a daycare quality law that focuses on the needs of children and employees when expanding daycare facilities:
DIE LINKE demands a nationwide standardized childcare ratio in daycare centers of at least one educator present for a maximum of three children up to the age of three and at least one educator for a maximum of eight children from the age of three.
We want good, tuition-free daycare centers (freedom from parental contributions).
All parents must be offered a place in a daycare center by the municipality.
All children should receive free healthy, hot meals every day, as is already practiced in some cities (see chapter on "Agriculture and nutrition").
We urgently need more educators for good education, upbringing and care.
There is currently a shortage of 191,000 educators.
Social and educational professions must be upgraded.
They deserve greater appreciation, better pay and working conditions.
This also includes the crediting of preparation and follow-up times as well as further training and a substitute in case of illness.
The care key must be adapted to the staffing level and time contingent.
We want to raise the training as an educator in early childhood education to university level.
People without a university entrance qualification should also have access to the education profession.
For the current training to become an educator, we want remuneration and the abolition of school fees to make the profession more attractive.
Employees in child day care are to be taken out of precarious employment situations and employed on a social security basis.
All-day care in elementary school:
In the coalition agreement, the grand coalition agreed on a legal right to all-day care for children of elementary school age from 2025.
The legal entitlement can only be met with rapid and substantial investment in the expansion of facilities and the training and recruitment of more staff.
A school for all: inclusive
The main cause of social division in education is the early division of students into different types of schools.
The Corona period has shown how different the students' prerequisites are: Some have their own room and a laptop, others have to share both.
Not all get valuable support at home.
Students* with disabilities struggle with additional barriers.
We want a school for all: a community school that leaves no child behind and counteracts social inequality.
The community school supports the children individually and comprehensively.
It is organized as an all-day school and offers all school-leaving qualifications.
Schools should be organized in such a way that social differences are not exacerbated, but rather evened out as much as possible.
We want a school that does without homework and makes private tutoring unnecessary.
Space and time must be created for this in everyday school life.
Teachers, school social workers, educators, school psychologists and medical professionals should work together in multiprofessional teams.
The community school is democratically organized with real co-determination of students.
Every student must have the opportunity to attend an all-day school, ideally a community school.
The legal entitlement to inclusive education and the right to learn together in a mainstream school belongs in every school law.
All schools must have barrier-free access for all children, which must not be limited to structural requirements.
They must have adequate equipment and qualifications in staff, assistance services, teaching and learning materials, and other aids for each child.
We want to implement a two-teacher system as one of the frameworks to make special schools obsolete.
Inclusion must not be made dependent on how much it costs!
The federal, state and local governments must launch an "inclusive education" investment program to comprehensively convert and equip educational facilities to make them barrier-free.
DIE LINKE wants an inclusive school where all children and young people are welcome and learn together with and from each other.
Inclusion is a task that does not apply to individual groups - neither to students with disabilities, nor to those of non-German origin, nor to those who are excluded from participation for other reasons.
Today, special needs are often identified.
However, too little and insufficient assistance is provided for these support needs.
That has to change.
Instead of imposing the label of special needs on more and more children, we want to gradually dismantle the multidimensional school system and provide comprehensive support for all children without pejorative labeling.
Thousands of refugee and immigrant children and young people are attending school or training in Germany.
We call for a program that is co-financed by the federal government and includes training and continuing education for additional teachers who teach German as a second language, an initial supply of school supplies for all children, additional language and literacy courses for refugee adults as well, and information on vocational training offered to refugees at the Federal Employment Agency.
The municipalities must be provided with the necessary funds for this.
In Germany, multilingual socialization is only valued for languages that are considered economically important.
We see multilingualism among children and young people with a migration background as an enrichment and an opportunity that schools should recognize and use for joint learning.
Including the mother tongue in the learning of other languages is important in order to acquire a secure footing in these languages.
The language of origin should be recognized as a first or second language in examinations.
We consider regional or minority languages as an expression of cultural richness and promote their offer in schools.
School social work must become an integral part of school work - at every school and on a permanent basis.
To this end, it must be anchored in youth welfare law as a regular task.
A school social work program guarantees the deployment of at least one school social work specialist per150 students.
These should be well networked with career and academic counseling centers to facilitate the path to higher education for students who do not come from academic families.
The lack of staff at schools leads to missed lessons and stress.
The staff must be able to compensate for shortages with regularly employed teachers.
This requires10 percent substitution reserve.
To end the staffing shortage in schools, significantly more teachers need to be trained and hired everywhere.
New, hybrid forms of learning, such as those practiced during the Coronalockdown, must not lead to a new social divide because not all learners have equally good learning conditions at home.
We want every child to have a laptop as part of their educational equipment and to be introduced to digital technologies at an early age.
Each child must continue to have access to a printer, including all supplies, as well as access to the Internet at home with a free educational plan.
The rulings of the social courts must finally be implemented.
This also applies to families who are just above the Hartz IV income.
The DigitalPakt Schule (Digital Pact for Schools), including all additional agreements on devices and administration, must be made permanent.
Hybrid forms of learning are no less labor-intensive than forms of face-to-face learning.
They are not suitable as a savings model.
We need more teachers for good teaching, also and especially in view of new forms of learning.
The IT infrastructure in schools must be managed by specialist staff.
Corresponding positions are to be created in the short and medium term.
The IT infrastructure of all schools and universities must be expanded with fast and powerful broadband connections, WLAN for all, learning and work spaces, and up-to-date hardware and software equipment.
Open Software and Open Educational Resources (OER) are to be promoted.
Media competence must be comprehensively strengthened: in preschool education, in schools and lessons, in the world of work, in civil society projects, and into old age.
Many students no longer learn to swim because many swimming pools are dilapidated and have to be closed.
This is where we want to redevelop.
School swimming and physical education must be secured again.
We want to invest in barrier-free,
energy-efficient and beautifully designed classrooms and sports facilities.
At least 50 billion euros are needed to renovate the schools.
Especially in so-called hotspot schools, the money is lacking.
We want to replace the Königstein Key as a distribution instrument for federal funding for education with a social index.
The social index is intended to distribute funds among the states and, within the states, among municipalities according to need, so that enough money gets to where it is really needed.
We want to prevent lobbying in schools and lessons.
For years, business players have been entering schools out of pure self-interest and increasingly helping to determine learning content.
Diversity in education suffers as a result.
Commercial advertising in schools must be prohibited by law.
In return, schools must be better equipped with teaching materials so that they do not have to resort to tendentious offerings from corporations and interest groups.
Education without the Bundeswehr!
The Bundeswehr should no longer be allowed to advertise or perform in schools or universities.
Instead, we need more political and peace education by teachers.
All teaching qualifications should be treated equally.
There is no reason to value teachers at elementary schools lower than teachers at high schools, for example.
Learners, teachers and parents should have a say about school.
We want to strengthen democracy, self-administration of schools and especially the co-determination rights of students in schools.
We want to bring school cleaning back into public hands across the board - for clean schools and good working conditions.
The pandemic demonstrated the importance of good hygiene standards in schools.
We are fundamentally opposed to public-private partnerships (PPPs).
They represent a particularly fatal sell-off of public property.
The same must apply to schools: public tasks in public hands.
Well trained
Every year, tens of thousands of young people in Germany are put off in their search for an apprenticeship.
They cannot find an apprenticeship with prospects or are stuck in endless waiting loops.
Almost two million young people have no vocational training.
Especially secondary school students and migrants are disadvantaged.
The economy is falling short of the target of 500,000 apprenticeships to be created annually.
Many employers complain about a lack of skilled workers and training companies are unable to find trainees.
But: The shortage of skilled workers is homemade, because many potential apprentices are not considered ready for training and are "parked" in waiting loops.
On the other hand, more than half of the trainees complain about too much stress, many also go to work sick or are exploited as cheap labor.
Due to the pandemic and the financial difficulties of some companies, many training companies have discontinued or significantly reduced their training programs.
This exacerbates the situation on the training market.
We want everyone who has started an apprenticeship to be able to finish it.
The federal government must provide funds and opportunities for this.
The conditions and quality of training must be improved and apprenticeships upgraded.
Here, too, we need more staff.
According to the German Education and Science Union (GEW), 160,000 teachers will need to be hired at vocational schools by 2030 to meet demand.
Now more than ever: DIE LINKE supports the right to a free and fully qualifying education for all.
Anonymized application procedures are intended to ensure that everyone has the same opportunities for training.
Trainees need a training allowance that is sufficient to live independently of their parents.
We demand a minimum training allowance that is 80 percent of the average collectively agreed training allowance for all sectors in the respective training year.
We support the trade unions and trade union youth organizations in their struggle for better collective bargaining solutions.
Training in professions that are not regulated on a dual basis, for example in all social, health and educational professions, must be better financed.
In principle, school fees are to be abolished and a training allowance based on the pay scale is to be paid.
We want to promote the construction of public trainee dormitories, especially in rural areas.
DIE LINKE demands unlimited employment after the end of training and the abolition of the probationary period for employment in the same company.
We want solidarity-based pay-as-you-go financing that makes all companies responsible for creating sufficient dual and high-quality training places.
At the end of vocational preparation measures, there must be a binding offer of training.
We want to abolish the "waiting loop" in the transition system.
People who have not completed training should be able to obtain a recognized vocational qualification - regardless of their age.
We want to abolish the "training maturity" criterion used by the Federal Employment Agency.
It blocks access to vocational training.
We want a fundamental reform of the Vocational Training Act (BBiG) that focuses on improving the quality of training and establishes a legal entitlement to fully qualifying training.
We want to strengthen the co-determination of trainees.
Their participation in the staff committees must be guaranteed.
We want a vocational training pact to ensure that long overdue investments are made for good quality at vocational schools.
And it needs significantly more staff.
Political education must also be part of vocational training.
Social work and socio-psychological accompaniment should also be strengthened in training.
Freedom of teaching and learning materials must be anchored in the Vocational Training Act - including textbooks for vocational school instruction.
Moreover, because the training market is still divided into so-called women's and men's occupations, the hurdles for young people to make an atypical career choice are great.
We want to counteract this: through gender-sensitive education and by upgrading areas in which wages are low and many women work.
Good further training
We are committed to lifelong, lifewide learning: as an offer, not an obligation, of self-optimization.
General, cultural, political and professional training is an important part of this.
It serves the development of the individual and professional training or reorientation and promotes social participation.
The right to continuing education must be secured by law.
Socio-ecological restructuring can mean that many people are given a future-proof perspective.
Continuing education plays a crucial role here.
New opportunities must be created here in continuing vocational training and at universities.
Adult education centers, which are often run by local authorities or are at least non-profit organizations, can offer a wide range of general continuing education courses independently of the profit interests of private education providers,
political education
and for catching up on school-leaving qualifications.
To this end, the adult education centers are to be strengthened financially so that they can expand their range of services and offer them free of charge.
It is important that offers of language support can be provided to immigrants.
A crucial prerequisite is good working conditions and good remuneration in all providers and areas of adult education.
In adult education, working conditions are often precarious.
We want to change that.
Teachers in continuing education need a generally binding collective agreement, based on the public service, for all areas of continuing education.
Honorary contracts are to be converted into permanent positions.
Honorary contracts, insofar as they are still necessary or desired by the employees, must be adapted to the TVÖD.
This also applies to teachers in language and integration courses.
Employment agencies and other public clients must consider the quality of education when awarding contracts.
and focus on good pay for teachers.
When the Federal Employment Agency awards training services, the applicable collective agreement provisions should be binding for all providers.
Adult education centers and other publicly funded continuing education institutions must be adequately and permanently funded.
Teachers should not have to shuffle from one temporary project to the next.
Rather, permanent positions must also be created for permanent tasks.
DIE LINKE wants to legally secure educational leave for all employees and all areas of continuing education nationwide, not just for continuing vocational education.
People who have not completed vocational training should be able to obtain a recognized vocational qualification.
To this end, retraining courses are to be extended in line with demand and access to external examinations is to be made easier.
We call for a continuing education allowance: Those who need or want to reorient themselves or gain further qualifications within the framework of socio-ecological transformation will be given sufficient time and funding to do so (cf. chapter "Social and ecological system change").
Good studies, good working conditions, good research
Studying is characterized by pressure to perform and time pressure.
This leads to stress among students and employees.
In addition, many students have lost their part-time jobs in the Corona crisis and do not know how to pay the rent.
This hits especially hard those who do not come from wealthy families.
Many are excluded from studying from the outset by barriers to entry.
Further, the pandemic-related closure of universities has further fueled the competition and isolation that has persisted for years in higher education.
This is politically intentional.
But it doesn't have to stay that way.
DIE LINKE is committed to a social, democratic, open and inclusive higher education and
science landscape.
We are on the side of initiatives and movements that are fighting for better conditions: for a permanent contract and fair pay for academic staff,
Good study and living conditions for students
and to ensure that the coronavirus crisis is also tackled with solidarity at universities.
Much remains to be done.
For years, colleges and universities have been expanding to become entrepreneurial universities under pressure from public funding systems.
The goal is to make knowledge, education and research economically exploitable.
Chronic underfunding means that the space for independent and socially critical research and teaching, and thus an essential function of science, falls by the wayside.
