Research without third-party funding is hardly possible anymore.
DIE LINKE demands sufficient funding for universities
and research institutions by the state.
We want to open up the universities further.
It should be possible to study with a passed specialized baccalaureate, the general university entrance qualification, a completed vocational training or a comparable qualification.
We will abolish all forms of tuition fees for people with and without a German passport.
BAföG must be adapted to the realities of life and provide comprehensive funding for education.
Only 11 percent of students still receive BAföG at all, and only 8 percent receive the maximum rate.
We advocate for a repayment-free, parent-independent and needs-based BAföG that reaches everyone who needs it.
Educational decisions should be able to be made free of financial concerns or parental preferences.
The BAföG subsidy rate must be regularly and automatically adjusted to the actual and rising cost of living and housing.
We want to abolish the age limits for BAföG and adjust the duration of entitlement to the real average duration of studies.
Likewise, the linking of BAföG to performance reviews must be abolished.
Funding gaps must be closed.
People with tolerated stay permits, residence permits and humanitarian residence permits must have access to educational support when they start their studies or training.
Access and admission restrictions such as numerus clausus, selection interviews, IQ tests or job interviews must be abolished.
We are proposing a Higher Education Admission Act for this purpose.
Access to a Master's degree must be open to Bachelor's graduates everywhere.
To this end, Master's places must be expanded in line with demand.
The aim is to make it easier for refugees to take up studies.
To this end, additional study places must be created and educational qualifications obtained abroad must be recognized quickly and unbureaucratically.
Taking up studies must ensure a right to stay and protect against deportation.
We also want to enable scientists who have been politically persecuted to continue their scientific work at universities in Germany.
We want to simplify access for foreign students.
We want to transform the association uni-assist e. V. into a public law institution financed by the federal government.
We want well-funded and democratically effective student councils that organize the student body.
And an additional mentoring program for students from non-academic families.
We are calling for a further education program for socio-ecological restructuring that is co-financed by the federal government and a levy on companies: Anyone wishing to reorient themselves professionally should be given the opportunity to study at a university or gain an additional qualification in a social or ecological field in which more employees will be needed in the future. (see "Further training" section in the "Work" chapter)
The content of teaching and research is increasingly geared towards economic usability and corporate interests.
We want universities to take social responsibility and are committed to critical science and teaching,
in the sense of a socially just,
ecologically sustainable
and peaceful world.
Democratization of universities: We fight nationwide for constituted student bodies with a general political mandate.
University committees should meet in public where possible.
They must have equal representation so that all status groups, including students, have equal voting rights.
Instead of unilaterally strengthening the university management, we need to strengthen the university committees, which are democratically elected by all university members.
Bodies based on supervisory boards - such as university councils - should be abolished.
We want to strengthen the university's democratic exchange with civil society players, trade unions, citizens' initiatives and social associations.
Universities should be open places for social debate.
This must take precedence over the commercial use of university premises.
Good science needs good work
To this end, the scientific and non-scientific junior and middle management must be strengthened.
Permanent tasks must be processed in permanent positions.
We reject precarious work, teaching at dumping wages, and the exploitation of adjunct and non-academic employees.
We want to increase the fees for teaching assignments; they must also cover preparation and follow-up work.
Central teaching duties must be carried out in permanent, open-ended positions.
Deadline is frustration.
Approximately 90 percent of mid-level scientific employees are employed on a temporary basis.
We want to abolish the special fixed-term employment law for scientific staff: Permanent employment contracts must become the norm.
Instead of being dependent on individual professors, young scientists should belong to departments.
We want to create more permanent positions alongside professorships.
Qualifying positions of doctoral students must be compensated at 100 percent.
We need a comprehensive collective bargaining agreement for student employees as well as their representation in the staff council.
Student employees must be integrated into the TV-L in the medium term.
We support the TVStud initiatives in their request for their own collective agreements in the short term.
Empowering women: We want to enforce a 50 percent quota for women at every career level and further develop the female professors program into a program for promoting women at all career levels.
The universities are supported to a significant extent by non-scientific personnel in administration, building management and research operations.
Anyone talking about working conditions at universities must not neglect this part of the workforce.
Learning from the crisis also means recognizing that a workforce expansion plan is needed for university administration.
In university administration, too, our motto is: permanent positions for permanent tasks.
Tax funds for research promotion may only go to institutions that are bound by collective agreements.
This also creates incentives for the institutes of the Max Planck Society, Fraunhofer Society, Helmholtz Association and Leibniz Association to become members of an employers' association.
Investments in social infrastructure
The federal government must assume permanent co-responsibility for the basic funding of public universities.
We want to remove the time limit on the Future Contract and develop it into a permanent subsidy.
The excellence strategy fuels competitive thinking in science.
The elaborate application and selection process is detrimental to a socially responsible scientific culture.
Instead, we want to provide funding for studies and science across the board and in all disciplines.
We want to provide significantly better funding for universities of applied sciences.
Not enough money is made available for students at universities of applied sciences, even though there are more and more of them.
Sufficient funding is needed instead of "cheap places to study."
Universities of applied sciences are to be granted the right to award doctorates.
The joint task of university construction must be enshrined in the Basic Law again.
and a special program for the construction of new halls of residence will be launched.
Teaching is to be secured by basic funding that is based on the number of actual first-year students and the cost of the study place.
DIE LINKE demands a university social pact: money for more affordable places in dormitories, dining halls and help for student unions, which have fallen into difficulties due to the Corona crisis.
We want a financial support program for low-cost semester tickets for students.
In perspective, we demand ticket-free public transport for all.
The dual study program must be accredited under public law and lead to equivalent qualifications.
Dual students must receive a training contract with a minimum salary.
Access to the dual study program must be possible without a high school diploma.
Transparent research and social responsibility:
Cooperation agreements, sponsorships and other contracts that public education and research institutions conclude with private companies or foundations must be disclosed.
They have a direct or indirect influence on science.
The expansion of IT must go hand in hand with better training for student teachers and active teaching staff: Digital skills and teaching methods must become an integral part of the curriculum.
Even after that, there is a need for further training.
Expanding digital infrastructure: The federal and state governments are to provide additional funding for the faster expansion and development of digital infrastructures at universities through a university digital pact.
Instead of lighthouse projects, we need a digitization offensive for universities nationwide.
But technology alone does not make for good online teaching.
Teachers must be given easier access to continuing education and training for digital teaching and learning.
Digital media must not become a gateway for privatization of education by private commercial providers, companies or publishers.
Software used in educational institutions should be free software.
Research for peace instead of for war and the arms industry:
We demand the anchoring of civil clauses at all universities and all scientific institutions as
well as the promotion of peace research.
To counter the neoliberal mainstream in economics with critical thinking, we want to promote pluralistic approaches in research and teaching at colleges, universities and in policy consulting.
These include (post-) Keynesian,
Marxist,
ecological,
and feminist economic theories.
We call for the establishment of a research cluster on socio-ecological transformation with a heterodox research orientation within the framework of federal research and innovation funding.
Plural approaches must also be given greater consideration in the promotion of doctoral students.
The theoretical and research approaches should also be taken into account in the tendering and awarding of scientific consulting services by the public sector.
We need government-funded research support that addresses societal challenges by paying attention to critical and pluralistic research.
Research and science must contribute to solving social division,
Climate change
and environmental problems.
With this in mind, we want to strategically align the billions in federal innovation and technology funding, including non-university research funded jointly by the federal and state governments.
In addition to technical innovations, social innovations are particularly important.
We want to link this research landscape more closely with the work of the universities.
Climate Protection Socially Just: For a Socio-Ecological System Change
The ecological crisis is the great survival issue of the 21st century.
At the same time, it is a class issue.
It is by no means only about climate change: Environmental researchers assume that some of the nine planetary boundaries (i.e. physical boundaries of the ecological Earth system) have already been exceeded.
This concerns in particular global warming, mass species extinction, land use change, and the disruption of phosphorus and nitrogen cycles.
Each of these problems has the potential to strip our society of its material foundation.
The corona pandemic shows: The destruction of natural habitats is rapidly increasing the probability of pandemics.
We must stop this devastating process of nature destruction.
Climate change is also a medical and nursing emergency: the number of heat-related treatments and heat-related deaths is growing.
Air pollution exacerbates chronic diseases, drinking water reservoirs dry up.
The prosperity of the industrialized countries is inextricably linked to the exploitation of the Global South.
Dirty industrial processes and exploitative jobs have been outsourced to developing and emerging countries, while the products and profits migrate to the Global North.
Environmental degradation cannot be separated from social conditions under capitalism.
Studies have long indicated that the ecological footprint is extremely unevenly distributed.
This applies not only to the relationship between rich and poor states, but also to Germany itself.
While the richest are responsible for an above-average share of climate-damaging greenhouse gas emissions, the poor are most affected by environmental change and pollution.
Those who own assets can take shelter from heat, drought and flood.
The poor can't.
The destruction of nature threatens material livelihoods
and itself becomes a social issue.
Planning the ecological conversion
To stop the destruction of nature, resource consumption and emissions must be reduced to sustainable levels.
Ecosystems have carrying capacity limits that must not be exceeded.
Under the conditions of the "free" world market, sustainability is not possible in the long run.
Instead of an economy that works for profits, we need an economy that follows clear social and environmental goals, that can manage the remaining resources and that works for the needs of the people.
All the experiences of the last decades prove it: Technological successes - for example through the expansion of renewable energies or through better drive systems - are immediately offset by so-called rebound effects.
Combustion engines are becoming more efficient, but vehicles are getting heavier.
Digitization allows for more environmentally friendly forms of working, but at the same time has triggered an ecologically devastating mining boom.
Of course, green technologies are part of socio-ecological system change, but they alone will not stop the destruction of nature.
We therefore need political measures that cap and reduce resource consumption and emissions.
This applies most urgently to emissions that are harmful to the climate.
Binding ceilings must be enforced for them, setting clear guidelines for companies, but also for society.
Our planet has physical limits - this realization must finally prevail in business and politics.
Social-ecological investment offensive
In order to sustainably reduce resource consumption and emissions, we need a targeted restructuring of the economy and society.
With socio-ecological investments, we want to ensure that this restructuring does not take place at the expense of employees and the population at large.
We therefore propose an immediate program to combat the social and economic crisis, which at the same time sets the course for a better, climate-friendly future for all
and makes society more crisis-proof through a strong public, social infrastructure.
It's about recognition for those who keep society running - and a better life for all.
Climate protection
and social justice are inseparable for us.
Without social justice, no major transformation toward a carbon-neutral economy can succeed, because people will not even be empowered to implement climate protection in their everyday lives and to commit to it.
Without climate justice, there is no social justice now and in the future, because the climate crisis hits those who are socially poor first.
It is time to question the profit mechanism in principle so that the many have a future.
Resource consumption beyond this is neither possible nor necessary.
It is time that those who have had a hard time in recent years finally benefit from the necessary transformation to a climate-friendly and solidarity-based society: Employees in the low-wage sector, in industry or construction, in social services and the "system-relevant" infrastructure,
tenants,
people who care for their relatives and friends.
Our program for a socially just and climate-just society therefore focuses on wages that are sufficient for a good life.
We want to use investments to create entry points to a new model of prosperity that is socially just, climate-just and gender-just, with a fair distribution of work and wealth.
Instead of blind growth of profits, we want more time and less stress for everyone through shorter working hours with wage and personnel compensation.
The infrastructure in many municipalities and regions has been cut to the bone.
There is a lack of facilities, services and staff.
This affects low-income earners in particular and leads to stress in the everyday lives of many.
We want to change that with a socio-ecological investment offensive.
We want to create attractive services and public offerings for good work - inclusive, democratic and oriented toward the common good.
In doing so, we are focusing on a renewable energy and mobility turnaround for ecological and affordable energy supply
and mobility for all.
Here's to investing in affordable, energy-efficient housing built by well-paid workers.
Towards a climate-neutral conversion of municipalities,
of care close to home,
Functioning infrastructure
and a better quality of life.
The German government is watching jobs being destroyed in Germany.
This has nothing to do with climate policy, but everything to do with returns for the shareholders of the corporations.
Billions of taxpayers' money from aid packages and subsidies go to the corporations, without conditions, without job guarantees.
A massive societal debate about direction has long been underway: returns for shareholders at the expense of the workforce and the future of our children and grandchildren - or a "social, ecological and democratic transformation" (according to IG Metall).
The productive work and knowledge of employees in industry are an indispensable basis for a socially just and climate-friendly model of prosperity in the future.
At the same time, we need a different production model that enables sustainable lifestyles and a high quality of life for all.
A production that relies on armaments and expensive condominiums, that builds cars with more and more horsepower, energy and resource consumption, has just as little a future as the production of disposable products (for example, electrical and IT equipment with a shelf life of only a few months).
Investing in well-paying, climate-neutral jobs and the infrastructure for a better life
Rules and concepts are needed for the necessary restructuring of the economy - incentives, subsidies and tax breaks are not enough.
Only with massive public investment can we achieve the transformation to a climate-neutral economy and infrastructure in a decade and a half.
LEFT economic policy focuses on secure employment,
good care for all,
and to democratic decision-making on investments that are intended to pave the way for an economy that is geared towards the common good, meets needs and is climate-neutral.
Instead of privatization and public-private "partnerships" that cater to the profit of a few, we want to shape investments so that the tax dollars used benefit everyone.
The investments must noticeably improve people's quality of life.
There is a shortage of 100,000 nurses in hospitals and affordable housing in many large and medium-sized cities.
We want to change that.
We will invest over 120 billion euros annually in public services of general interest.
and infrastructure.
Higher income from taxes and social security contributions can refinance at least half of this expenditure.
More public investment at the local, state, and federal levels, and an equitable distribution of work, can create more than one million new short full-time (30-hour-per-week) jobs.
With the socio-ecological investment and future program, we are investing in: More personnel in care and health: We want to end the care crisis, which is damaging the health of care workers and endangering human lives.
To achieve this, we want to recruit 100,000 nurses in hospitals and 100,000 in care facilities and care services.
We want to make the public health service crisis-proof and expand it (see chapter on "Health and care").
Good education for all: We will hire 200,000 additional educators to guarantee all children a good daycare place and to ensure comprehensive all-day care.
We also want to create 100,000 new positions for teachers and social workers in schools.
We want to refurbish buildings,
Equipping daycare centers, schools and universities to meet future needs
and inclusion - 58 billion euros per year (see "Education" chapter).
We are creating a new start in social and non-profit housing.
We will create at least 250,000 affordable apartments per year whose rents ordinary employees can afford.
We are investing in a funding program for socially just ecological modernization of buildings (see chapter "Housing and rents").
Renewable energy transition: To save the climate, renewable energies must replace the fossil energy system by 2035.
Renewable energy is limited by resources and available land.
Therefore, the limitation of absolute consumption is necessary.
Funding under the Renewable Energy Sources Act is geared towards making it profitable for small operators and municipalities.
The big energy companies will be stripped of their power
and energy supply will be geared to the common good.
The energy transition in public and cooperative ownership can create more than 100,000 high-quality, well-paid jobs in the production, installation, and maintenance of these systems by 2030.
Investments in the energy transition strengthen the regional economy in particular (see chapter "Climate justice and energy transition").
We are expanding bus and rail services and drastically reducing prices.
We are introducing a 365-euro annual ticket for local public transport and gradually making it completely free of charge for users.
If people are no longer dependent on motorized individual transport, cars can be replaced by ecological means of transport.
We need fewer cars and models with a smaller environmental footprint.
This restructuring must not be left to the market and private corporations.
We are shifting short-haul flights and large portions of freight traffic to rail.
We invest in cycle paths, footpaths and urban redevelopment, promote short distances and create networked mobility (see chapter "Equitable mobility").
Strong communities with climate-neutral, social infrastructure for a better life: We relieve the burden on municipalities,
support disadvantaged regions
and invest in equal living conditions in east and west, in all regions of the country.
In the case of investment funds, priority will be given to structurally weak regions and socially deprived municipalities and urban districts.
We are creating access to fast Internet everywhere
and investing in accessibility: in transport, public buildings and housing.
Regional economic development and economic cycles create jobs,
social infrastructures make life easier.
The transformation of electricity, mobility and heating will create socially just and climate-neutral communities with a better quality of life for all: affordable housing, good healthcare close to home, short distances, less noise, more parks and urban gardening, playgrounds and sports facilities, affordable and climate-friendly local recreation facilities.
Rescue parachute for industrial jobs: Our Industrial Transformation Fund benefits companies that drive socio-ecological transformation
while securing jobs on good terms.
Socially and ecologically just in Europe: We want to align the European Central Bank with the goal of promoting good and meaningful work, full employment and socio-ecological transformation in the EU.
The ECB must make loan programs available so that the public investment banks of the member states can support a climate-neutral transformation of the economy by 2035 and invest in healthcare and education, renewable energies, rail and mass transit, and social and ecological housing (see chapter "Europe").
Job and Income Guarantees: Entering a New Model of Prosperity
It is also about a new model of prosperity: With the socio-ecological investment offensive and a general reduction in working hours in the direction of the short full-time (28 to 35 hours with full wage and necessary personnel compensation), we create secure and meaningful work for all and more time prosperity.
This will allow us to create over 2 million new, well-paying jobs with a future over the course of ten years.
Jobs that will be lost in the medium term due to digitization and rationalization, structural change and ecological modernization will be more than compensated for.
Ecologically destructive work or work experienced by employees as meaningless, poorly paid Mc-jobs, are replaced by good and meaningful work.
The people who keep society running are paid better.
This goes hand in hand with the upgrading of social professions.
Our socio-ecological system change is therefore also a path to greater gender justice.
A just transformation includes ensuring that employees who change jobs and industries can continue to gain qualifications without jeopardizing their income.
For the period of further training, we want to introduce a further qualification allowance that amounts to 90 percent of the last salary.
The training allowance is financed proportionally by the employment agency and a fund into which companies pay.
The period of further training is not counted towards the entitlement to unemployment benefits.
We want to open up universities of applied sciences and universities to employees in industry
and make them more attractive by offering their own further training opportunities for future professions and key qualifications in cooperation with works councils and trade unions.
Creating industrial jobs with a future
The future of industrial sites touches many regions.
Families and neighborhoods are affected, as are municipal revenues and their social infrastructure.
The German government's industrial policy follows the interests of capital: The profits of the large export corporations come first, not the medium-term future of employees, climate protection and the benefits for society.
The dependence of Germany's industrial structure on exports and the auto industry is a dead end in terms of economic and industrial policy.
The industrial structure must become more regional, more crisis-proof and less dependent on exports
- and make industry climate-neutral in the long term.
Unlike concepts of structural change in the past, it is not about subsidies for corporations and a certain "social cushioning" of the consequences of crises, but about a better future for employees in industry: meaningful and secure work, wages that are enough for a good life, less stress and more free time.
Our goal is for industry to produce in a climate-neutral, sustainable and energy-efficient way by 2035
and the industrial structure in Germany becomes less dependent on exports of cars, weapons, security technology and environmentally harmful forms of chemical production.
Together with the trade unions, we want to initiate a process of arms conversion (see chapter on "Peace").
It must be ensured that new, equivalent jobs are created in the affected regions.
Instead of subsidies for shareholder returns, we call for a rescue package for industrial jobs that ensures secure and meaningful work in the future:
no tax money for nothing in return.
Government funds (whether direct aid payments or hidden subsidies) must be tied to long-term guarantees of jobs, collective agreements and binding investment plans in order to drive forward the necessary ecological restructuring of production,
guarantee planning security and secure incomes for employees.
Veto rights against clear-cutting, co-determination on the future.
The workforce must have a say in decisions on relocations, closures and outsourcing, mass layoffs and decisions on investments in the future!
Works councils must also be given co-determination rights in economic matters, and all important company decisions must be confirmed by employee assemblies.
The German government, together with the workforce, trade unions, science, environmental and social associations, must develop a binding plan for the future of industry that ensures climate-neutral industrial production by 2035 and is
linked to job and income guarantees for employees.
The industrial groups must be obliged to initiate this restructuring - they must be committed to the common good in accordance with the Basic Law.
In financing the ecological modernization of production, we want to hold corporations and shareholders accountable.
As a reminder, Daimler, VW and BMW alone had retained earnings of almost 180 billion euros last year.
An industrial fund worth 20 billion euros a year: A government transformation fund worth 20 billion euros a year is to support the necessary ecological transformation, particularly in the automotive supply industry.
Only companies that secure jobs, have good wages and nationwide collective agreements benefit from this fund.
An investment program for a future-proof transformation towards a climate-neutral steel and basic materials industry, including the use of green hydrogen.
State aid must only be provided with democratic control
and in return for public ownership shares in the steel companies
and greater codetermination of the workforce.
We want a supply chain law that is both socially and climate friendly.
The law must anchor the Paris Agreement as well as independent environment-related due diligence obligations for companies (see chapter "Social justice worldwide").
We advocate a European carbon offset mechanism that puts a price on the import of CO2-intensive products.
In this way, we prevent the decarbonization of industry in Germany and the European Union from being at the expense of local employees and
leading to the relocation of CO2-intensive production to third countries.
Democracy in the economy.
Promote cooperatives and solidarity-based economy
We want to promote more democracy in industry as well: Funds for research and development, for strengthening a regional industrial structure are to be controlled by regional economic and transformation councils in which, in addition to the state government and companies, trade unions, environmental and social associations also have equal voting rights.
Democratic public and cooperative forms of ownership can be at the heart of a non-capitalist economy in the future.
Cooperatives and workforce enterprises build on the knowledge, experience and skills of employees and give them more opportunities to have a say in the nature and content of production.
In order to achieve the Paris climate targets, our living conditions, including the (defense) industry, must be transformed.
We are developing co-determination in companies into genuine economic democracy.
This is also necessary because impulses from politics and industry will not be sufficient to protect the climate at the required speed.
State subsidies must be prioritized for ecological modernization,
Regional structural policy in economically underdeveloped regions
and for cooperatives.
Cooperatives must be given equal consideration in all areas of state economic development.
We promote companies that are wholly or partly collectively owned by the workforce by giving them preference in the award of public contracts.
We want to anchor a binding proportion of basic research in the area of the solidarity-based economy in the Research Promotion Act.
In addition, we want to establish a socio-ecological chamber of commerce that supports regional lighthouse projects and business start-ups in the field of solidarity-based economy by providing advice and financial support.
In the case of companies in crisis, we also want to promote workforces that want to continue the company collectively:
State subsidies to companies and aid in economic crises must be awarded in the form of collective employee shares where the workforces are in favor of this.
When companies are sold, employees must be given the right to be informed in advance and the right of first refusal.
DIE LINKE is fighting to transfer public utilities, banks and insurance companies, energy corporations, pharmaceutical and medical companies, the postal service, telecommunications infrastructure and other key industries into public (or cooperative) hands and into forms of social ownership.
We want to disempower the large electricity companies and transfer them to public ownership.
The energy industry is to be organized through municipal utilities that are decentralized and democratic in the municipalities.
The socio-ecological transformation needs holistic projects and concrete places that bring together people from different sectors to develop solutions together.
We want to create centers that enable and promote active social participation in the transformation.
These transformation centers will provide training and education for Fair and Good Work according to the requirements of environmental and climate justice.
Fair mobility: Ecological and affordable for all - with good jobs
We want affordable and climate-friendly mobility for all.
The transport sector is the only one that does not save CO2 and is the driver of the climate crisis.
At the same time, there is no money for good alternatives such as buses, trains, pedestrian and bicycle paths.
Our vision: We are expanding bus and rail services.
We are making local transport more attractive and gradually making it free of charge.
Investments are being made in the railroads and rail travel is becoming cheaper.
Fewer cars are driving in cities, and more destinations are being reached by demand-responsive public transportation, walking and biking.
Delivery traffic is organized publicly
and working conditions are improved.
By 2030, the majority of people in cities and also in rural regions will no longer be dependent on cars, so their overall number can be significantly reduced.
The coronavirus crisis in particular has shown how important it is to increase the frequency of public transport services,
affordable prices,
good working conditions
and well-developed cycle paths - but almost nothing has happened.
In many places, transit agencies have experienced financial hardship/slippage because there has been less ridership.
Instead of investing in climate-friendly mobility for all, Lufthansa was bailed out with billions - without job security.
The burden of cars and trucks mainly affects those who cannot afford to move away from the main road.
Air pollution causes millions of premature deaths every year, 80,000 in Germany alone.
We want to change these conditions.
And we are not alone: citizens' initiatives against destructive transport projects, for better rail services or safe bike and pedestrian paths are active all over the country.
There is support from environmental groups.
The climate targets make a socio-ecological change in transport imperative.
Mobility for all - with less traffic
We want affordable and truly barrier-free mobility for all - with little investment of time and energy.
The focus for us is therefore on public mobility services.
Those who walk or bike need better conditions.
No one should be dependent on the (own) car.
Our goal is a jointly financed zero fare for public transport for all.
The first steps are significantly lower fares (for example, a 365-euro annual ticket), nationwide social tickets for low-income households, a social rail card, and free tickets for schoolchildren, trainees, students, and people in further education.
Fare evasion should be decriminalized and not punished more severely than parking tickets.
Local public transport must be
and barrier-free.
By 2030, we want to double the number of users (compared to before Corona).
We need much more funding from the federal government for this.
In addition to rails and vehicles
more jobs, good pay and good working conditions for employees.
Almost 200,000 employees will have to be recruited within the next ten years in the driving service, in maintenance and in other areas of the transport companies so that the expansion of the service and an ecological mobility turnaround can succeed.
We are in favor of municipal, democratically controlled local transport companies.
The priority of owner-operated companies must be abolished.
Instead of profits for Uber and Co, we want new mobility services exclusively under public (e.g. municipal) sovereignty as part of local transport in close coordination or cooperation with cab companies.
All offers should be bookable in a public platform (see chapter "Digitization").
We want a mobility guarantee for rural areas: connections between communities and to the nearest urban center at least every hour from 6 am to 10 pm.
Services such as citizens' buses or shared-call cabs as well as modern area-call bus systems and also cabs can be included or supplement the basic service.
Additionally, mobility stations should be established with a selection of shared transportation options.
We want to make cycling and walking more attractive and safer in everyday life: More space on the roads, more safe and intact cycle paths and footpaths and more bicycle parking facilities are needed.
This improves the quality of life and traffic safety.
We want to make the road traffic regulations more pedestrian and bicycle friendly.
Germany needs a nationwide cycling network.
Fast cycle routes with green waves must be created in cities and conurbations.
To this end, the federal government must provide sufficient earmarked funds for the municipalities.
DIE LINKE is committed to car-free city centers.
The municipalities are given considerably more leeway for this.
They must be able to independently shape the traffic turnaround on site.
We call for a women-friendly transport infrastructure, for example women's night cabs and safe stops and stations, so that women can move around in public spaces around the clock without fear.
We want a comprehensive program to research the social and technical preconditions as well as consequences of a socio-ecological transport turnaround towards a mobility oriented towards the common good.
Rail for all!
Social and ecological transport planning
The rail service and route network must be expanded nationwide and be affordable, so that all destinations can be reached comfortably by rail.
We are making rail tickets cheaper and introducing a social rail card that cuts ticket prices in half.
DIE LINKE advocates funding for the railroads that covers demand and for expansion.
We demand reliable, timed schedules
and barrier-free and user-friendly stations and trains with service personnel.
We are committed to good work for employees, with good wages and working conditions that do not make people ill.
We want to align Deutsche Bahn's business policy with the common good and environmental sustainability, rather than with net income.
Rail transport must be publicly organized.
All privatisations, spin-offs and splits of existing railroad companies and also the transformation of DB into a stock corporation must be reversed.
We want a democratic citizens' railroad that
also makes use of the competence and experience of the employees.
We want to increase public investment in rail infrastructure fivefold.
All rail lines that can currently only be used by diesel vehicles must be rapidly electrified or converted to alternative and sustainable drive technologies (for example, hydrogen or battery-electric drives).
Freight traffic must also return to the railroads at distances of less than 300 kilometers.
Adequate noise barriers will be built.
Their exteriors can be made available to local art projects.
With a reactivation program, we want to rebuild numerous rail lines that have been shut down in recent decades and thus reconnect entire regions to the rail network.
Mobility by rail must also be possible in rural areas.
Track access charges for passenger transport must be cut by at least half to get more traffic onto the railroads and make rail travel cheaper.
We are adapting the regulations on the DB Bahncard for local transport so that they apply to all tickets and fare levels of the regional transport associations.
In the future, we want to upgrade ICE lines to modern train paths for speeds of up to 250 km/h with at least hourly intervals.
Public transport in medium-sized centers and small towns should connect the ICE stations at least every hour.
DB should also serve all major cities with night trains (couchettes).
We are also campaigning for a Europe-wide night train network so that travel is comfortable even without an airplane.
and ecologically possible.
By 2030, all major European cities must be accessible by long-distance rail in a coordinated timetable.
We are against expensive and nonsensical prestige projects with which the railroads waste billions.
It makes more sense to invest the money specifically in route and network modernization to achieve the necessary capacity increases.
Instead of building new highways, we want to finance and democratically shape the expansion of public transport as well as bicycle and pedestrian traffic in the municipalities and regions:
When planning transportation projects, we want to fully involve citizens and interest groups from the very beginning and put real alternatives up for discussion.
We want to introduce citizens' councils at federal, regional and municipal level in order to democratize transport planning.
Stop new highway construction and expansion.
We want an alternative transport infrastructure plan that achieves the socio-ecological mobility turnaround and focuses on rail-based passenger and freight transport.
Federal structural and transformation grants are not to be used for new road construction and expansion projects.
We oppose all direct or indirect privatization of transport infrastructure.
Public-private partnerships (PPPs) also cause additional costs in the long term,
are a risk for the public sector
and restrict democracy.
We reject the federal government's Autobahn GmbH.
It enables privatization through the back door.
Highway rest areas belong back in public hands.
The privatization of Tank & Rast was and is a bad deal for travelers, employees and the public purse.
We want to transform the commuter allowance into a socially just mobility allowance
and additionally offer an incentive to use the environmental network.
We want to abolish the company car tax privilege so that high earners, employers and the automotive industry in particular do not continue to benefit at the expense of the general public.
and the environment.
To protect people and the climate, we finally need speed limits: 120 km/h on highways, 80 km/h on country roads and a standard speed of 30 km/h in built-up areas.
DIE LINKE wants to regulate and reduce environmental noise, road, rail and air traffic noise with a binding noise protection law.
Funding for noise abatement must be increased (see above).
Noise makes you ill!
Transforming the automotive industry socially and ecologically
The LEFT's socio-ecological transformation offers a way out of the crisis in the auto industry that benefits the workforce more than the federal government's policy of strengthening the big car companies, sticking to individual transport and only wanting to change the drive system.
Federal investment in rail infrastructure and local public transportation can create more than 200,000 well-paying industrial jobs over the next few years.
Priority is given to the production of vehicles for collective mobility concepts such as e-buses, trains and streetcars.
Change of drive: Phasing out the fossil combustion engine by 2030 at the latest is not only without alternative in terms of climate policy,
but also creates planning security for employees
and for investments in the future.
From 2030 at the latest, no more passenger cars with internal combustion engines may be newly registered or exported.
E-mobility must not lead to a return of nuclear power.
The energy supply must be provided by renewable energies
and in a public and cooperative ownership oriented to the common good.
We reject purchase premiums for cars.
The purchase of commercially used, purely electrically powered vehicles for craft businesses, social services, cab companies and other small businesses can be subsidized in exceptional cases depending on the individual business situation.
The state must coordinate the creation of an adequate charging network for electric vehicles - also with the countries of the EU.
We promote electromobility in public transport, i.e. for streetcars, trains, buses, also with overhead lines.
We want to expand research for longer service life and usability of vehicles, for energy-efficient electric vehicles, sustainable and environmentally friendly battery production and improved recycling, and for hydrogen fuel cell propulsion for (small) buses.
We want a ban on advertising for passenger cars with CO2 emissions above the respective current EU target value.
Sustainability must be a top priority.
No more clearing for highways.
We are in solidarity with the protests in Dannenröder Forst.
Reduce air traffic
Flying harms the climate.
Many routes could easily be covered by rail, but the German government continues to subsidize air travel and injected 22 billion euros into Lufthansa during the Corona crisis without achieving guarantees for employees.
We want to shift domestic German and European air traffic to rail as far as possible.
We want a ban on flights to destinations that can be reached by train in up to 5 hours and that are no further than 500 kilometers away.
Online conferencing can eliminate the need for many business trips.
We are committed to ensuring that airports that are necessary for transport policy continue to be operated under public management.
We want to transfer the federal holdings in Lufthansa and Deutsche Bahn to a federally owned company.
The latter must use its options to expand rail traffic
and, in turn, gradually reduce domestic flights significantly and to zero.
Jobs that are lost in air transport can thus be preserved by expanding rail and public transport.
We advocate a strict ban on night flights from 10 p.m. to 6 a.m., especially for areas close to cities.
This ban on night flights must be anchored in the Air Traffic Act.
Flight routes must be drawn up in a transparent, public, democratic and cross-state procedure.
One way to start reorganizing the airport system is to shut down loss-making regional airports.
We want to stop the expansion of further flight capacity.
We want to prevent social and ecological dumping competition in air traffic.
We want a uniform kerosene tax in the EU.
The full VAT rate is to be applied to airline tickets to foreign countries.
We want to abolish the billions of euros in state subsidies for diesel fuel, aviation gasoline and "biofuel.
We reject the allocation of public funds for the development of air cabs and delivery drones.
Reduce freight traffic and put it on the rails
The international corporations ensure that more and more transport miles are put into the products, because the most profitable conditions are used everywhere in the world.
Governments subsidize transportation while longer commutes cost businesses too little.
The price for this is high: accidents, noise, exhaust fumes, climate change and environmental destruction.
The costs of this are borne by the general public - they add up to several billion euros per year and are a burden above all on health insurance funds and the environment.
We want to reverse this trend and make transportation more expensive
and strengthen the regional economy.
We want to extend and increase the truck toll to all roads.
External costs such as air pollution and noise pollution must be included.
We want to prohibit the use of federal and state highways for trucks if a federal highway exists in parallel.
We reject the approval of Gigaliners (long trucks).
Similarly, we oppose federally funded projects to test and introduce overhead power lines for hybrid trucks with pantographs on highways and electronic drawbars for convoy driving by trucks and other commercial vehicles as a wrong turn.
We want to enforce longer rest periods and better working conditions for truck drivers.
We want to relieve city centers of delivery traffic.
The purchase of e-load bicycles is to be promoted, as are intermodal buses or streetcars that also transport parcels.
We want to support municipalities in developing local logistics centers
with good working conditions.
From there, distribution can take place, preferably on foot or by cargo bike.
There should be an increased purchase premium for shared cargo bicycles for all.
Large industrial and commercial areas should be required to have adequate rail sidings.
State aid for shipping must be linked to social and ecological criteria.
We want to ban flags of convenience for German shipping companies.
Competition between ports must be replaced by close cooperation.
Only cargo and cruise ships powered by diesel or environmentally friendly types of propulsion are to be allowed to enter the territorial waters of the EU.
This restricts the use of heavy oil, which is highly harmful to the environment.
DIE LINKE wants to ban the import of "biofuels" because they displace food production in countries of the Global South and destroy biotopes.
Regional vegetable oil fuels should only be allowed to be used in the agricultural sector and for public transport.
Climate justice and energy transition
To save the climate, a fundamental change in our society is necessary.
But the government is delaying the climate, energy and transport turnaround by setting the wrong course in the interests of corporations.
The coal phase-out comes too late.
With the policies of the Grand Coalition, the 1.5 degree target for limiting global warming cannot be achieved.
Although everyone knows that the climate cannot be saved in this way.
The CDU, SPD and Greens want to pass on the costs of the climate crisis to the people.
Yet it is the corporations that make profits with their climate-damaging business models: 100 companies are responsible for 70 percent of global industrial CO2 emissions.
DIE LINKE stands for a socio-ecological system change: for not exploiting man and nature.
For the fact that it is not the wallet that decides whether one can afford an ecological lifestyle.
Climate change is also an issue of rich and poor.
In Germany, too, a socio-ecological turnaround is a question of justice.
The higher the incomes, the higher the environmental impact caused and the CO2 emissions per household.
The price, on the other hand, will be paid by the poor, who will not be able to insure themselves against climate damage or will no longer be able to afford food as food prices rise.
We want a socio-ecological turnaround that benefits everyone through affordable energy, affordable mobility, healthy food and a better quality of life.
To achieve this, we want to disempower the large corporations
and align production with social and ecological goals.
A socio-ecological system change in Germany is also a question of global justice.
The countries of the Global South are particularly affected by climate and environmental degradation and are the least responsible for it.
Women and children in particular suffer disproportionately from the climate catastrophe and environmental damage.
Climate justice also means reducing raw material and resource consumption in this country and working for
a fair distribution of raw material and resource consumption.
In the climate crisis, too, corporations are the crisis winners.
The same corporations that received huge sums of taxpayer money for shutting down and dismantling nuclear power plants are now cashing in again for shutting down coal-fired power plants.
The same threatens with a future shift in power generation away from natural gas.
Our hope is the millions of people who have been on the streets in recent years, striking for climate justice.
We stand alongside the climate movement and support demands for a socially just climate change
towards climate neutrality by 2035. For
us, climate neutrality also means international climate justice.
Germany must not overspend its CO2 budget
or buy its way out of other countries.
With "business as usual," the residual budget will be used up in fifteen years at the latest.
The recent ruling of the Federal Constitutional Court points the right way: Politics must also take responsibility for the livelihood of future generations.
Our program for consistent climate protection and climate justice:
We accelerate the energy transition and switch completely to renewables as quickly as possible.
We want to phase out coal by 2030 at the latest.
We want to disempower the energy companies and bring about an energy transition in the hands of citizens, in public or cooperative ownership.
For a climate-neutral society, the phase-out of nuclear and coal must be followed by a phase-out of fossil natural gas combustion.
DIE LINKE wants a natural gas phase-out law with a binding phase-out path
and social protection for affected employees
and regions.
We want the Federal Republic to be climate neutral by 2035.
By 2030, emissions must be reduced by at least 80 percent compared to 1990 levels.
The goal must be enshrined in the Climate Protection Act.
Emissions trading does not provide effective climate protection.
We reject emissions trading as a leading instrument in climate protection.
Primarily, binding climate targets and emission limits must give clear guidance to corporations.
Subsidy programs and government infrastructure programs must support the conversion.
Electricity, gas, water, heating must not be turned off.
We want to ban energy freezes that hit low-income households and introduce a low-cost basic quota for electricity, water and heating fuels.
We demand that environmental and climate protection be included in the constitution as an extension of fundamental rights.
All political decisions and the disposal of property must be oriented toward the common good, which includes climate protection
and the reduction of social inequality.
Binding climate targets and emission limits must provide clear guidelines for corporations.
The state must not continue to support climate destruction with taxpayers' money.
We therefore call for divestment, i.e. the withdrawal of the state from financial assets, investments and subsidies that flow into projects that serve the fossil and nuclear energy industries.
Get out of coal, make transitions fair
We want to protect the foundations of life and implement the Paris Climate Agreement:
This can only be done if coal-fired power generation is ended by 2030 at the latest, not 2038, as the grand coalition decided in 2019 in the Coal Phase-out Act.
The gradual phase-out of lignite-based power generation must be accompanied by labor market, economic and social policy measures.
Local and regional employee representatives must be involved and dismissals avoided.
DIE LINKE demands the amendment of the national coal phase-out law with the following key points:
The gradual coal phase-out begins immediately.
The last coal-fired power plant must be taken off the grid by 2030 at the latest.
The construction of new coal-fired power plants and the development and expansion of opencast lignite mines will be prohibited.
The new hard-coal-fired power plant Datteln 4, commissioned in 2020, will be taken off the grid immediately.
Structural change in the opencast mining regions must not be carried out on the backs of the employees in the mining areas.
and the local population.
It will take 40 billion euros over the next few years to make the transitions fair.
We call for a gender-equitable structural change.
In regions particularly affected by structural change, we want to set up transformation councils to provide expert support for the social and ecological restructuring of the economy.
They should have the right of initiative over the money from the transformation fund and the regional infrastructure policy.
The councils must be adequately funded to ensure their ability to function.
They are made up of representatives of science, environmental and consumer associations, trade unions and half of directly elected citizens and representatives of the workforce.
We want to promote the effective participation of children and young people, especially in rural areas.
No more villages must be dredged for lignite mining, and
Hambach Forest must not be destroyed any further.
We call for the promotion of hemp cultivation in former lignite areas.
The cultivation of hemp is a promising chance to meet our demand for a socio-ecological change within the structural change of an ecological use of the mining area while at the same time offering job opportunities.
The German government must ensure that operators meet their obligations under mining law: Opencast mines must be made usable again and costs for mining damage must be borne by the companies.
Until the necessary phase-out of coal is achieved, the consequences of lignite mining must be limited.
DIE LINKE advocates a reform of the Federal Mining Act: Instead of corporate interests, the environment and local people must come first and have a say in decisions.
The ban on the construction and commissioning of new hard coal and lignite plants in Germany is supplemented by an analogous ban on the construction and commissioning of new hard coal and lignite plants abroad by companies based in Germany, including their subsidiaries.
The export and sale of hard coal and lignite production facilities and corresponding technology abroad will be prohibited by law, and federal subsidies and guarantees in this regard will not be permitted.
We stand by the climate movement and oppose the criminalization of climate activists.
In connection with the redefinition of the EU climate protection and EU energy targets for 2030, the German government must advocate a significantly greater reduction in greenhouse gas emissions compared with 1990 and a significantly higher share of renewable energies in final energy consumption.
At the EU level, we support a reform of EU emissions trading that leads to an increase in climate protection targets in the emissions trading sectors to the Paris targets and excludes any abuse of the instrument.
We reject an extension of the emissions trading system to the heat and transport sectors.
Invest in renewable energy, disempower energy companies
The energy transition will only be successful if it is socially just.
and is shaped by the citizens themselves.
The supremacy of large corporations in energy supply must come to an end.
We want the energy supply to be close to the people
and organize them as part of public services of general interest.
Energy supply must serve the common good and be removed from the profit motive.
Unjustified industrial rebates in eco-taxes, network fees, emissions trading and the Renewable Energy Sources Act (EEG) must be abolished.
They prevent the necessary structural change.
Renewable energies must be expanded in such a way that imports of fossil-generated energy can be dispensed with.
Electricity and heat networks must be transferred to public ownership and democratically controlled.
Large energy companies are being socialized.
If the coal phase-out is accelerated and a decentralized energy supply with storage systems is advanced, much less grid expansion will be required than is currently planned - driven by the profit interests of transmission grid and coal-fired power plant operators.
We want a structural reform of the EEG.
The share of green electricity must be increased to 100 percent as quickly as possible.
Tendering systems are expensive, risky, and burdensome for citizen energy projects; we reject them for projects up to 18 megawatts or five turbines.
The expansion of renewable energies must be steadily increased in the next legislative period and in subsequent years.
In the years up to 2025, we want to install at least 10 gigawatts (GW) of photovoltaics per year, as well as 7 GW of onshore wind energy and 2 GW offshore.
DIE LINKE supports a regionally oriented energy transition that is anchored in the population, for example energy cooperatives and bioenergy villages.
Institutions, facilities, businesses, cities and municipalities should be given the legal right to purchase the grids they use for power generation and self-supply.
Ecological energy generation and affordable energy prices can best be achieved in municipal utilities with direct democratic participation of the population.
At the same time, this creates the basis for promoting regional economic structures.
Investors must be obliged to offer the local communities a share in new wind power plants, photovoltaic power plants and energy storage systems.
As a result, the municipalities become co-owners.
They must participate in the financial returns of green power operators in this way or through operator levies on siting municipalities.
In order to drive forward the energy transition, we want to improve the legal framework for homeowners, tenants' associations, businesses and local authorities who want to take control of their own energy supply.
DIE LINKE supports tenant power concepts of an in-house power supply through photovoltaic systems on the roof.
We want a solar obligation for new buildings as well as for existing buildings after a comprehensive roof renovation and if there is a technical suitability for solar power generation.
Bioenergy from energy crops grown specifically for this purpose or newly harvested wood should no longer generally be considered ecological and should not receive government support as renewable energy.
Nuclear phase-out immediately: The phase-out of nuclear power must be enshrined in the Basic Law and all operating nuclear power plants must be shut down immediately.
Nuclear exports must be banned.
The corporations must bear the long-term costs of the nuclear industry.
We are committed to the nuclear phase-out in Europe and all over the world.
A pan-European nuclear decommissioning plan is needed.
The German state development bank KfW (Kreditanstalt für Wiederaufbau) is not allowed to promote nuclear power plants abroad.
We want to ban the import and export of uranium fuel.
The production of uranium fuel in the plants in Gronau and Lingen, which have so far been excluded from the nuclear phase-out, must be ended.
No storage in the "final repository" Schacht Konrad in Salzgitter.
For the nuclear waste to be retrieved from the scandalous Asse II waste repository in the Wolfenbüttel district, a fair search for a site for an interim storage facility at a greater distance from residential areas than has been planned so far is needed.
Nuclear waste storage cannot be imposed from above and without the participation of those affected and those active in the anti-nuclear movement.
This requires comprehensive co-determination and rights of appeal in all phases of the search procedure to be developed.
The costs for the decommissioning and dismantling of nuclear facilities must be borne by the nuclear companies.
The highest level of radiation protection and safety must apply
as well as comprehensive public participation that goes beyond existing nuclear law.
Public funds, including pension reserves and retirement funds, must be immediately withdrawn from investments in fossil-nuclear energy companies.
Public institutions must not invest in fossil and nuclear energy companies.
With their Fracking Permit Act of June 2016, the CDU/CSU and SPD approved fracking in sand rock (so-called tight gas reservoirs).
We want to ban fracking without exceptions.
Now that the decision has been taken to phase out coal and nuclear power, the task is to launch a roadmap for an ecological and socially acceptable phase-out of natural gas in order to achieve climate neutrality in 2035.
We are working to ensure that underground injection of CO2 (carbon capture and storage, CCS) is also banned.
CCS must not be available for greenwashing natural gas or hydrogen.
For residual emissions (these are CO2 emissions that cannot be prevented in the future and permanently, such as in agriculture or the cement industry), sinks are promoted to compensate, for example through peatland and forest management.
Control electricity prices more tightly, make energy affordable for all
Access to energy is a fundamental right.
DIE LINKE wants to prevent energy poverty.
Payment difficulties must not lead to people having to sit in the dark or freeze.
For the average consumption of electric power, water and heating energy, we want to create low-cost base rates.
Anything above the average consumption will be more expensive.
This creates incentives to save electricity.
Electricity prices must be monitored more closely
and socially fairer.
The responsible state authority is therefore to be assisted by an advisory board in which consumers, environmental and social associations, and trade unions are represented.
We want to introduce a uniform national grid charge across all voltage levels so that grid charges in regions with many green power plants are not higher than in regions with few green power plants.
We are calling for stricter competition and antitrust laws for electricity, gas and mineral oil companies.
We want to reduce the price of electricity for end customers by: financing the promotion of renewable energies to a significant extent via the federal budget instead of via the current green electricity levy (EEG levy) and reducing the electricity tax for private consumers*.
Housing benefit is to be paid on the basis of the gross warm rent and extended to include a component for electricity costs.
The heating, hot water and electricity cost components are to be combined in the housing allowance to form an energy cost component ("climate housing allowance").
This prevents energy poverty.
We want to set up an eco-scrapping premium for household appliances.
The electrical appliances to be replaced must be at least ten years old and the new appliances must have the best electricity efficiency.
The incentive bonus for replacing refrigerators in low-income households will be increased from 100 to 200 euros, and additional incentive bonuses will be paid for washing machines and dishwashers.
The cheapest and most environmentally friendly is still the kilowatt hour that does not have to be provided.
Standards are needed that specify the maximum energy consumption of products, production methods and buildings.
Only durable, repair-friendly, material- and energy-saving products may be manufactured.
An energy efficiency fund can support and socially accompany the transition to an efficient economy.
The existing building stock must be almost completely renovated to make it more energy efficient by 2035.
To this end, we want to expand socially just subsidy programs (see chapter "No Profits with Rent").
Green hydrogen in the energy transition
With the help of hydrogen, coal and natural gas can also be replaced where the direct use of green electricity is not possible.
Strategies to run cars and building heating systems on hydrogen in the future are neither social nor ecological: its production consumes too much energy.
DIE LINKE calls for hydrogen and its derivatives to be produced in the future only on the basis of green electricity and to be used exclusively where no more efficient alternatives are available, such as in the decarbonization of the steel industry, parts of the chemical industry, in aviation and maritime transport, and for reverse power generation during dark periods.
Where the electrolysis plants are publicly funded, they must be at least proportionately publicly operated.
We reject the import and promotion of hydrogen from nuclear power or fossil sources.
For sustainable agriculture.
Healthy food for all
Food is often transported hundreds or thousands of miles before it reaches the table.
The food chain is dominated by large corporations that make their profits at the expense of people and the environment.
Small and organic farms are having a hard time.
The agricultural sector is becoming increasingly export-oriented across Europe.
This contributes to the destruction of local agricultural structures in many countries of the Global South, but also here locally.
We want to promote socially just agriculture oriented toward the common good, with an emphasis on regional production, processing and marketing.
And: Good working conditions are needed in agriculture and food production.
Four large retail groups determine 85 percent of food sales in Germany and make fat profits,
while many farmers barely make ends meet.
We advocate good working conditions and incomes through nationwide collective agreements in agriculture, forestry and fisheries.
In agriculture, too, you have to be able to make a good living from your work - as a family worker, in seasonal work as well as full-time.
We want affordable and healthy food for all.
We want regional processing and marketing structures as a counter-strategy to the market power of slaughterhouse, dairy and retail groups.
We limit corporate power through effective antitrust legislation geared to the common good.
Links between business and politics must be disclosed - not only in agriculture - through a mandatory lobby register.
We promote peasant, cooperative and organic agriculture.
We will expand organic farming to at least 25 percent of agricultural land by 2030.
Cooperative farming, forms of solidarity farming and producer and marketing associations are to be given special support.
We want to make land available for regionally based farms and rural populations.
Farmland does not belong in the hands of non-agricultural investors.
We want to strengthen public ownership of agricultural and forestry land and transfer land owned by the Land Utilization and Management Company (BVVG) in eastern Germany into the hands of the federal states.
We want to introduce a public land fund that would provide long-term leases to sustainable, local farms on fair terms.
We want to promote young farmers and cooperative concepts.
We want to tackle this with a comprehensive reform of the regulatory, tax, subsidy and price regulations on land.
As a matter of principle, agricultural land is to be sold to farmers and non-profit land companies at prices that correspond to the capitalized value.
DIE LINKE is committed to a fundamental reform of EU agricultural policy.
From the coming funding period, payments are to be consistently linked to scientifically based environmental and social criteria.
and bound to animal welfare.
Only farms that implement these requirements should receive direct payments - whether large or small, organic or conventional.
There should only be money for concretely verifiable public services.
The creation and preservation of jobs subject to social insurance contributions should be supported
and yield-oriented investors must be excluded.
With higher producer prices, we want to reduce the dependence of farms on subsidies and ensure that food remains affordable through a fair distribution of profits in the value chain.
DIE LINKE wants to ban patents on life.
To safeguard genetic diversity, old plant varieties and animal breeds are to be preserved and free reproduction rights secured.
We want to strengthen GMO-free classical and organic breeding with higher research funding.
We want to ban the cultivation and trade of genetically modified plants, including those from new genetic engineering processes.
Cloning of animals must remain prohibited.
We want imported food produced from cloned animals and their offspring to be labeled.
We want to ban the cultivation, trade and import of genetically modified plants.
We want to advocate for a global moratorium on the release of gene drive organisms.
Glyphosate and neonicotinoids must be banned.
We want transparency and a strict set of rules for the approval of crop protection products.
Pesticides and pesticide active ingredients not approved in the EU may neither be produced in Germany nor exported.
Through an ambitious pesticide reduction strategy, farms are to be supported in the conversion to environmentally friendly arable farming.
We want to strengthen domestic production of animal feed, regional processing and marketing structures.
We want to promote farming systems that are particularly protective of the climate, soils, animals and plants (for example, organic farming, paludiculture, permaculture, agroforestry systems, deep-rooted crops).
To this end, we want to develop a comprehensive support and training program for farmers that not only provides financial support, but also creates knowledge for the socio-ecological agricultural transition.
We want livestock production that is land-based and related to domestic demand.
We are introducing inventory caps for regions and locations.
We reject mega stables.
We strengthen citizen participation in approval procedures for the construction of fattening pens.
We are initiating the transformation to socially accepted and climate-friendly animal husbandry.
At the same time, socially fair financing must be ensured.
We are making the groups that have profited to date pay an appropriate share of the conversion costs.
We want a ban on live animal transports that exceed the maximum of four hours.
Preference should always be given to the nearest slaughterhouse.
More frequent unannounced inspections and tougher penalties for violations are needed.
More regional slaughter options including mobile slaughter and pasture slaughter are needed.
Slaughter procedures must become less painful and less stressful.
We want to ban torture breeding and non-curative interventions on animals (beaks, horns, tails).
This also applies to the shredding of chicks, tethering for cattle and cage rearing.
Breeding sows must not be kept in crates.
Put an end to cruel castration methods!
The use of antibiotics in agriculture must be limited to sick animals after medical prescription, animal welfare controls must be tightened and violations must be punished more severely.
To prevent misuse, the prescription and sale of antibiotics must be separated.
Vital reserve antibiotics are not to be used in agricultural animal husbandry.
We want to strengthen agricultural research.
By improving epidemiological research, we aim to detect and contain the outbreak and spread of animal diseases more quickly.
To this end, we call for an interdisciplinary epidemiological center to develop, for example, an early warning system for pandemic risks.
We want to introduce free daycare and school meals nationwide that rely on regional and ecologically sustainable foods.
We want to strengthen school and self-harvest gardens.
This is also a contribution to short distances in the supply of food.
DIE LINKE advocates a simplification of food labeling:
A mandatory label on the front of the packaging should provide information on the sugar, salt and fat content of the product.
A binding, governmental labeling of animal husbandry helps so that consumers can also contribute to more animal welfare.
Food must be safe and not make people sick.
We therefore advocate for more and unannounced food inspections.
The results of food inspections must be published.
Placing contaminated food on the market must be punished more severely.
To reduce food waste, we advocate binding reduction targets along the entire value chain.
Supermarkets must be required to provide discarded but still edible food free of charge.
Protect biodiversity, animals and resources
The diversity of the earth's ecosystems seems almost endless.
They form the basis for all life on our planet and must therefore be resolutely and effectively protected.
It has long since ceased to be just a matter of protecting individual biotopes and species.
It is about the restoration, development and protection of the planet's ecosystems.
Often, short-term interests of companies and their lobby stand in the way.
This was prominently demonstrated by the disputes over the Hambach and Dannenröder forests.
Forests are being destroyed, and this in the midst of climate catastrophe.
The environment, nature and climate are being sacrificed to profits worldwide, with drastic consequences.
About 150 animal and plant species become extinct every day.
Through wildlife trafficking and uncontrolled human encroachment into natural habitats, we increase the risk of viruses spreading from animals to humans.
This can lead to new pandemics.
DIE LINKE stands for a turnaround as quickly as possible.
This is not possible without clear rules for companies and society.
We want to reduce subsidies that destroy nature and the environment and invest the money freed up in nature and environmental programs.
Nature conservation and biodiversity goals must be integrated into other policy areas in a binding way to ensure the conservation of nature and biodiversity.
For control purposes, the environmental administrations must be equipped with more specialized personnel.
To ensure compliance with EU nature conservation directives and their national equivalents, they must be supported financially.
We want to increase the federal "Biological Diversity" program.
We want to implement the UN Convention on Biological Diversity and realize a nationwide, coordinated biodiversity monitoring program (biodiversity monitoring).
It is intended to record the total population of animal and plant species and their development throughout Germany and to create the basis for more nature conservation at all levels.
Landscape planning is a key conservation tool, but needs improvement.
We want to realize nature conservation in the area.
We will provide more financial and human resources for landscape planning.
Study programs in areas such as landscape planning, environmental planning, landscape ecology should be expanded.
We advocate the legal anchoring and full extension of the right of environmental, nature and animal protection associations and individuals to take legal action in accordance with the Aarhus Convention.
Nature conservation areas belong in public hands and should be given to nature conservation and environmental associations on a leasehold basis.
We want to secure and expand the national natural heritage - financed by a natural heritage fund.
To meet the 2020 goal of 2 percent wilderness, areas beyond these lands must also be designated for wilderness development.
We want to create more biotope networks.
Insects must be protected as an important part of the ecosystem, preserved and biodiversity must be promoted.
To achieve this, the use of pesticides must be drastically reduced (see chapter "Agriculture").
The forest is a central and important CO2 sink and must be preserved.
This can be achieved with near-natural forest management, which relies on mixed forests with a diverse age structure and European tree species.
We will consistently pursue and combat environmental crime.
Protecting animals effectively: Animal protection as a state objective
Our treatment of animals often depends on profit interests.
Animals are subject to our actions, so we have a responsibility to reduce and avoid their suffering.
Current policies and laws do not reflect the wishes of the public or the scientific knowledge of animal sentience.
We are committed to a comprehensive reform of the Animal Welfare Act in line with the state objective of animal welfare enshrined in the Basic Law and to eliminating the enforcement problem and ensuring that it is enforced.
We want the democratization of animal welfare: decisions must be made in parliament and not via regulations.
