We need higher standards without loopholes, more transparency in the animal industry (for example, through a publication requirement for administrative acts, etc.) and the implementation of independent controls and appropriate personnel.
On average, a barn is inspected only once every seventeen years.
This is also problematic for pest and disease control and environmental protection.
We demand the right to sue associations nationwide and the introduction of an independent federal animal protection commissioner, based in the Ministry of Justice, who is involved in legislation and educates parliaments and the public through campaigns.
Employees in relevant authorities need to be further trained and sensitized.
Cruelty to animals must be punished more severely.
We want to prohibit cruelty breeding, including in pets, and medically unnecessary interventions in physical integrity.
We demand a binding phase-out plan from animal testing with concrete steps and set deadlines.
Animal experiments of the severity level "most severe" and "severe" must be banned immediately.
In order to secure research locations in the long term, taxes should only flow into animal-free methods.
Husbandry standards in zoos, commercial and domestic settings must be minimized to meet the basic needs of each species.
Social animals should only be kept individually in exceptional cases.
We demand an immediate ban on dolphinariums, wild animals in circuses and a ban on keeping animals at fairs and similar places.
Animal trade (especially on the internet) must be strictly regulated, poaching and illegal wildlife trade must be fought.
The trade in fur must be banned.
We need real protection for wildlife through area-wide biotope connections and wildlife corridors and passages, including, for example, fencing along highways and speed limits to reduce wildlife accidents.
Natural and marine protected areas need to be expanded as habitats to the maximum.
Habitats for animals should also be preserved in cities.
We want to limit recreational hunting.
We want to prohibit the hunting of dogs and cats, as well as predators such as foxes.
Protecting soils and oceans
Natural and intact soils are the basis for an intact planet.
They form the foundation of the natural basis of life and are themselves treasures of biodiversity.
Soils fulfill a wide variety of functions, from carbon sinks, water reservoirs and pollutant filters to the basis for all human uses and a valuable archive of the earth's history.
The oceans cover 70 percent of the Earth's surface and have an enormous impact on climate.
Marine, aquatic, and terrestrial ecosystems harbor a vast array of creatures and habitats that are irreplaceable to life on our planet.
The consequences of the enormous destruction and degradation of soils, waters and oceans are already visible and threaten life on earth.
The use of soils, waters and oceans must finally become ecologically sustainable, because soil and ocean protection is also climate protection in action.
New sealing of soil must be significantly reduced.
New sealing may only be approved if it is accompanied by at least an equal amount of land unsealing in the region.
New roads may only be built if there is an independently determined need.
Unsealing potential must be recorded in land use and landscape plans.
A fund must be introduced to free polluted land from contaminated sites.
In Germany, approximately 90 percent of peatlands are degraded, accounting for up to 5 percent of our CO2 emissions.
The preservation or renaturation and rewetting of peatlands can make a major contribution to achieving climate protection goals and must therefore be promoted.
We want to better protect ground and surface waters.
The EU target of bringing all waters to good ecological status by 2015 was missed.
Rivers and groundwater are still used as waste dumps for the potash industry, for example.
Too many nutrients from sewage treatment plants and agriculture are discharged into rivers and groundwater.
The oceans are heavily polluted, and the climate catastrophe is clearly exacerbating the situation.
Together with environmental protection associations, we are calling for a marine offensive: no overfishing, effective protection of marine species and habitats.
Marine protected areas must be preserved and expanded - at least 50 percent of protected areas must be taken out of commercial use.
And more money and personnel are needed to implement measures.
We reject the privatization of water supply and access to sea and ocean areas (see chapter "International").
We want to drive forward the Water Framework Directive.
This includes the preservation or restoration of near-natural structures, the reduction of pollutant inputs from fertilizers and pesticides into rivers and seas and the protection of floodplain areas.
The National Action Plan for Plant Protection (NAP) is to be transformed into an effective plan for reducing pesticides in Germany.
We want to continue, implement and financially secure the federal "Blue Ribbon Germany" program.
Environmental pollution of water bodies due to improper disposal of pharmaceuticals is dangerous.
We want to (re)introduce the take-back system for medicines.
We are committed to protecting Natura2000 areas in the North Sea and Baltic Sea.
The protected areas should be free from fishing, military use, resource extraction and other economic interventions.
We want to promote alternative fishing methods to eliminate bottom-disturbing (trawls) and habitat-damaging methods,
and sustainable fishing with catch quotas based on scientific recommendations.
The military legacy on land and in water bodies must be eliminated.
In particular, former, hitherto uncleared military training areas and the legacies of two world wars in the North Sea and Baltic Sea represent time bombs whose defusing must finally be tackled with vigor.
Funding is to be provided from the Bundeswehr budget.
There is no planet B: Managing resources in the cycle
Global resources are limited; renewable raw materials also need time to renew themselves.
We need to get out of the throwaway society and into a circular economy.
n To protect natural resources and increase the use of recycled materials, we want to promote regional economic cycles and introduce a resource consumption tax for primary raw materials and disposable products.
We want to expand ecodesign requirements for products to create requirements for durability, updatability, upgradability, repairability, reusability, and recyclability.
We support the "top runner model" for the production of devices (the most sustainable device at a given time sets the new standard).
For repair services and dismantling, we want to reduce the sales tax to 7 percent.
Repair and reuse must take priority over recycling.
Waste treatment and waste disposal must be a public service.
It must not be privatized.
If privatization has already taken place, DIE LINKE fights for remunicipalization.
Waste should be disposed of and processed as close as possible to where it was generated.
We want to introduce a deposit system for energy-saving light bulbs, disposable cups, cell phones, televisions and other electrical appliances and batteries to increase the collection rate and improve recycling.
We want to introduce quantitative waste avoidance targets ("Zero Waste"),
achieve a decrease in absolute resource consumption
and get a grip on the plastic flood.
One contribution to this is to be made by standardized reusable systems, which are to be available in every store at least throughout Germany, and not only in the "to go" sector, but also in mail order and in business-to-business transactions.
The reusable systems are also to be created for food, detergents, cosmetics, etc.
Where these systems are operational, disposable packaging should be banned.
Any remaining plastic packaging must be designed in such a way that it can be recycled.
Wood is also becoming increasingly important as a building material.
To prevent wood poverty, we must also use wood as a resource sparingly.
We want a much better wood recycling system with a utilization cascade in which wood combustion for energy production is only at the very end.
Energy directly from the forest is not a contribution to climate protection.
More rights for consumers
Companies, banks and corporations have the upper hand over consumers and often use their power to the detriment of consumers.
DIE LINKE is not only focusing on transparency, but also wants to strengthen the rights of consumers.
It combines consumer policy with the social question, because the windy business practices are aimed especially at people with low incomes and senior citizens - who are particularly hurt by this rip-off in the wallet.
We want an independent consumer protection authority with strong enforcement powers.
Consumer protection associations are to be better funded and their rights strengthened.
To this end, they are also to receive income from the federal government from the fines imposed for cartel penalties.
Debt collection rip-offs must be stopped by clear fees capped by law and by increasing reminder requirements for companies.
More than 15 Euro collection costs or 5 Euro for claims up to 50 Euro are unserious.
We want to greatly curb the power of Schufa and other economic information files on people's everyday lives.
A Schufa inquiry should only be permitted for actual credit transactions, no longer for consumer contracts for everyday needs such as rent, electricity and cell phone bills.
A negative Schufa score must be deleted again after one year.
In addition, in the future, credit rating information will no longer be allowed to be provided by a private company, but only by the public sector.
Unfair telephone advertising must be stopped.
Contracts concluded by telephone may only become effective when consumers confirm the contract in writing.
We want to abolish cost traps such as two-year contract terms for fitness and cell phone contracts and automatic contract renewals.
Extortionate prices for consumer loans through imposed or foisted residual debt insurance must be ended.
Consumers must be protected against insolvency of tour operators and airlines.
To enable consumers to jointly defend themselves against corporate trickery and enrichment at consumers' expense, we are campaigning for class actions that lead directly to compensation from companies.
A legally guaranteed minimum useful life of five years is to become mandatory for durable technical equipment such as refrigerators, washing machines and vehicles, IT and electrical appliances.
In addition, IT products and household appliances must be easy to repair and upgrades must be possible at any time.
We call for product liability to be adapted to the digital age.
Consumers have a right to transparent information from public authorities and companies.
For this, we need a strong consumer information law.
We want consumers to have the right to short, clear and comparable information, for example about costs and contract terms for loans and investments, Internet contracts and insurance policies.
We want a stricter transparency standard for online marketplaces and online platforms.
We want a gradual restriction of product and brand advertising in public spaces.
Immediately we demand a ban on advertising in schools and daycare centers.
Consumer education must include social and environmental impacts.
Consumers must have the right to determine for themselves what happens to their data without being disadvantaged.
The General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) contains important rights for this purpose, which have not been sufficiently protected and used to date.
Good consumer protection depends on whistleblowers who draw attention to abuses in companies, public authorities and other institutions.
We need a whistleblower protection law in Germany so that these people are protected and do not remain silent for fear of reprisals.
Consumer *inside protection for financial products!
Independent advice instead of penny-pinching.
We will abolish commission-based sales of financial and insurance products.
Fee-based advice and independent financial advice by consumer centers must be strengthened.
Keeping promises to consumers.
We require insurers and other financial services providers to honor the guarantees and commitments made for their products, even under low interest rate conditions.
In the case of traditional life insurance policies, valuation reserves and surpluses, to which consumers are generally entitled, may not be reduced.
Regulate the entire capital market and limit fees.
We subject the almost unregulated "gray" capital or credit market to effective uniform financial supervision and regulate it strictly.
Good financial consumer protection also includes limiting unreasonable fees and charges for banking services.
We also significantly limit prepayment penalties for early repayment of loans.
Self-confident East Strengthen East German interests
East Germany deserves more: more self-confidence, more visibility, more respect, more honesty.
But beyond the commemorative hours for the fall of the Wall, nationwide interest always fades quickly.
There is a lot to talk about.
The unfinished unity raises the question of the state of equality
and cohesion in the Federal Republic.
The question of participation - and of opportunities for advancement, regardless of origin and social status.
We need to talk about the East as a neoliberal testing ground for Bonn's policies, about the consequences of the Treuhand's radical economic restructuring and the loss of public infrastructure.
Decisions made by the Treuhand and the policies of so-called Reconstruction East still determine the development paths of East German society today.
Deindustrialization, mass unemployment and population decline were and are the consequences.
We need to talk about right-wing violence and organizing and the long history of its trivialization.
Talks about the weak anchoring of political institutions, skepticism about party democracy, about a lack of influence among East Germans.
Because the consequences are still visible today.
If one looks at differences in wages and pensions, at top functions and assets, at poverty or emigration - the old borderline between West and East Germany continues to stand out.
Many East Germans wish to be visible in other ways.
With what they have worked for and achieved, both in the past GDR and in the thirty years since.
East Germany stands for the courage to live of different generations.
Many, especially among the younger generation, are no longer willing to accept the structural disadvantages and keep quiet about the problems in the East.
Many know the feeling that their own abilities and achievements - or those of their parents - are not recognized.
Almost every second person in the East feels that his or her work is not valued.
For a long time, East German employees were prepared to perform even under tough conditions and to put their own interests aside: in the interests of the company and in view of the poorer prospects in the East for everyone.
The lost battles against the Treuhand were in the bones of many for a long time.
Now the willingness to strike and fight is growing again.
The struggle is about more than "just" wage levels and jobs:
Strikes have become a symbol for justice, recognition, more co-determination and self-determination.
They fight for their own rights, the obstinacy of the East and a new beginning for the East.
DIE LINKE is connected to the experiences and struggles of the people in East Germany.
We are the voice of the East.
In the federal states where we hold government responsibility, we are implementing this:
with the introduction of non-contributory kindergarten years and longer joint learning for more educational equality,
through more collective bargaining and through procurement laws with a tariff loyalty clause in public contracts for higher wages.
We are concerned with affordable housing,
shorter working hours, for example through additional public holidays, and
improving the quality of hospital care.
The democratization of universities, schools, municipalities and state politics in general is just as much a part of our government policy
as the goal of preventing the sale of land through the purchase of large farms by non-agricultural investors.
We are concerned with practical, solidary, just and democratic politics.
We are concerned with our own departure.
Equal pay for equal work - What else?
The persistence of unequal living conditions is not an accident of German unification,
but a political will.
Instead of preventing low wages, federal and state governments used them to woo investors for decades.
The result is corporate subsidiaries that exploit the East-West divide, but do not remedy it.
Every third (!) employee in the eastern German states works in the low-wage sector.
In the West, the figure is 16 percent.
This has an impact on lower purchasing power, asset accumulation and pension entitlements.
Half of the full-time employees in the new federal states are threatened with a mini-retirement, despite decades of work.
In a comparison of median gross wages (2019) in eastern and western Germany, 700 euros more gross was in the western pay packet.
In any month.
In Saxony-Anhalt, people work an average of 75 hours longer per year and receive almost 3,000 euros less in annual wages than in neighboring Lower Saxony.
Almost 4 million people have migrated from the East.
This has massively increased structural obsolescence in the east.
In the next few years, a huge wave of retirements in the eastern German states will have to be compensated for.
This requires perspectives, also for returnees and new immigrants.
Equal pay for equal work with equal working hours between women and men, in East and West - that is our claim:
The low-wage sector must be closed and the statutory minimum wage must be raised quickly to 13 euros.
Employees in eastern Germany in particular would benefit from this.
DIE LINKE is calling for a wage offensive in the east through more collective bargaining coverage and nationwide collective agreements in order to bring wages in the new Länder 100 percent into line with the level in the west by the end of the next legislative period in 2025.
We want uniform pay scales in the east and west.
The IG Bau trade union has proven that wage alignment is possible.
The East-West wage wall can be overcome where unions are particularly influential.
In comparable industries, the same working hours and vacation regulations must apply nationwide.
We want to make a minimum award wage based on the level of the lowest salary class in the collective agreement for the public service of the federal states (TVL) binding for awarding contracts.
Recognize lifetime achievement in the East - Equal pension for equal lifetime achievement
30 years after the end of the GDR, work and life achievements are still not worth the same.
Pensions are not to be fully equalized until 2024.
The equalization of pensions in the east must not be to the detriment of current employees.
Around 20 percent lower salaries and wages in the east mean fewer pension entitlements in old age.
Among people who (will) retire in the East in twenty years, the risk of poverty is twice as high as in the West.
Anyone who was 30 years old when the Wall came down will still have to reckon with disadvantages when they themselves retire in 2027.
The diversity of the GDR old-age security systems did not match the pension system of the FRG.
There were gaps or even deletions during the transition to German law.
Injustices that still exist.
This concerns the large group of scientific, technical, educational, medical and artistic intelligentsia.
Likewise, pension commitments for certain occupational groups were eliminated, for example, for GDR employees in the Reichsbahn, the postal service or in lignite refining.
Women are particularly affected, especially if they worked in the health care sector, were assisting wives or were divorced in the GDR.
Since the 1990s, groups forgotten by the Federal German legislature have been demanding the restoration of their entitlements.
They have had our support ever since.
DIE LINKE wants an immediate 100 percent adjustment of eastern pensions to the western level.
This means that the pension value (East) must immediately be raised to the West level of the general pension value.
Prevent pension cuts!
As long as the wages of East German employees are structurally significantly lower, the conversion must remain in place for pensions.
A legal correction of the pension transition remains necessary.
Adequate compensation payments can also be a way to finally recognize these claims, at least in part.
For periods of low pay, we want to introduce a general increase in the value of pensions for all employees in both East and West.
That is why we want to remove the time limit on pensions based on minimum earning points and improve them.
More posts for the East - More plural visibility
Even 30 years after the end of the GDR, the leading positions in the united Germany are firmly in West German hands.
In the East and even more so in the West.
The social transformation of the 1990s was more than a politically desirable and necessary change of elites.
Almost without exception, people from the former GDR moved into the second row, making way for new bosses from the West.
This state of affairs has become entrenched.
The new thematization of the disadvantages faced by East Germans is part of a hard-won emancipation process.
For decades, newspapers of West German publishers and West German editors reported from East German state radio stations, and mostly in a one-sided way.
The greater skepticism toward public broadcasting has one of its causes here.
For decades, the predominant theme was convergence with the norm of the West.
If you want to strengthen democracy, you have to involve everyone.
Leadership positions must be a reflection of a society, otherwise they violate the democratic principle of the equality of all.
This means more women, more East Germans, more migrants in the management levels nationwide!
It's time for policy-driven practices that end disadvantage:
We need a leap in gifted education to prepare and enable careers instead of masking underrepresentation.
We call for the implementation of the proposed Transformation Center in Eastern Germany as a research and support site for the working society in the digital and ecological transformation.
The civil service must become an engine to enable career paths for East Germans, with appropriate support instruments to lift up underrepresented groups.
This is what we are committed to.
We want to create visibility for discrimination instead of hiding it behind the formula of "unity." We call for the voluntary collection of birthplace and biographical data from federal and state agencies, higher education funding programs, foundations, and grant-making agencies.
Our goal is to relocate more areas of public broadcasting to the eastern German states with more decision-makers with an eastern biography.
We are fighting to ensure that federal agencies or companies in which the federal government has a stake relocate their headquarters to eastern Germany.
We want to locate newly emerging federal agencies in the east.
Reappraising the Treuhand past
While the East Germans were drawing their waiting numbers at the employment office, West German and foreign entrepreneurs were busy at the Treuhandanstalt.
You could get rich in the East if you came from the West.
94 percent of the GDR companies privatized by the federal government went into West German or foreign hands.
Together with associated land and real estate.
The majority of landlords of East German apartments have since been based in West Germany, or the apartments are now owned by real estate groups.
The work of the Treuhand not only has consequences that reach into the present, it was also accompanied by political and economic scandals.
Thousands of those who risked everything on the streets in Leipzig in 1989 were already standing on Leipzig's Augustusplatz again in 1991.
Profit interests of West German corporations stood above the fate of millions.
This disappointment continues to have an effect in the East to this day.
DIE LINKE is fighting for this injustice to be dealt with.
DIE LINKE wants a committee of inquiry into the Treuhand in the coming legislative period.
DIE LINKE also wants to take another closer look at the Unification Treaty.
Its content and effects need to be examined - also with regard to whether claims of East Germans were neglected or ignored in the implementation of the treaty, and whether they may still be enforceable.
To this end, we propose an inquiry commission.
For an economic awakening in the East
The East has undergone tremendous economic development over the past thirty years.
However, the economic performance of the eastern countries still lags behind the western countries.
Promising approaches that already existed, such as the solar industry in eastern Germany, were destroyed by the wrong political course set by the CDU and their respective coalition partners.
Tens of thousands of jobs in an industry of the future were thus recklessly put at risk.
We rely on a regionally anchored economy that is geared to the needs of the people in the respective regions.
This also applies to agriculture.
The East should no longer be the extended workbench of large West German corporations.
DIE LINKE is committed to public welfare-oriented and cooperative economic concepts.
Against the dominance of market-based exploitation and efficiency logic, we are committed to good care,
Public services of general interest
and stopping the privatization of public property.
Workers in East Germany have developed a new self-confidence in recent years.
Many went on strike for better wages and working conditions.
We stand in solidarity with and support the workers and trade unions, especially in the labor struggles in eastern Germany.
After reunification, the East lost its industrial base, including food processing and marketing.
We now want to drive forward a reindustrialization of the east in order to create well-paid and secure jobs in the long term.
We want to make the east a region of the future where climate-friendly industrial jobs are created.
We want to strengthen regional products, processing and distribution structures.
Production cooperatives and distribution cooperatives from the regions should be connected.
We want a reindustrialization program for the East.
This is intended to promote the creation of climate-friendly industrial jobs throughout the East.
Reactivation of public infrastructure
The history of the East after reunification is also a history of the dismantling of (social) infrastructure.
Closed schools, swimming pools, savings banks or disused railroad lines characterize the picture throughout the eastern part of the country.
We want to reverse this trend.
We want to create social centers in the villages.
The supervision of the social centers takes place through jobs paid according to collective agreements.
In Saxony alone, almost a quarter of the rail network has been shut down since 1994.
Nearly 2,500 kilometers of rail track throughout the East.
This was a serious mistake in terms of climate policy and structural policy.
In many places, rail connections are sorely missed.
Entire regions are thus permanently cut off.
As the owner of Deutsche Bahn, the federal government has a duty to change this course.
The railroad must return to the area.
The digital infrastructure in eastern Germany also needs a major boost.
Poor mobile networks and a lack of broadband expansion are unfortunately the order of the day in many regions in eastern Germany.
For companies operating purely according to profit logic, expansion in sparsely populated regions is not worthwhile.
In many eastern German municipalities, there is a considerable need for investment in the age-appropriate and barrier-free conversion of apartments.
The age-appropriate conversion of housing is becoming a major task for many eastern German cities and communities.
Many eastern German municipalities lack a sufficient supply of barrier-free apartments and housing for people with disabilities.
Often, entire neighborhoods and districts have disappeared as a result of the demolition of prefabricated buildings.
We want to promote social mixing in the existing housing stock in industrial construction across generations, for example through flexible apartment floor plans with the option to combine apartments vertically and horizontally, and equip them with community spaces (fitness, library, small cinema, co-working spaces).
We propose a support program "Every Village Needs a Shop!"
and a reform of the commercial tenancy law to protect and reestablish small stores, crafts and service businesses.
We want a reactivation program by Deutsche Bahn for disused lines in coordination with the federal states, and a nationwide supply of buses and trains.
We are committed to a redevelopment program for rail stations.
The East in particular needs lively train stations as places of encounter and exchange.
Closing wireless gaps and broadband Internet coverage:
For us, this is an elementary component of a sustainable east.
In future, funding will focus on converting buildings to make them suitable for the elderly and disabled and improving the living environment in urban districts.
The municipal contribution to upgrading measures is to be eliminated.
Here, as with demolition, 100 percent funding must be possible.
We want to establish a subsidy program for collective housing with rent control for the prefabricated housing that is widespread in eastern Germany.
We want to support cooperative forms of housing by providing advice on the establishment and financing of new housing or on the acquisition of land and buildings, for example through concept awards.
Against old and new Nazis
The unification process has a dark side that is finally being talked about more.
Much has still not been dealt with or made known to the general public: Freed from repression in the GDR, right-wing violence erupted in the 1990s on a previously unknown scale.
Allies in spirit and deed were quickly found, on both sides: Rostock-Lichtenhagen, Mölln, Solingen, the NSU's series of murders-deadly violence swept the country.
The neo-Nazis tried to dominate the public space and exercised control - at least in neighborhoods and residential areas.
The East German state governments pioneered a shameful trivialization, continuing the common political practice of the West.
There was also no outcry in East German society.
It was up to a few activists, anti-fascist groups, journalists, and people involved in left-wing parties to name the dangers.
Democracy work, education and counseling centers for victims of right-wing violence have been doing a lot for a community based on solidarity and human rights for over twenty years.
Often they are the only offer that helps people defend their rights and dignity after right-wing and racist attacks.
Strong communities, good quality of life
The quality of everyday life is decided on site, in the communities.
The privatization of public property and public services has made everyday life more difficult in many communities and neighborhoods.
Many municipalities in economically disadvantaged regions are over-indebted and under receivership.
The gap between poor and rich municipalities in Germany continues to grow.
The debt brake has a devastating effect on the quality of life of people with lower incomes
and on local democracy.
If the city or municipal council sometimes only decides on the management of the shortage and on supposed constraints, democracy in the municipality is stifled.
We want to bring public services back into public hands
and strengthen the municipalities' own economic activities.
Municipal services of general interest must not be thrown onto the market!
We want to remunicipalize privatized areas of public service.
We want to ensure that the federal government makes funds available to local authorities for the remunicipalization of housing, hospitals, water and energy supplies.
This can be done through a remunicipalization fund.
Support and legal advice can be organized by a remunicipalization agency so that the wheel does not have to be reinvented in every municipality.
Existing restrictions on the economic activity of local authorities must be removed,
Inter-municipal cooperation must be made a model
and in the area of municipal services of general interest, a preference in favor of the public sector can be achieved.
We want incentives for the development of regional economic cycles.
In order to create equal living conditions in all regions and municipalities, the participation of the municipal umbrella organizations is to be ensured through a binding right of consultation and participation of the municipalities at the federal level.
Solidified cash loans of the municipalities must be taken over by the federal government into an old debt fund and repaid with by the federal government.
Cash advances, which were actually intended as short-term financing, have increased by 40 billion euros over the past twenty years.
They are often the only way to fulfill mandatory municipal tasks.
Municipal budgets must be relieved of social benefits.
These must be borne in full by the federal government.
Costs incurred by the federal or state governments must also be financed by them (connexity).
DIE LINKE advocates a reform of the trade tax into a municipal business tax.
Combined with the implementation of connexity, the municipalities can get back on a reliable financial footing.
Many municipal tasks are now "externally determined" down to the last detail by laws and ordinances, and local conditions are hardly taken into account.
That has to change.
Self-government must be strengthened and the municipalities' leeway in economic and construction matters increased.
The promotion of voluntary work must be guaranteed, and therefore municipal expense allowances must not be offset against benefits under SGB II and BAföG.
Ongoing federal programs for municipalities must be made permanent, combinable and adapted to needs.
A large number of municipalities cannot even afford the relatively small contributions they make to federal programs in order to obtain funding for necessary investments that would be almost impossible to finance on their own.
For this reason, own contributions must be abolished, at least for municipalities in difficult budgetary situations.
For fair municipal financing, 100 percent of the municipal financial strength must be included in the state fiscal equalization system.
Reverse with taxes
Never before have income and wealth been so unequally distributed.
Increasingly large fortunes have become concentrated in fewer and fewer hands: Two-thirds of all wealth is in the hands of the top 10 percent of the population.
The 45 richest households alone own as much as the entire poorer half of the population combined.
The richest one percent of the population accounts for around 35 percent of wealth, i.e. more than one third.
The richest 5 percent have more than the "remaining" 95 percent.
If you have a lot, you can easily increase it.
A cheap tax is levied on profits from capital and shares.
Those who have little or nothing, on the other hand, pay more and more: income tax cannot be evaded, it is deducted immediately.
The value-added tax places a heavier burden on low-income people.
Because public property has been privatized, many services have to be paid for privately.
A large proportion of assets in Germany are inherited.
High incomes are taxed less than they were in the 1990s.
For decades, a wealth tax was levied in Germany - but not since 1997.
We want to change that in order to combat the scandalous inequality in Germany.
Private wealth is offset by an impoverished public infrastructure: Libraries and swimming pools are closing, hospital staff is being laid off in order to finance necessary repairs, bus and train services rarely come to the countryside and are often overcrowded in the city because there is not enough capacity.
Here, the revenue from a millionaire's tax would be particularly helpful:
It goes to the states and can strengthen public infrastructure.
The risk of poverty has never been so high: more than one in six people in rich Germany is poor or at risk of poverty.
The rich have many allies in politics.
They can give their voice more weight.
We hold against it!
More justice
and a strong public service can only be achieved by reducing the burden on those at the bottom - and increasing the burden on those at the top.
High assets and incomes, inheritances and profits from capital and shares must be taxed more heavily.
We use it to finance investments in good public services and a welfare state that protects everyone from poverty.
We strengthen solidarity
and ecological forms of the economy
and create jobs.
It's doable, and we know how we're going to pay for it.
There is enough for everyone if everyone contributes enough:
DIE LINKE calls for a wealth tax with a progressive rate and an exemption amount for private assets of 1 million euros per person (excluding debt).
Those who are "paper millionaires" with a downtown condo, for example, will not be charged.
This is particularly important because of the development of real estate prices, which led to massive asset growth for homeowners, but unlike large real estate sharks, this is not accompanied by high returns.
The tax-free amount for business assets is 5 million euros.
Retirement savings to be exempt from tax.
The entry tax rate of the wealth tax starts at 1 percent and increases steadily up to net assets of 50 million euros.
From 50 million euros, the maximum tax rate of 5 percent applies.
This is appropriate because large assets yield particularly high returns.
Moreover, in the case of very large assets, redistribution is also necessary at the expense of asset substance.
The estimated revenue would then be 58 billion euros per year.
Strong shoulders carry more: To tackle the corona crisis, we want to levy a wealth tax.
This is to be levied on net assets in excess of 2 million euros (for business assets the exemption amount is 5 million euros).
The property levy is progressively graduated from 10 to 30 percent and can be paid in installments over twenty years.
The annual burden on net assets is thus between 0.1 and 1.5 percent.
The estimated revenue is 310 billion euros over twenty years.
Inheritance tax: Wealth is inherited, - usually without significant taxes being paid.
The super-rich in particular can bequeath or give away their multi-million assets in company shares tax-free.
We will ensure that tax loopholes are closed.
To this end, the privileges that currently exist for business assets in the case of inheritances and gifts are to be abolished.
We will increase the inheritance tax on high inheritances.
Normal, owner-occupied residential property remains exempt.
Additional revenue per year: 8 to 10 billion euros.
Corporate taxes were massively reduced years ago.
Corporation tax must be increased to 25 percent again.
We want to stop the corporate race to avoid taxes and are pushing for Europe-wide and global minimum corporate tax rates.
When profits are shifted to low-tax jurisdictions, they are to be taxed in arrears in the individual countries in which a group operates.
We will ensure that companies and corporations do not evade taxes.
Megacorporations like Amazon became even more powerful during the Corona crisis, but they hardly pay any corporate tax.
We therefore need a tax reform that taxes such corporations more heavily at the location of their economic activities and sales.
In addition, extraordinary profits made by companies like Amazon because of the Corona crisis must be skimmed off with an excess profit tax to limit the market power of the crisis winners.
Sales tax: We want reduced tax rates for labor-intensive crafts, products for children and pharmaceuticals.
Tax evasion: We want to combat money laundering and subsidy fraud more effectively and thus dry up tax havens - including those "made in Germany".
To this end, we want to set up a federal financial police force and increase tax enforcement staff in line with demand.
It is realistic to collect around 15 billion euros more per year with more consistent tax enforcement and combating tax evasion in tax havens.
Financial transaction tax: We curb speculation on the financial markets.
A tax rate of 0.1 percent is to be applied to every financial transaction.
The funds raised are to be used for sustainable development in the countries of the Global South.
and for global climate protection
and, on the other hand, for the socio-ecological restructuring of our industrial society.
Municipal business tax: We want to convert the current trade tax into a municipal business tax.
The tax base will be expanded (rents, leases and royalties will be taken into account) and high-earning self-employed and freelancers will be included.
To this end, we will raise the tax-free allowance to 30,000 euros and take the tax assessed into account in income tax.
The trade tax levy is abolished, which relieves the financial burden on cities and municipalities.
DIE LINKE advocates the abolition of the sparkling wine tax.
What works in the long term must also be financed in the long term:
The debt brake and the European Fiscal Compact block long-term developments
and are intended to drive privatization.
The debt brake makes no economic sense and should be abolished.
It promotes the privatization of public infrastructure, which is often even more expensive for taxpayers because the general public then has to finance high returns for private investors.
Instead, it must once again be possible to borrow to the extent of the investments.
After all, the interest rates that the state currently has to raise on the capital market are extremely low, and a good infrastructure will still benefit our grandchildren.
Therefore, it makes sense to also stretch the financing of investments through loans.
As long as the debt brake exists and there is a repayment obligation for the federal government's Corona loans, repayment must be spread over at least fifty years.
Expenses for interest payments must not additionally restrict the scope for debt.
This will also expand the financial leeway within the debt brake.
n Fair budget: education,
health
and climate protection
instead of rearmament.
The federal budget includes an increase in military spending.
The German government continues to approach the 2 percent of GDP mark for defense spending.
This prioritization is wrong.
We strongly oppose this and call for an annual reduction in military spending.
Reducing climate-damaging subsidies can also ease the burden on the federal budget.
Overall, savings of 12 billion euros per year are easily possible.
We can use this additional revenue to finance the entry into a society based on solidarity: better social security,
more staff in education, health and care and a new start in non-profit housing construction,
Accessibility
and the start of a socio-ecological restructuring of the economy.
Our claims are offset and realistic.
Reform income tax fairly
We also want to make income taxation fairer.
We want to ease the burden on low and middle incomes.
High incomes must be taxed more heavily.
As a rule of thumb, anyone who (as a single person, tax class I) has a gross income of less than 6,500 euros per month pays less tax according to our tariff.
Everyone benefits from improved public services and lower contributions to our solidarity-based health insurance.
All taxable income below 14,400 euros per year remains tax-free.
The control curve is flattened.
Medium incomes in particular benefit, as a higher tax-free amount means that taxes only have to be paid at all on income above this amount.
We want to tax higher incomes more heavily.
From 70,000 euros taxable income per year, the tax rate is 53 percent.
Taxable income means: what remains of the gross income after the usual deductions (flat-rate allowances and special expenses).
70,000 euros taxable income corresponds to around 81,000 euros gross income for a single person without children.
53 percent tax rate applies to income from 70,000 euros.
The average tax rate for an income of 70,000 euros is around 30 percent.
We envisage two levels of a separate wealth tax: 60 percent for incomes above the current wealth tax threshold of 260,533 euros and 75 percent for incomes above 1 million euros of taxable income.
Income from capital gains should no longer be given preferential treatment, but should be taxed at the same rates as all income.
We will abolish the flat-rate withholding tax of 25 percent, but retain restrictions on the offsetting of losses from capital assets and the saver's allowance.
Marital splitting will be replaced by gender-equal individual taxation with socially acceptable transitional arrangements.
The unused taxable minimum income must be transferable between spouses or partners.
We want to reintroduce tax allowances for severance payments in the event of redundancies.
The commuting allowance will be replaced by a mobility allowance that provides the same tax benefit per kilometer of commuting to work for all employees, regardless of their income.
DIE LINKE wants to maintain the solidarity surcharge for high incomes and transform it into a Solidarity Pact III.
The Soli is the most socially just tax: with the strongest relief at the bottom and for people with children - and the strongest burden for those at the top, especially people without children.
DIE LINKE calls for a Solidarity Pact III to cope with structural change in regions in and after industrial upheaval.
The financial volume must tie in with the Solidarity Pact II, which is why we are calling for at least 10 billion euros a year to be made available from federal funds for structural change and cohesion.
Our Solidarity Pact III is aimed at all structurally weak regions in Germany.
For planning security, we propose a period until 2035 for the Solidarity Pact III and thus a total volume of at least 150 billion euros.
Real Estate Transfer Tax and Share Deals.
Rising real estate prices and the increase in real estate transfer tax rates in almost all German states have significantly increased the tax burden for most real estate purchases.
Real estate groups, on the other hand, which buy large and very large real estate packages, usually get away without paying taxes through so-called share deals.
Formally, they do not buy the real estate, but the majority (up to 90 percent) of the shares in the respective companies that own the real estate.
We are calling for a reform of the real estate transfer tax so that pro rata property purchases (over 50 percent) are also taxed proportionately.
This makes share deals largely unattractive.
Nonprofit.
In recent years, more and more politically active associations have had their non-profit status revoked by the tax office or in court.
However, democracy thrives on participation and diverse debate.
We need a reform of the non-profit law with an expansion of the purposes recognized as non-profit (for example, the promotion of human and fundamental rights, peace, climate protection or social justice).
Participation in the formation of political will must be explicitly named as harmless for the non-profit status, whether for the pursuit of own purposes or beyond that for democracy, rule of law and human rights.
Care must be taken to ensure that this does not result in covert party financing and that the boundaries to party financing are maintained.
Also, the mention of an association in a federal or state report on the protection of the constitution should no longer automatically lead to the deprivation of its non-profit status, as happened most recently in the case of the VVN/BdA.
The use of charitable foundations for tax avoidance must be more restricted.
Tax enforcement.
The major problems in tax enforcement must finally be solved.
On the one hand, this requires significantly more staff and IT capacity at the tax authorities, but it is at least as important to implement and enforce federal tax laws uniformly across the country.
The frequency with which large companies and wealthy individuals are inspected through company and tax external audits varies widely across countries.
We need much more frequent and intensive tax audits for corporations and wealthy individuals.
The effective solution to this interest-driven petty stateism would be to transfer tax enforcement to the federal level ("federal tax administration").
The tax authorities are also often inactive in pursuing and combating semi-legal and prohibited tax structuring models (see the following chapter).
Breaking the power of banks and financial markets
More than ten years after the financial and global economic crisis, its causes have not been overcome.
The government has failed to fundamentally change the financial system and align it with the interests of the majority of the population.
This requires the courage to take on the big banks, hedge funds and multi-billionaires.
We want to free society and democracy from the stranglehold of financial corporations:
Billions flow into the financial markets from funded pension schemes.
We want to reverse pension privatization and withdraw the funds from speculation (see chapter on "Pensions").
It is precisely the highly complex financial instruments (for example, higher-grade derivatives) that pose the greatest risks in the event of a crisis that are of little benefit to the community.
DIE LINKE therefore wants to return the financial sector to a service function for society and the real economy.
The financial markets are to be decelerated and shrunk in volume.
If ever larger parts of public services are organized privately, then returns must be generated, and the financial market takes control.
We want to delist hospital, care and real estate groups.
DIE LINKE wants to concentrate the financial sector on socially useful core tasks.
These are primarily offerings in the area of payment transactions and secure savings, as well as the financing of private and public investments.
Banks should be returned to a business model that is geared towards the needs of the real economy and society:
Savings banks and cooperative banks form the basis of a new financial sector.
We want to promote them.
Like savings banks, commercial banks must be committed to the common good.
The majority of the banks' so-called capital market business is driven by speculative motives.
They do not serve the needs of the real economy or the majority of the population.
Short-term investment banking - investing only in businesses to generate high returns quickly - is something we want to wind down as a business area.
Shadow banks, off-balance sheet special purpose vehicles, derivatives, hedge funds and private equity companies must be broken up or strictly regulated.
In this sense, banking must become boring again.
We want to ban speculation with agricultural commodities and foodstuffs.
With democratic control of the banks by representatives of employees, trade unions and the public sector, the banks' resources could be used to steer the economy in the interests of the majority of the population.
This is the only way to protect the deposits of small savers
and to provide businesses with favorable loans.
Social organizations, consumer protection and environmental associations, and other civil society actors must also be represented in the monitoring bodies.
All people must have a legal right to a free checking account.
We want to limit overdraft interest rates to a maximum of 5 percent above the central bank rate.
Stop financial crime!
Germany is a paradise for financial crime and money laundering.
The big private auditing and consulting firms are too powerful - as the Wirecard scandal shows.
In the so-called Cum/Ex and CumCum transactions, criminal traders in the financial market had the state reimburse them for taxes that were never paid.
A network of banks, consultants, lawyers and investors thus enriched themselves at the expense of the general public.
The damage in the last twenty years is estimated at over 35 billion euros.
Preventing Cum/Ex and Cum-Cum transactions: Tax fraud with Cum/Ex-like share transactions must finally be effectively prevented.
Therefore, we need an automated and database-driven reconciliation between those who apply for refunds of capital gains taxes and those who have actually paid capital gains taxes.
Combat money laundering
Law enforcement must be improved.
Without a corporate criminal code, the big banks often get off lightly in state aid cases.
We need such corporate criminal law to hold large corporations accountable, not just individuals.
This requires effective sanctions and tightening of the German Banking Act to revoke the licenses of banks that repeatedly aid and abet criminal acts.
The Customs Anti-Money Laundering Unit (FIU) has failed in the fight against money laundering and does not have criminally trained personnel.
We need greater involvement of criminal investigation departments in the analysis of suspected money laundering reports.
In particular, the real estate or non-financial sectors, as well as the new fintech companies that process payments online or use crypto technology, need to be better supervised.
Ownership structures must be uncovered: The transparency register introduced in 2017 to centrally identify the owners of companies and foundations contains too many loopholes in reporting requirements and is not networked across Europe.
We need a real estate register with the true owners of real estate and land.
Reform financial supervision, strengthen financial consumer protection: Every investment of money and assets as well as every credit transaction must be recorded and placed under the supervision of the Federal Financial Supervisory Authority (BaFin) through an ongoing substantive right of examination (product supervision).
BaFin must be empowered with more staff with auditing qualifications to carry out independent audits of financial statements.
Break the power of the big auditors ("Big Four"): Auditors are no longer allowed to audit and advise at the same time.
The liability privilege of auditors and the associated liability limit of 4 million euros for stock corporations should be abolished.
We need a four-eye principle (joint audits) as well as pool financing for auditors so that the company being audited does not pay the auditors directly.
Auditors must rotate every three to five years.
Introduce a financial MOT: In the future, only those financial transactions and instruments should be permitted that also generate a macroeconomic and/or societal benefit.
Instead of permitting all financial practices that are not explicitly prohibited, as is currently the case, financial instruments will in future have to receive explicit approval from a "financial MOT" before they can be put into circulation.
Drain tax havens
Through tax havens and tax tricks, the rich and corporations deprive the general public of hundreds of billions of euros every year.
Money flows are often disguised via shell companies and other legal constructs.
We want to make that impossible.
Transnational corporations should be obliged to disclose their core data such as their value creation, turnover, profits and tax payments on a country-by-country basis.
Double taxation agreements with uncooperative states must be terminated immediately and their financial institutions' licenses in Germany must be revoked.
We want to make tax evasion unattractive by imposing a withholding tax of 50 percent on all payments flowing to non-cooperative states, on dividends, interest and royalties paid by companies.
This is also possible immediately on a national level.
The burden of proof must lie with the companies and wealthy individuals through a crediting of withholding tax only upon disclosure of all tax-relevant information.
We want to combat the shifting of corporate profits abroad: Existing tax exemptions for capital gains flowing abroad must be abolished.
We want to eliminate tax advantages for investment income earned in a low-tax country: The tax difference must be levied in Germany.
Law enforcement agencies and tax offices must be put in a position in terms of personnel, technology and legal framework to consistently pursue tax evasion as a business model.
Each tax investigator brings in about1 million euros more than he or she costs.
Banks, auditors and law firms that aid and abet tax evasion must be severely punished - up to and including the revocation of their banking or business licenses.
Following the example of the U.S. Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA), financial institutions are required to disclose tax-relevant information.
For digitization that benefits people
Digitization can open up opportunities for self-determined work and life,
for new forms of democracy that encompass everyday life, work and the economy.
However, the German government's digital strategy is a subsidy worth billions for private corporations.
The business associations are beating the drum for further "flexibilization of work," for the twelve-hour day.
They use the buzzword "digitization" to undermine workers' rights
and as an opportunity to divert funds for public services to their private accounts.
On the neoliberal path, digitization will lead to more precarious work
, deepen social division, and
surveillance technologies and growing corporate power will further erode democracy.
We want to take the shaping of digitization away from the profit interests of corporations in order to benefit prosperity for all people.
Who benefits from digitization will now be decided.
Strengthening employees and their rights
Digital technologies used in the company and digitized work processes must benefit employees.
Used correctly, you can promote work-life balance and create more freedom in choosing where you work and when you work.
This is to be contrasted with an approach in which companies invest in digital workflows to secure profit opportunities, increase work pressure and condense work.
In this logic, working in digital environments enables comprehensive performance and behavior control.
Digital platforms are used to undermine labor rights.
Our demands and goals show that this can also be done differently.
We want to reduce the full-time working hours to thirty hours per week with full pay and necessary personnel compensation.
In doing so, we support the trade unions in their struggle (see chapter on "Good Work").
The co-determination rights of works councils and staff councils must be strengthened and expanded when digital technologies and digital work processes are introduced so that works and service agreements can be made in the interests of employees.
Works councils and staff councils must have a say in staffing levels, performance requirements and training needs and be given the right of initiative.
The possibility of outsourcing to subcontractors must be strictly limited and tied to the continued validity of existing collective agreements (see chapter on "Good Work").
Above platforms employees must be entitled to full labor and co-determination rights as well as social security coverage.
This also applies to continued payment of wages in the event of illness and the employer's obligation to provide work equipment.
The concept of operation must be adapted and the employee status clarified.
Employees must have the right to work for multiple platforms simultaneously.
Trade unions need a digital right of access to workplaces, especially if they are organized via digital platforms.
We need an Employee Data Protection Act that prohibits the exploitation of personal data generated digitally in the work process as well as the monitoring of employees and imposes severe sanctions for violations.
We want to strengthen the rights of employees in mobile working (see chapter "Good Work").
Limiting the power of Internet corporations and platforms
Technological, economic and political power is extremely concentrated in the hands of a few digital corporations.
The "Big Five," Google, Amazon, Facebook, Apple and Microsoft combine enormous wealth, market and monopoly power: over $6.4 trillion (July 2020).
In the pandemic, they further increased their profits.
We need antitrust law that also has sharp teeth online: Monopolies must be broken up.
We rely on commons-based public alternatives.
This is the only way that alternative platforms have a chance of survival and can become attractive to many people.
At European level, we advocate guidelines and requirements for the unbundling of dominant monopolies.
It must not be left to the profit interests of these corporations to decide on content and access to the Internet.
Digital corporations must pay taxes in the countries in which they are economically active.
To this end, we call for stronger withholding taxation of profits at the place of sales and the restriction of deductibility of business expenses (for example, royalties) that serve the sole purpose of profit shifting.
The concept of the virtual permanent establishment must also be anchored in tax law.
We want to promote platform cooperatives and publicly operated platforms as alternatives.
By means of a platform structure law, we want to prohibit self-interest on the part of IT companies, ensure data protection, and guarantee the interoperability and portability of user data with sanctions.
All commercial services and software vendors must be required to offer import and export of all personal content in open formats.
These manufacturers must also be required to allow use on their platforms to their private accounts with their services competing offers.
Commercial software vendors must be required to support all popular and especially free operating systems and platforms to allow fair competition between operating systems and to give users the freedom to choose between operating systems.
Commercial software must also include its source code.
Platforms like Airbnb must be required to share their data with public authorities.
Competitors are to be granted access rights to data from platforms based on data monopolies.
This can be organized through trustees.
We want to replace Airbnb with a public benefit-oriented alternative for purely private home exchange (see chapter "No Profits with Rent").
We reject the use of upload filters and network blocks.
Platform operators must not be obliged to delete content without a court order,
nor may large platforms create their own parallel right without public control.
Against disinformation, we need stronger media education instead of censorship.
Expanding digital infrastructure for all
The profit-oriented mobile network operators have no interest in nationwide network expansion.
Numerous people still live in regions with poor Internet.
Grid expansion must be geared to the goal of reliable supply and the common good.
To achieve this, broadband and mobile networks must be in public hands.
We are promoting fiber-optic roll-out with investments of 10 billion euros a year throughout Germany.
Municipalities should be able to operate the networks in public ownership on a permanent basis.
All apartments are to receive fiber optic connection (FFTH).
We want a uniform mobile communications network from a single source that ensures coverage of the entire area.
A single network is less expensive than parallel networks and mitigates radiation exposure.
Competition among providers leads to unnecessary multiple structures and, in many places, no network at all.
Grid expansion and operation should therefore be carried out by the public sector.
This ensures good network quality throughout the country
and the working conditions of employees.
A federally owned company operates the public mobile communications network.
Telecommunications companies can offer their services via the public network.
DIE LINKE is committed to ensuring that everyone can use digital and other public services, regardless of their pocketbook.
Internet must be part of the basic service.
Telephone connection and internet may not be cut off (like electricity and water), not even in case of payment arrears.
The costs for this must be included in the minimum security, as well as for the terminal equipment.
Every child needs a free loaner from the school for the entire school term.
The rental devices are to be equipped with open source operating systems and free software as well as youth-friendly (cf. chapter "A school for all").
We want to create social centers in the villages that are close to people's homes, serve as meeting places and offer basic services such as a post office, bank and public Internet access.
The public sector, including public companies, should provide end-to-end encrypted communication channels via e-mail and chat that can be operated independently of providers and used in a decentralized manner.
There must always be non-digital ways of getting a ticket for the swimming pool and an appointment at the office, etc., to ensure that no one is excluded.
Digital offerings must not be used to cut staff in the public sector.
Net neutrality must be ensured by constitutional law.
Expanding digital infrastructure for all without barriers
The accelerated digitization of society and the associated growing media dependence on profit-oriented companies harbor high risks for the equal coexistence of people.
More and more people are being excluded - people with disabilities, the elderly and people - including many children and young people - from poor backgrounds.
DIE LINKE is campaigning against the growing trend to exclude people,
and instead wants to use opportunities to increase digital participation in all areas of life.
However, there are many barriers that make it difficult or even impossible for users to make full use of the Internet, digital systems and software.
In recent months in particular, a clear imbalance has become apparent in terms of ensuring everyday life, especially in terms of healthcare, participation in digital education, work, social life and political participation, as well as in terms of satisfying elementary basic needs, such as doing banking, shopping online or using cell phones.
DIE LINKE wants to increase people's digital participation opportunities in all areas of life in order to counteract the increasing exclusion of people with disabilities, the elderly, and people from poor backgrounds in particular.
This requires inclusive digital formats and the adequate provision of the necessary financial resources to ensure equal and equitable access to products and services for all.
Data security and data protection
If cars, refrigerators and electricity meters are to be digitally controlled and connected to the Internet in the future, it must be ruled out at the manufacturing stage that unauthorized persons can gain access to these systems, the users' data and control over these devices.
This particularly affects IT and IoT devices in households and small businesses.
The responsibility for data security must be guaranteed by design and must not be shifted to the users.
We must be able to trust that our online banking, our electronic medical records, our data at all offices are secure and will not fall into the wrong hands.
Providers of the technologies must effectively ensure security.
The liability of manufacturers for IT security must be extended.
We need legal requirements on product lifetimes that provide for mandatory support and security updates for this period.
By regulation, security by design and by default must be mandated.
This should be implemented at European level as a regulation for the internal market.
Safety certification must become mandatory for market access.
The purchase of information about and commissioning of security breaches in IT systems by secret services must be prohibited and stopped.
They jeopardize data security for everyone, as these security gaps are exploited not only by the state, but also by criminals.
There must be an obligation to report security breaches.
Research on IT security must be promoted more strongly and must not be criminalized.
In the area of defense against attacks on IT security, the Bundeswehr and intelligence services have no place;
instead, we will strengthen the independence of the Federal Office for Information Security (BSI) and expand its advisory and assistance services.
We oppose the EU Commission's efforts to criminalize end-to-end encryption.
The possibility of end-to-end encryption is an essential component of the fundamental right to informational self-determination.
We want to promote the development and operation of open source operating systems and applications by the state in order to enable the traceability, control and improvement of the systems.
The possibility of reviewing helps to find and fix errors, also voluntarily and not only via contracts and money flow with software companies.
The promotion of open source technologies can also be linked to the development of privacy-by-design standards.
Public agencies must be required to use open source technology to ensure full government and societal control over the technology used.
The federal government should provide money to support the maintenance of free operating systems as well.
The interests of users and employees in the protection of their data and personal rights when using digital systems must be defended against the interests of companies in developing new business models by exploiting and utilizing the largest possible volumes of data.
It must be possible to use publicly accessible offerings without the resulting data being commercially exploited, as is currently the case with tracking, profiling and personalized advertising.
Terms and conditions must be generally comprehensible and include the option to exclude further use of the data generated.
The terms and conditions must be accompanied by a simplified and accessible version.
The General Data Protection Regulation must be consolidated and extended.
Companies that violate data protection requirements must be consistently sanctioned.
This includes strengthening the data protection authorities.
It must be possible to share data between different social networks.
We want freedom of choice through interoperability and data portability between services.
This must not be at the expense of safety standards.
Contracts must be terminable in the same manner in which they were entered into.
Protect fundamental rights
DIE LINKE stands for a living democracy.
Digital technical possibilities must not be used to monitor citizens.
and used to restrict democracy.
Video surveillance in public spaces must end.
We want to ban automated facial recognition.
Instead, we need more staff in public spaces and at train stations who can provide support, information and assistance.
A camera does not prevent violence and does not provide help.
We oppose the unprovoked retention and central storage of biometric data such as photos of faces and fingerprints.
We want to reverse the corresponding storage in registers and in identity documents.
Sources Telecommunications surveillance and online searches (state Trojans) must be banned.
We want to enshrine the right to privacy, secure communications and encryption in law.
Spyware of all kinds must be banned.
Data retention of IP connections, mobile connections and locations must be banned.
We reject mandatory identification for e-mail, messenger services and the like.
The export of surveillance technology
and we want to ban the use of autonomous weapons systems and armed drones.
The storage of personal data by public authorities must also comply with proportionality and the fundamental right to informational self-determination for refugees.
The Central Register of Foreigners has become an instrument of total registration, allowing access to almost all personal data of numerous authorities.
Cell phones of protection seekers are systematically read and analyzed for asylum decisions.
This sets dangerous precedents and threatens the fundamental rights of all people.
Digital violence on the net must be legally recognized and prosecuted.
This also requires building competence in law enforcement agencies.
This is especially true of digital violence against women, children/youth, and members of minorities.
We want to revise the imprint obligation in order to secure the privacy of website operators.
The secrecy of telecommunications and the protection of stored data must also apply to young people:
Parents must not gain access to obviously protected data.
We reject apps for monitoring location, for example.
Non-commercial copying and use of copyrighted material should not be criminalized.
A modern copyright law must do justice to the new possibilities of use on the Internet and at the same time strengthen the back of the authors (cf. chapter "Culture").
No user rights need to be restricted for fair remuneration.
We will also work at the European level to ensure that everyday uses are permitted more flexibly.
ancillary copyright and database protection law are to be abolished for press publishers.
The use of so-called artificial intelligence (AI) must be regulated by law to ensure public good-oriented application.
All algorithms used for decision-making must be independently verified to be non-discriminatory.
We want ethical guidelines for the creation of algorithms.
When applying AI to personal data, democratic design options must be guaranteed,
Extensive data protection
and free formation of opinion in digital media must be guaranteed.
AI must be socially distanced,
Counteract monopolization tendencies in the economy by a few technology companies and surveillance.
On this basis, the potential and regulatory approaches of AI will be further explored and exploited.
Decisions on, for example, social benefit claims, creditworthiness or predictions of delinquency should therefore be rejected for the time being.
We want to protect whistleblowers.
Individuals and structures that make public abuses and crimes in the economy and in democratic institutions are vital for a democracy.
Regulating digital payment systems
Internet corporations are developing their own payment systems for their hardware and software products (for example, ApplePay, AmazonPay, PayPal) or are thinking about establishing their own parallel currencies (for example, Facebook's plans for the complementary currency Diem).
Digital payments enable personal profiling and inference of sensitive personal information.
That is why we want to enshrine in law the right to make cash payments below upper limits to prevent money laundering.
Digital payment must also be possible anonymously, at least for smaller amounts.
We strictly regulate data privacy in digital payment services.
We enforce a strict separation between pay and other corporate services.
Money and currency must remain part of state sovereignty; we reject creeping privatization.
Innovative financial technology companies (fintech) or their platforms must be subject with their financial services to the same rules and laws that apply today to conventional financial service providers (for example, banks and insurance companies).
Public administration democratic and digital
The digitization of public administration facilitates new participation formats for democratic decision-making,
transparent decision-making
and faster processing of citizen concerns.
However, this must not lead to an increase in dependency on external service providers and the use of external "consultants".
Instead, public administrations need sufficient competent personnel to maintain the digital systems, support citizens in their use, and ensure personal responsiveness for all concerns.
We want to develop new digital participation formats for democratic decision-making.
We want to expand the Freedom of Information Act into a transparency law.
Information created with public funds must be publicly accessible free of charge in the sense of Open Data.
In particular, data that enable democratic control, such as contracts for tax-funded contracts, plenary minutes, and documents, should be machine-readable and available for automated retrieval using open interfaces.
Data collected as part of commercial SmartCity projects must be made available to the general public free of charge.
n Free software and open data formats must be used in public administration.
This serves both data security and the protection of public and democratic capacity for action and decision-making.
Public procurement law must be adapted accordingly.
Software funded by public money must be published as free software and be available for reuse in other cities and administrations as well as by the general public.
The same should apply to publicly funded hardware and other technologies: They are publicly documented and thus also benefit other fields of application.
We want to expand public WLAN in municipalities and public buildings through Freifunk instead of through commercial providers.
Public administrations and registration offices may not disclose people's personal data to third parties without their express consent.
Supporting school and learning digitally
Digital applications can help both with creating school operations, such as organizing schedules or delivering distance learning, and with learning itself.
However, the best programs cannot and should not replace teachers, but support them and their students in their learning.
The use of educational software must therefore always be embedded in a pedagogical concept.
Health and learning psychology aspects must be taken into account.
In addition, exposure to widespread technologies is an important part of learning social agency.
However, digitization in education must not be allowed to become a gateway for corporate profit interests (cf. chapter on "Good Education").
Free teaching and learning materials must be ensured at all schools, including for digital devices.
Sufficient network infrastructure must be created in schools.
Teachers need to be trained in the use of these technologies and in data protection and data security issues.
They must be able to use and understand the technology in order to use it with students and explain it to them.
The safe use and operation of digital teaching and learning tools and digital concepts must be a mandatory part of teacher training.
It must be redesigned accordingly.
Under no circumstances should educational software be used as a substitute for a lack of teaching staff.
The use of digital technology in schools requires a higher staffing ratio for the support of the students as well as the software and devices.
Additional teachers and technical staff must be hired for this purpose.
Educational plans, teaching concepts and the use of media must be conceived from the point of view of people, learning processes and specific subjects.
Media and digital technology are teaching aids and not ends in themselves.
The question is not what you can do with the latest digital technology, but what the teacher needs in terms of media and technical support.
The learning software used must not store any personal data of the students (such as learning progress) outside the school.
All data collected must remain on the devices transparently and demonstrably for all or be stored within the school.
