No forecasts of learning success or further academic development may be made from the data stored by learning software used.
Data storage must be data protection-compliant and decentralized.
Students also have a "right to be forgotten," especially since they are minors and adolescents.
We oppose the collection of biometric data from learners and AI-based prediction systems that predict learning outcomes.
Dependence on specific IT companies and products must be avoided from the outset.
The software used shall comply with the standards of open source free software.
Learning programs must be created, managed, and maintained publicly.
So-called Open Educational Resources (OER), i.e. free teaching and learning materials with an open license, are always preferable.
Technology assessment in educational research must be promoted in order to reveal experiences, opportunities and risks in learning with digital technologies.
The media and data protection skills of children and young people must be promoted as early as possible.
Digital skills development must also be promoted in adult education.
Digital education should primarily take place via free educational materials (OER), which can be jointly developed, shared and reused.
This includes Open Hardware.
In science, we want to enforce open access for research results as standard.
What has been funded with public money must be available to the public free of charge.
Digitization in healthcare
We reject the use of digital applications and methods for the mere purpose of reducing costs while accepting a deterioration in medical care.
The focus must be on meaningful digitization that relieves the burden on caregivers.
Government money should first go toward combating the nursing shortage and improving the healthcare infrastructure instead of using it to subsidize IT corporations.
We reject the idea of passing on the costs of digital applications to the residents of care facilities.
Only a radical change of direction in the financing of health and care through full long-term care insurance will prevent digitization from being used to cut jobs.
Health insurance companies must not use the reserves paid in by insured persons to speculate on the success of IT corporations!
For e-health applications, we need evidence-based evaluation procedures analogous to other medical treatment methods.
Routine data from health insurance companies, registry data, or other data that accrue directly in everyday treatment (real world data) are not suitable for this purpose.
Health apps need certification according to government standards.
The informational self-determination of patients and insured persons must be preserved at all times.
The disclosure of sensitive data may only take place if consent has been obtained in accordance with the GDPR.
Data collected with the electronic health card must not be stored centrally or misused for commercial purposes.
Permission to view third parties must be available in accordance with the GDPR.
Digital health technologies should be designed to be barrier-free and accessible to all people without discrimination;
this goes hand in hand with appropriate further training and information opportunities for the insured, patients and healthcare providers.
The say of the affected people with care needs, including a right of veto for the use of robots, for example, must be defined.
Opportunities for online consultations, especially in rural areas, should be expanded as a complementary service.
Improving public transport for all through digitization
The automotive and IT groups are in the process of tapping into new sources of profit with digital mobility offerings.
They want to define their services as part of public transport and divert funds for public transport to their coffers.
In this context, public transport can be made more attractive through digital traffic control.
The overview and bookability of all transport offers in one app are overdue.
The use of shared small vehicles (ridesharing) can be a useful addition to public transportation.
Real climate protection in transport cannot be achieved with digital car fleets.
The decisive factor is the will to make public mobility available to all and to finance it from tax revenues in such a way that it does not depend on the individual's wallet whether ecological alternatives are affordable.
And that municipalities do not have to resort to profit-oriented offers from corporations due to empty coffers.
We advocate for a public mobility platform on which all offers from all transport associations are visible and bookable.
In perspective, this platform must include all European regions.
The resulting data may only be made public in aggregated form.
Under no circumstances may anonymized user data be made public, as anonymized movement profiles also allow conclusions to be drawn about specific individuals.
The obligation to provide aggregated traffic data naturally also affects all private providers of transport services.
Accessibility to all transport services must remain possible even without a smartphone or app, so as not to exclude people who cannot or do not want to use smartphones and computers.
Children and people with disabilities can also board streetcars and buses running at regular times independently.
This must also be preserved in a digitalized world of transport.
We reject pricing systems that charge for public transport according to the number of kilometers traveled and the time of day.
They allow for-profit and (partially) private providers to make higher profits, but make it more expensive for most people to use.
The so-called last mile must also be included in the public transport ticket.
Ticket prices must fall, and in the long term they must be free of charge for everyone.
When inviting tenders or awarding public transport contracts to private providers, it is mandatory to comply with applicable collective agreements in order to ensure good working conditions.
DIE LINKE supports nationwide collective agreements for local public transport.
Insofar as self-driving vehicles are used, it is mandatory to ensure that they are accompanied by human personnel who can provide immediate assistance in emergency situations and help people with disabilities to board and exit the vehicle.
We also finally need staff back at all stations.
Cameras and information columns do not provide support and protection in emergencies!
Sustainable digitization: ecological and social
The environmental costs of new applications must be weighed against the societal benefits.
Digitization requires high energy and resource consumption for data centers and end devices.
This applies to both the electricity required and the raw materials needed.
In addition, working conditions in many countries are often poor in the mining of raw materials, in the manufacture of devices and also in IT service.
While many new technologies are energy efficient, the savings are eaten up by larger terminals, higher resolution, heavier usage, and shorter equipment life.
This "rebound effect" significantly increases both raw material requirements and electricity consumption.
If this increasing electricity consumption is to be generated ecologically so as not to further damage the climate, all the more wind turbines, solar fields and hydroelectric power plants will have to be built - which in turn consume land, materials, rare metals and energy for their production.
An increasing demand for raw materials coming from other countries also increases the danger of war in a capitalist world.
DIE LINKE is therefore committed to a social discussion about the areas in which we want to use digital applications,
and where this is in the interests of environmental protection,
the protection of working
and human rights
and within the framework of an internationally fair trade policy.
Strict socio-ecological requirements must apply to public procurement with regard to labor and environmental protection in the manufacturing countries, durability and reparability.
Companies that violate their due diligence obligations in the supply chain must be excluded from public contracts and foreign trade promotion (see section "Supply Chain Act" in the chapter "Globally fair").
For digital devices, we need legal requirements for minimum service life, energy efficiency, modular design, reparability by users and workshops, and mandatory software updates and availability of spare parts (cf. eco-design requirements in the "Consumer protection" chapter).
Manufacturers must include repair instructions.
At the latest when manufacturers end support and no longer provide security updates, the source code must be published so that others can write and provide security updates.
For batteries and electrical appliances, the introduction of a deposit system should enable the effective return of raw materials to the production cycle and recycling of the components.
Repair and reuse must take priority over recycling of materials (see chapter "Climate and environmental protection").
It is mandatory that waste heat from data centers be used for building heating (local and district heating supply).
All data centers must be included in a cadastre with an energy certificate.
We seek a ban on the energy- and resource-wasting generation of so-called cryptocurrencies.
The "top runner model" must also apply to data centers and software (cf. ecodesign requirements in the "Consumer protection" chapter).
The carbon footprint of IT products, data centers or software must be transparent and comparable.
For software programming, specifications must be made for energy-saving programming.
The principle of data economy must be effectively anchored in law.
In addition to meeting data protection requirements,
this also reduces the power consumption of digital applications.
For streaming and video-on-demand services, specifications must be made for energy-saving default settings.
For justice, self-determination and gender diversity
Money, time, recognition and power are unequally distributed between the sexes.
We no longer want to allow people to be devalued because of their gender or sexual orientation - nor do we want people to be forced to conform to a certain norm.
Every person is worth the same and "All genders are beautiful".
Left Feminism - Time for a self-determined, safe and just life
As LINKE, we stand for a feminism that goes to the roots.
First and foremost, this means distributing money, work and time fairly between the sexes.
We want a society in which everyone can live freely, safely and independently, with time for family and friends
and at the same time be able to do meaningful and well-paid work.
In this way, we counteract a retraditionalization of gender roles, according to which women bear the main responsibility for care work in families.
We want a society in which women can participate in political decision-making in the same way as men.
In which life does not revolve around wage labor alone.
Capitalism, with its concomitant devaluation of unpaid (care) work, is a significant pillar of patriarchy - and vice versa.
Since patriarchal structures cannot be finally abolished without a change of system, we are fighting not only for our short- and medium-term demands for the upgrading of women and their work, but also for the overcoming of capitalism as systematized sexism.
Redistribute (care) work and time
On average, women and queer people receive lower wages and then lower pensions.
And they have lower wealth than men (gender pay gap).
Care work, which is considered a woman's business, is systematically devalued in the capitalist economy.
Women do most of the paid and unpaid caregiving and parenting work, and they are more likely to work part-time or in lower-paying jobs.
Those who are absent for a longer period of time due to parental leave and take a back seat in their job are less likely to find a good and secure job and are less able to move up the career ladder.
This is another reason why the majority of workers in the low-wage sector are female.
Many of them have a migration history.
In East Germany, wage differentials are smaller, but overall wages are much lower - more than one in three works for low pay.
In Germany, women perform 50 percent more unpaid care work than men (gender care gap).
Accordingly, women have less time for other activities or are forced to split their time between family, job and leisure.
Not infrequently, this multiple burden ends in burnout and other illnesses.
It's not just about improving the work-life balance so that women can juggle their children and careers even faster.
We need new working time models - for everyone!
That is why we are fighting for a society in which all activities and needs come into their own and in which gainful employment does not set the pace.
DIE LINKE supports the trade unions in their struggle for a significant reduction in working hours in the direction of a new normal working relationship with a 30-hour week, which could also take the form of a four-day week, for example (see chapter on "Good Work").
This leaves everyone more time for family, for themselves and for participation in politics and society.
This also includes a limit on overtime,
a right to family-friendly shift times
and a minimum wage of 13 euros.
In particular, we want to upgrade nursing, care and service occupations, in which a particularly large number of women work, and finally pay them decently.
We are abolishing the low-wage sector so that everyone can live from their work (see chapter on "Good Work").
This benefits women in particular.
We want to fundamentally restructure our economy.
It should not only be more sustainable
and more democratic,
but care work must be placed at the center.
Because the fact that nurses or geriatric nurses, educators or employees in household-related services often work poorly paid and under miserable conditions is systematic.
We need not only better paid nurses and educators, but also more of them!
100,000 nurses are needed in each of the hospitals and old people's homes, so that the nurses finally have time again for the people they care for.
We can finance this through solidarity-based health insurance and solidarity-based comprehensive long-term care insurance.
We will abolish flat-rate payments per case
and return hospitals and nursing homes to non-profit ownership, away from the market and profiteering (see chapter "Stop the nursing crisis! System change in health and care").
We want to expand child daycare nationwide, improve quality and hire more educators.
And of course, educators must be well paid so that the profession is attractive to many.
Because only with comprehensive all-day care will parents not have to choose between caring for their children and their careers (see the chapter on "Good Education").
With dignified wages for all, we will also finally put an end to the undignified pensions on which many women in particular have to live.
The improved recognition of child-rearing and care periods also means that unpaid care work is valued accordingly (cf. chapter on "Good pensions").
There are currently no real wage replacement benefits for family carers who are still working.
We want six weeks' leave with full, employer-financed wage compensation (cf. chapter "Stop the nursing crisis!") and regardless of the degree of relationship.
A majority of women are employed in the retail or cleaning sectors and are particularly often trapped in precarious employment.
We are calling for the abolition of fixed-term contracts and the transformation of mini-jobs into fully socially secure employment relationships.
We want to put an end to involuntary part-time work: All employees must have a legal right to a full-time position.
We want equal pay for equal work and work of equal value!
To this end, we will introduce a binding Equal Pay Act, including the right to take legal action by associations, so that women no longer have to go to court alone.
Private companies, too, must no longer be allowed to evade this.
We support the trade unions' efforts to reach comprehensive collective agreements so that women do not get into such a situation in the first place.
Our demand to raise basic salaries in nursing by 500 euros is a contribution to upgrading this work.
In order to promote the sharing of care and work in families as partners, we want to extend the parental allowance to twelve months per parent.
The parental allowance entitlement applies individually and is not transferable to the other parent.
In addition, there needs to be additional parental protection of ten days paid time off for the second parent after the birth of the child.
Women are less often represented in leadership positions in business, science and politics.
That has to change.
That is why we are calling for a 50 percent quota for women in management positions and greater sharing of management tasks and positions through job sharing or other working models (in contrast to the 30 percent quota of the grand coalition).
Social power relations are also reflected in sex work.
The Left Party is discussing different ways of dealing with prostitution politically.
We are united in rejecting the criminalization and stigmatization of sex workers.
There is a need to strengthen self-organization, voluntary counseling, retraining, and continuing education, adequate health care, and the social rights of sex workers as a whole, who face many disadvantages even as self-employed workers.
We also demand an entitlement to social benefits and socially insured employment, as well as inclusion in a solidarity-based employment insurance scheme.
Never cut back on life - no cuts at the expense of women and families
Privatization and cutback measures particularly affect education, care, social work and education.
Women suffer doubly from this: as employees and as unpaid care workers in the families, where they have to absorb the cuts through extra work.
This leads to additional workload and reinforces old role models.
The multi-billion dollar rescue packages for companies in the Corona crisis must not be absorbed by cuts in the social sector.
On the contrary, we advocate a socio-ecological system change that strengthens those areas in the economy and employment that are climate-friendly and make life better for everyone: personal services, education, training, an expansion of rail and public transport.
Our restructuring of the economy and the welfare state will make our society crisis-proof in the future and promote the life opportunities (not only) of women:
We are abolishing the debt brake.
Instead, we promote investment in the expansion of social services in public hands, beyond the market and profit.
We will raise the necessary funds for this by reintroducing the wealth tax (cf. the chapter on "Changing course with taxes").
Women, single parents and children benefit most from good and free social infrastructures - and people with low incomes.
Social and budgetary policies must be examined for gender equity and changed accordingly in the sense of gender budgeting.
End violence against women
We want every person - regardless of gender, sexual orientation, and lifestyle - to be able to live without fear of violence.
The state must ensure this through the Basic Law and through international agreements, but it does not do so sufficiently.
Violence against women is an expression and consequence of a social devaluation and oppression of women, of hierarchical and patriarchal gender relations.
It takes many forms and occurs in families as well as in public spaces.
Violence against women does not depend on social status; it exists in the digital world as in analog life.
Far too often, it ends fatally for women.
Every third day in Germany, a woman is killed by her partner or ex-partner.
To dismiss this violence as an "escalated relationship dispute" or a private matter misses the structural problem: murdering women because they are women is what we call femicide.
To effectively protect women from violence, we need social conditions in which women can live independently and in a self-determined manner - this also includes economic independence.
When women experience violence, they need rapid and needs-based protection and qualified help in women's shelters and other shelters.
Counseling centers must be easily accessible - regardless of physical impairment, residency status, or the living situation of those affected.
We want to change patriarchal structures; this is the only way to sustainably prevent violence against women:
The Istanbul Convention, the Council of Europe Convention on Preventing and Combating Violence against Women and Domestic Violence, must be implemented consistently and in full.
We want to reverse the restrictions made by the federal government during ratification so that numerous refugee or migrant women are not denied access to protection.
We want to expand violence protection structures and support systems and provide them with sufficient financial resources.
The financing of women's shelters and specialized counseling centers must no longer be a voluntary service.
What we need here is a nationwide flat-rate financing scheme in which the federal government participates.
Violence against the mother massively endangers the child's well-being and can be life-threatening for mothers and children.
When making decisions on custody and access rights, protection against violence must have top priority.
State authorities such as the police, courts and offices, as well as medical staff, must be sensitized to gender-based violence - including in digital form.
Explicit alternative (first) points of contact to the police in the form of non-governmental organizations must be created and financed, to which those affected can turn.
Refugee women often experience sexualized violence, not only in their country of origin and during their flight, but also in their country of refuge.
In the case of domestic violence, the right of residence previously dependent on the husband must be revoked and converted into an independent residence permit.
Mass shelters are also places that foster violence against women and must be dismantled.
On the run, after rejection and pushbacks at the European border and in the camps, women are often exposed to massive sexual violence and rape.
An open, solidary and humane refugee policy is the only effective measure against systematic violence against women.
It must be fought that human trafficking for the purpose of sexual exploitation and human trafficking for the purpose of labor exploitation must be fought without criminalizing and stigmatizing those affected!
As long as those affected do not receive secure and independent residence status, the perpetrators are protected by the victims' fear.
Residence permits, protection and compensation must be granted regardless of the victim's willingness to testify as a witness in criminal proceedings.
For those affected, we demand therapeutic resources, medical as well as psychological care, legal assistance and legal aid, access to social services and educational opportunities.
All forms of violence and glorification of violence against women, children and LGBTIQA* (lesbian, gay, bisexual, trans*, intersex, queer and asexual persons) must be consistently punished.
Public film funding needs a gender quota and the establishment of an effective as well as independent control outside the German Advertising Council to stop sexist advertising.
Women must have access to social positions without having lifestyles imposed on them.
Both the ban on headscarves and the obligation to wear them would be a restriction on women's opportunities for development.
It is important not to patronize women in their personal decisions about how they dress and not to exert any pressure on them - either in one direction or the other.
Our feminism: solidary and international
In Brazil and Poland, India and Nigeria, Germany and Ireland, women are taking to the streets for their rights.
They denounce violence against women,
they fight for their right to abortion
and against racism.
They are united by the common experience of sexist structures and violence - and they unite in the fight against it: on the net, on the street, in everyday life at work, in court, at home, in the travails of the plains.
Women and children worldwide are particularly affected by climate change and make up the majority of people fleeing their homes.
But they are not only victims, they are also important climate policy actors and fight against the exploitation of people and nature.
LEFT feminism is always concretely on the ground
and at the same time aware of international responsibility and solidarity
In economic and political decisions, values such as care, sustainability and health must be central.
We call for the use of civil measures of violence prevention and conflict resolution.
German foreign, development and human rights policy must be peace policy
and gender equality worldwide.
UN Resolution 1.325 "Women, Peace and Security" must be implemented - neither women's participation in peace processes nor in conflicts must be sidelined.
The conditions in the accommodations for refugees are inhumane.
We demand functioning and lockable sanitary facilities, protected zones and good health and food supplies.
A gender-responsive climate policy must take into account women's particular vulnerability to climate catastrophe.
n We want to make International Women's Day on March 8 a national holiday to commemorate women's struggles around the world in a wide variety of places and circumstances and to honor their common fight to overcome devaluation, exclusion and violence - Berlin has led the way.
Reproductive justice: Free choice for a life with and without children for all
In order to live self-determined lives, women and queer people must have real choices.
We want all people to be able to decide whether and how they want to live with children.
Only then can we achieve reproductive, physical and sexual self-determination for women and queer people.
This includes comprehensive information, access to contraceptives and the free decision to terminate a pregnancy.
Only when women can decide for or against pregnancy and parenthood without constraints is self-determined family planning possible.
But a life with children must also be socially secured:
This begins with good health care and education during pregnancy and birth.
Living with children should not be a risk of poverty.
Parents and single parents must be able to raise children in safe and healthy conditions (see chapter "Supporting families where they need it").
We want legal access to abortion for women, trans* and non-binary people.
We want to delete sections 218 to 219 b of the German Criminal Code (StGB).
Ongoing proceedings under 219 a must be discontinued immediately.
Public hospitals must ensure in their planning that abortions are performed.
Abortions are part of health care and, like other medical services, must be regulated.
The necessary technical training for this must become part of medical school.
All contraceptive methods must be paid for by all health insurance companies without exception.
Funding must be made available for research into new contraceptive methods to develop additional methods for men as well and to make contraceptive methods more tolerable for all.
Menstrual hygiene products must be provided free of charge by public health agencies and in public facilities.
Artificial insemination must be available to all people free of charge through health insurance coverage, including non-married, lesbian, single, trans* and queer people.
Women with disabilities have a right to reproductive self-determination and parenthood.
This includes the right to preserve and promote their fertility, as well as access to support services, for example, assistance to parenthood, and barrier-free access to comprehensive, independent counseling.
In order to implement the right to parenthood, housing and support services must be made available throughout the country in the context of accompanied parenthood.
For physical and sexual self-determination and equality of all lifestyles
We want diverse lifestyles to be treated equally under the law.
In the future, special protection and support from the state and society should not be reserved for married couples, but should benefit those who live with children or those in need of care - regardless of their sexual orientation and gender identity.
We want equal rights for all lifestyles where responsibility is taken for others.
We call for an elective kinship law in which not only (heterosexual) couples are allowed to take responsibility for each other, but any community that feels connected to each other.
This can also be a more than two-person relationship (for example, a multi-parent family with two lesbian mothers and two gay fathers).
These people should be granted extensive visiting rights in the event of illness, adoption rights and the right to refuse to testify.
At the same time, special allowances are due if a relative needs to be cared for (in accordance with elective kinship law) or if there are children in an elective kinship.
We want to reform the law of descent in such a way that existing disadvantages of lesbian and gay marriages and partnerships compared to heterosexual marriages and partnerships are eliminated.
This includes legal recognition of co-parenting as well as trans*, intersex, and non-binary parents.
This must also apply retroactively.
We will replace the marital splitting system with family- and gender-sensitive tax models and a freely transferable subsistence minimum (see chapter on "Changing taxes").
School curricula must comprehensively reflect the real diversity of lifestyles and gender and sexual identities.
Sexual health education initiatives in schools, workplaces, society, and queer scenes need to be strengthened.
The evaluation of different lifestyles in school lessons must be dispensed with.
Legal guardians must not be offered the option of excluding their children from sex education classes.
Offensive and Social for LGBTIQA*
The rights of lesbian, gay, bisexual, trans*, intersex, queer and asexual people (LGBTIQA*) are non-negotiable for us.
We want LGBTIQA* to be recognized as a natural part of social reality as we age.
That's why we want more queer education opportunities in all areas of society.
We advocate for discrimination-free language that does justice to the diversity of gender and sexual identities.
Strengthening queer communities: bailout against Corona consequences
Corona also hit the facilities and structures of queer communities: Many association spaces, clubs, bars and cafés had to close.
In times of empty coffers, queer projects are the first to be cut.
We want to prevent that.
We call for a queer bailout to protect community structures and institutions.
In the allocation of public funding, we want to reduce structural discrimination against lesbian, trans* and inter* initiatives and projects: Lesbian and gay projects should be funded to the same extent.
Lesbian communities should become more visible!
We want to build queer structures especially in rural regions and smaller cities.
Against poverty and social exclusion
One in three queer people in Europe struggles to make ends meet financially.
For intersex and trans* persons, the situation is even more precarious.
Queer youth often experience homelessness after coming out.
We want sanctuary and housing for young queer people at risk of homelessness.
Outreach youth work and homeless assistance must keep the specific (emergency) situations of LGBTIQA* in mind.
We want to eliminate structural exclusions and problems of lesbians (for example, lack of visibility, poverty among the elderly).
The same applies to the structural exclusions and problems of trans* and inter* persons.
For queer people we want more offers for self-determined living in old age with appropriate care and support options.
Above all, non-commercial public service and alternative housing and house projects such as multi-generation houses or housing cooperatives are to be promoted.
Fight discrimination
The fight against LGBTIQA* hostility is a task for society as a whole.
We therefore want a National Action Plan against LGBTIQA* hostility and for the acceptance of sexual and gender diversity.
To research intersectional forms of discrimination and gender-based violence against LGBTIQA*, we want to publicly commission and fund studies.
Discrimination and violent attacks continue to be part of everyday life for queer people.
Official crime statistics reflect only a fraction of this.
DIE LINKE is committed to providing comprehensive support for prevention projects and organizations that work to help victims of violence.
Prosecution of queer-hostile violence must be more vigorously pursued and punished than it has been in the past.
Hate crimes against queer people, communities or their supporters must be recorded and prosecuted nationwide.
The self-help and educational projects of LGBTIQA* communities must be supported and promoted in order to increase social acceptance.
Queer people still experience discrimination in the workplace.
Trans* people are disproportionately affected by unemployment.
People with HIV also experience discrimination at work.
The structural exclusions are intensified for people who experience multiple discrimination, such as racism or hostility towards people with disabilities.
The Federal Anti-Discrimination Agency is to be funded in such a way that it can provide counseling services in a target group-oriented, multilingual and barrier-free manner in the world of work.
We want to strengthen discrimination protections for trans* and intersex people.
An important key in the fight against discrimination in the workplace is employee self-organization.
We want more queer educational opportunities that provide impetus for self-organization in the world of work.
Initiatives that promote an open workplace free of fear and discrimination in workplaces must be encouraged.
The blood donor guideline must be adapted to the state of science.
Exclusion criteria and periods that discriminate against gay and bisexual men and trans* persons must be abolished or shortened accordingly.
We want to include protection against discrimination based on gender identity, sexual orientation and lifestyle in Article 3 of the Basic Law.
In order to guarantee this extended fundamental right, anti-discrimination bodies and a right of action for associations in the General Equal Treatment Act (AGG) are needed.
Self-determination for trans*and intersex people
We want self-determined gender registration for all.
A change of first name and civil status must be possible with a simple declaration at the registry office - without the previous compulsory consultations, expert opinions, medical certificates and court proceedings.
The Transsexual Act (TSG) pathologizes.
We want to abolish it and replace it with a right of self-determination.
The externally determined operations on trans* persons and intersex people due to the legal obligation of surgery and sterilization in the TSG in the years 1981 to 2011 must be historically reviewed.
The people affected by this must be adequately compensated.
We want to set up a compensation fund.
We want to strengthen the rights of trans* and intersex children and youth.
The right to physical integrity is a fundamental and human right.
We prohibit all medically unnecessary interventions on the internal or external sexual characteristics of children.
This includes recognition of their self-designated gender.
We advocate for gender-neutral restrooms and washrooms, especially in public buildings, to reduce discrimination based on gender identity.
Trans* persons need free access to all necessary medical services (medical therapies, psychotherapy, if desired operations) and the assumption of the costs incurred for this by the health insurance companies - even if they have no health insurance and regardless of the current residence status.
Conversion treatments must be completely banned, including on adults.
In the future, guardians or legal guardians must be able to be legally prosecuted if they nevertheless accept or arrange conversion treatments.
We advocate for queer health centers focused on trans* and inter* even in small towns and rural areas.
The rights and special concerns of trans* and intersex persons must also be protected in the penal system and during police searches.
Safeguard and empower queer refugees!
People who flee to Germany are confronted with many difficulties.
The Covid 19 pandemic has further restricted the right to asylum and exacerbated the precarious situation of many refugees.
The requirement for physical distance in times of pandemic turns out to be particularly problematic for mass shelters.
The even greater isolation puts the mental health of many refugees at risk (see chapter "Solidary Immigration Society").
We demand decentralized accommodation for queer refugees (as for refugees as a whole), access to the internet, the right to barrier-free health care regardless of residence status, and the expansion of specific networking and support services for queer refugees.
Queer people who are persecuted must be granted unrestricted asylum or protection.
They must not be deported - not even to so-called safe countries of origin.
We want to establish specialized centers for LGBTIQA* refugees nationwide.
There, queer refugees can get advice on the asylum procedure as well as on residence and migration law.
There is also a need for opportunities for psychological counseling for LGBTIQA* refugees.
Self-determined living in an inclusive and barrier-free society
We want a country in which all people live together on an equal footing and participate in democratic decision-making - regardless of their individual abilities, physical condition, origin and social status, gender, age or sexual orientation.
An inclusive society in which no one is excluded.
The reality is different.
Approximately16 percent of the population lives with recognized disabilities and chronic conditions.
Due to a variety of barriers in everyday life - for example, in transportation, workplaces, educational institutions, medical practices, government offices or in the digital realm - participation is only possible to a limited extent for them.
The general labor market is still not barrier-free and inclusive more than ten years after ratification of the UN Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities (UN CRPD).
On the contrary, those affected are threatened with a poverty spiral.
People with disabilities and chronic illness are disproportionately unemployed, dependent on welfare, and institutionalized.
DIE LINKE advocates the full and effective participation of all people, including those with disabilities.
The basic prerequisite for this is accessibility - in terms of construction, communication and structure.
Accessibility benefits everyone.
It must therefore be a binding obligation for both the public and private sectors.
We understand inclusion as a process to reduce social inequalities.
It refers to all those people who are excluded from participation and pushed to the margins of society: People with disabilities, the elderly, refugees, Sinti*zze and Rom*nja, linguistic and cultural minorities, people with other faiths and sexual orientation and many more.
Inclusion gives all people the opportunity not only to be part of political, social and cultural life, but also to actively shape it in a self-determined way.
Policies for people with disabilities and chronic illnesses must be designed as a human rights task - the United Nations Convention makes clear stipulations here.
These are also binding for Germany and must be implemented.
Human rights must not be subject to cost.
That is why we want to anchor self-determination as the most important principle in disability policy and make it enforceable.
People with disabilities and chronic illness have a right to self-realization.
Barriers must be broken down - also in people's minds and in the digital world.
Accessibility is the basis for equal participation and promotes solidarity-based cohesion.
We want a guaranteed right to personal assistance in all areas of life for a self-determined life in work, education, housing, leisure, family and parenthood as well as in voluntary work.
It must also be possible for those who do not organize their personal assistance/support staff themselves via the employer model to take the personal assistants with them during a necessary stay in the hospital and in preventive care and rehabilitation facilities.
We want to improve the working conditions of the assistance and support staff.
Their work should be paid according to collective agreements, even if they are employed directly by the assistance recipients in the so-called employer model.
For this to work, municipal payers must be required to refinance collectively agreed wages.
Collectively agreed wages are to be at least at the level of the collective agreements for the public sector.
In addition, a tariff loyalty regulation is to apply to public contracts.
We want to provide the approximately 500 counseling centers of the supplementary independent participation counseling (EUTB) nationwide with the financial and personnel resources they need to offer their counseling services on a long-term basis and without barriers.
We want to pay the employees working there according to the collective wage agreement.
In particular, people with disabilities and chronic illnesses are to be employed as consultants subject to social insurance contributions.
The application procedures for the approval of funds must be simplified.
Health and nursing care must be provided close to the patient's home and made a mandatory municipal task.
Good work and income from which one can live must also be promoted more strongly for people with disabilities in an inclusive labor market.
This includes employees in workshops!
People with disabilities are disproportionately affected by unemployment: Because there are too many barriers and because of other discrimination.
We need an inclusive labor market.
The statutory employment obligation of companies must be raised again to six percent and implemented consistently - subject to sanctions.
Initiatives to reduce long-term unemployment must specifically include people with disabilities.
Special consideration should be given to women with disabilities.
We want to significantly increase the compensatory levy.
All regulations should be eliminated that allow companies to reduce the payment of the equalization levy and thus effectively nullify the employment obligation.
We ensure that the funds from the equalization levy are only used to create and secure inclusive conditions in the general labor market and not for institutional funding.
We want to promote and expand inclusive companies with employment subject to social security contributions for people with disabilities and chronic illnesses to a much greater extent.
We want to make special work environments (workshops for people with disabilities) obsolete step by step - with the help of immediately enforceable exit strategies and timetables as well as incentives for employment with public and private employers in the general labor market.
In doing so, we want to ensure that people with disabilities do not experience any reduction in their social protection or retirement benefits, which are currently linked to workshops for people with disabilities.
We consider the immediate introduction of the collectively agreed or statutory minimum wage to be an intermediate step for employees of workshops for the disabled.
In order to implement these demands, we want to align the rights of the representatives of severely disabled persons and the workshop councils with the rights of the works and staff councils.
People with disabilities must be provided with work assistance for their political work.
The activities of the women's representatives and the workshop councils must be financed and secured to meet demand.
Public investments and subsidies must be tied to the criterion of accessibility, including in doctors' offices, medical facilities and renovation measures.
The private sector must also enable comprehensive accessibility.
To this end, we want to include binding and effective regulations in the General Equal Treatment Act (AGG) and in the Disability Equality Act (BGG), as well as in all laws that oblige private providers of publicly accessible goods and services to create accessibility in accordance with the UNCRPD.
We want to introduce a right of action for associations so that anti-discrimination associations can sue.
In the future, housing construction will be subject to a fundamental requirement of barrier-free accessibility.
An investment offensive is needed to implement social, non-profit housing construction with barrier-free apartments and inclusive housing options - including in existing buildings.
Landlords must no longer be able to refuse consent to a handicapped-accessible conversion of their apartment.
Urban development funding must be directed towards the development of inclusive and comprehensively barrier-free living spaces and urban quarters in which an equal coexistence of all people with and without disabilities, oriented towards the social space, is achieved: a universal design (design for all or benefit-for-all concept) in accordance with Article 2 of the United Nations Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities.
One school for all!
We want inclusive education and upbringing of children and adolescents with and without disabilities in all phases of development with appropriate qualification of staff and sufficient staff and material resources in the facilities (see chapter "Good education").
All laws and regulations must be reviewed to determine whether they comply with the UN CRPD and, if necessary, amended accordingly.
The position of people with severe so-called mental and multiple disabilities, mental impairment and chronic illness should also be improved.
A Federal Participation Act that conforms to human rights and does not provide for cost reservations, income and asset imputations and reasonableness tests, thus creating real equality of opportunity.
We want participation benefits for people with disabilities and chronic illnesses to cover needs and to be financed independently of income and assets in all areas of life according to uniform nationwide criteria and through federal funds.
We also want to introduce a participation allowance.
An immigration society based on solidarity
Immigration is not a threat, but everyday life for many, a component of our society and the right of every individual.
Germany is home to people from a wide variety of places, with different histories and more diverse than ever before.
We live, love and work together.
We will not join in when employees and pensioners in Germany are played off against people fleeing poverty, oppression, the consequences of the climate catastrophe and war.
If wealth were distributed more equitably, there would be enough for good living, housing and working - for everyone.
The economy is often based on the exploitation and poor working conditions of migrants with often precarious residence status and sometimes limited health care, for example in slaughterhouses, asparagus fields and in care.
People with a migration history are even more frequently affected by poverty, exclusion and unemployment after generations.
Their children are systematically disadvantaged in the education system, and those with a migrant-sounding last name are more likely to have problems finding housing and jobs.
These legal and social discriminations must be dismantled.
But instead, the German government continues to rely on deterrence, division and isolation.
The result: growing racism in society and state institutions such as the police, where extreme right-wing networks (cue NSU 2.0!) are up to mischief.
And again and again right-wing terror.
Our Agenda against Racism: Social Offensive and Equal Rights for All
To overcome racism and discrimination, a just distribution of rights, wealth and resources is needed.
We want participation instead of integration.
Because democracy requires participation in everyday life.
We want all people who live here to be equal legally, politically and socially as part of a participation agenda.
Together with numerous movements and anti-racist initiatives like Seebrücke, Aufstehen gegen Rassismus and Black Lives Matter, we stand #indivisible against social division, racism and right-wing agitation.
For us, anti-racism is much more than symbolic politics.
Investment is needed in cohesion and participation rather than exclusion and compartmentalization.
And equal rights for all.
Our goal is a fundamental policy change - towards global freedom of movement,
equal rights for all and
an immigration society based on solidarity.
We oppose everyday racism and structural racism in state and society.
DIE LINKE stands for open borders for all people in a Europe of solidarity that does not seal itself off.
We fight for safe escape routes and a society that realizes human rights - instead of building walls and adapting basic rights to the current budgetary and mood situation.
Residence and work permits are needed regardless of the length of employment and employer
, as well as nationwide controls to enforce the minimum wage of 13 euros for all people (see chapter "Work").
To counter a possible shortage of skilled workers, there is no need for the targeted poaching of qualified people abroad, but for decent training, working conditions and pay for all people in this country.
There needs to be better recognition of the qualifications and degrees of non-EU citizens so that they can continue to practice their professions.
We oppose the restriction of social security for migrants from EU countries and other states by the federal government.
Health protection must not be restricted: There needs to be a nationwide hardship fund and an anonymous health insurance voucher for the treatment of people without coverage; we want to abolish exceptions to compulsory insurance (see the chapter on "Health").
There should be a legal entitlement to interpreter services within the framework of medical services.
Inclusion, participation and accessibility must also no longer be a question of the residence title.
We want the right to vote and stand for election at all levels for all people with a migration history who live in Germany for the long term, so that they can help shape society on an equal footing.
All children and adolescents born here whose parents live permanently in the country should be granted German citizenship and have a right to multiple citizenship - without having to renounce the citizenship of their parents.
Migrants should have a legal right to naturalization after five years of residence in the Federal Republic.
We demand legalization possibilities for people without residence status and effective right to stay regulations for people who have to live in an uncertain residence status or with chain toleration.
For them, we want to create safe access to education, health and labor protection against exploitation.
We reject deportations, especially to war, persecution and misery or as a form of double punishment
- in contrast to all other parties represented in the Bundestag.
We have always voted against it here and will continue to do so in the future.
Anti-racism into law: A clear working definition of institutional and structural racism is needed, as in Thuringia.
We also call for a fundamental reform of the General Equal Treatment Act (AGG) and a right of action for associations.
There is a need for protection against discrimination that also includes state action.
We call for a Federal Anti-Discrimination Act (FADA) to protect against discrimination by government agencies.
There needs to be an anti-racism officer with real powers.
There is a need for institutionalized support and counseling structures for people with experiences of racism that are low-threshold and appropriate.
These structures are to be financed on a regular basis throughout the country.
DIE LINKE demands that a protection and promotion clause against racist discrimination be included in Article 3 of the Basic Law.
Racism and esprit de corps in the authorities must finally be addressed!
This requires organizational development in the administration that is sensitive to discrimination and police reform (see chapter "Security for All").
We want a Participation Act to better include people who have experienced racism and make them more representative in society.
This includes a quota to increase the proportion of people with a migration history in public administration in line with their share of the population, and a participation council to be involved in important decisions in business, science and politics.
Here it is crucial for us that migrant self-organizations are part of the participation council and that it is represented by an equal opportunities officer.
We demand that an Enquete Commission be established to advise the Bundestag on the implementation of the demands from the NSU Committee as well as the UN Committee on Anti-Racism (ICERD).
We demand a humanitarian right to stay for victims of right-wing violence without a permanent residence status.
Victims of racism and their families must be better supported.
There needs to be an expansion of compensation for victims of racist and anti-Semitic attacks.
People who experience racism are not a security problem.
Responsibility for migration and integration must be taken away from the Federal Ministry of the Interior.
We call for a Federal Ministry for Migration and Participation.
We want to support civil society groups that work against racism, anti-Semitism, homophobia and transphobia, antiziganism, religious fundamentalism, anti-Muslim racism and for more democracy, as well as refugee councils, migrant associations, self-governing counseling services and the self-organization of migrants more strongly and finally on a permanent basis through a Democracy Promotion Act (see chapter "Against Right-Wing Violence").
Anti-racist initiatives are to receive more financial support.
Coaches, trainers and volunteers in clubs and (fan) projects who carry out participation work must be given more support.
Significantly more investment is needed in public infrastructure and social cohesion, i.e. better equipment, better working conditions and more staff in schools, daycare centers, administration, youth and cultural centers (see chapter "Investments").
We want to expand low-threshold services, especially for migrants and refugee women as well as queer refugees and migrants, and support them.
We want a fund for welcoming municipalities that ensures freedom of movement for refugees and helps welcoming municipalities and cities that show solidarity.
Municipalities that want to improve the conditions for a welcoming culture can use it to apply for funding for the care and integration of refugees.
These investment funds can then be used for public services in general.
We will launch an immediate program to train and hire additional school social workers and teachers to teach German as a second language.
The right to schooling must apply to all children nationwide and regardless of residency status, including the legal right to childcare and all-day places.
Qualifications for vocational training must be offered regardless of age.
We want to provide educational and integration opportunities regardless of residency status.
We want to provide decentralized housing for refugees throughout Germany and offer them free language courses nationwide.
Instead of discriminatory benefits in kind, we want regular cash benefits equivalent to the solidarity-based minimum income for all people.
Defending humanity: Saving people, clearing escape routes, fighting the causes of flight
German corporations export weapons all over the world, but people who flee from these weapons and the wars waged with them are to be locked out.
Many are fleeing because Western corporations are destroying their countries.
But their entry into Europe is hampered by inhumane means.
More than 20,000 people have died on their way to Europe in the past seven years, drowned in the Mediterranean, dying of thirst in the desert.
In the camps on the borders, on the ground of the EU, there is unbearable misery.
Germany is making itself politically dependent on regimes that are taking over the job of fending off refugees at Europe's external borders; at home, the extreme right is mobilizing.
But it could be done differently.
Because there is enough space and resources.
If wealth were distributed more equitably, there would be enough for everyone.
Human life and dignity must not depend on passport or residence permit.
That is why we stand up against isolation and deportations, for the right to go, to come and to stay.
And for overcoming the economic injustices and ideologies of inequality such as racism and nationalism that repeatedly become popular weapons in the competition for resources, wealth and life chances.
Stop it!
Instead of being played off against each other, let's stand together for justice:
saving people,
globalizing social justice
, and actually fighting the causes of flight - not the refugees.
Enough with the excuses: Save the people!
The EU's deportation agency Frontex must be disbanded and replaced by a civilian European sea rescue program.
We want to put existing instruments for monitoring the Mediterranean and the external borders at the service of sea rescue.
The criminalization of civil society sea rescue must end immediately.
All European "hotspots," such as the Moria slum camp and its successors, must be dismantled.
There needs to be an immediate humanitarian program to receive the people.
As long as a European solution cannot be implemented, the German government must lead the way with a coalition of the willing.
We want legal and safe ways to enter the EU.
This deprives touts of the basis for doing business.
The Geneva Refugee Convention, the UN Convention on the Rights of the Child and the European Convention on Human Rights must be respected.
In January 2021, the UN Refugee Agency denounced the practice of refoulement at Europe's borders, saying the right to asylum is in danger.
The principle of non-refoulement at the EU's external borders and on the high seas must be followed without restriction!
The refugee deal with Turkey and similar agreements or forms of cooperation with militias and dictators in states such as Libya, Egypt, Sudan and Morocco must be revoked.
Escape is not a crime!
Individual access to asylum procedures and legal protection must be ensured for asylum seekers at the EU's external borders.
Women, the sick, the elderly, children, religious and ethnic minorities, and people with disabilities and queer people are particularly vulnerable.
They must be safe from violence, misery and exploitation.
We reject fast-track procedures and detention of protection seekers (whether in so-called return, transit, controlled centers or "hotspots").
Extend and enforce the right to asylum!
We want uniform protection standards at a high level;
we want to put an end to the shifting of responsibility to other states with the help of safe third country or country of origin regulations.
Persecution on the grounds of sexual orientation and of trans* and intersex people (LGBTIQA*) must be recognized in practice as a reason for flight.
Negative competition through lowered standards of housing, care and rights must be abolished!
The German government must finally push for the EU to take action against member states that systematically disregard their human rights obligations.
We demand a nationwide independent asylum procedure counseling by welfare organizations and associations, which must be publicly financed; there
should be no blanket asylum revocation examinations; the quality of asylum examination and internal control must be significantly improved in order to effectively reduce the large number of illegal and erroneous decisions of the BAMF
There are no "economic refugees" - no one flees voluntarily!
We call for the extension of binding refugee rights to poverty, environmental and climate refugees, as well as a corresponding humanitarian visa allocation.
There is a need for comprehensive admission quotas through the UNHCR's resettlement program
and the lifting of visa requirements for those seeking protection.
The Dublin system must be overcome:
We want a European refugee apportionment to share responsibility, which is based on the wishes and interests of the refugees and takes into account existing family ties, language skills and individual circumstances.
Unequal distribution can then be compensated for by equalization payments from countries with low admission numbers;
countries, regions and cities that are willing to take in more refugees receive financial support from EU funds.
The right to family reunification must apply without restriction - also for "subsidiary" beneficiaries of protection.
Unaccompanied minor refugees must have the right to be joined by their siblings.
We demand that municipalities be allowed to decide for themselves whether to accept additional refugees beyond those allocated to them.
Municipally based boards should also be able to order hardship permits in the future.
No human being is illegal!
The right to freedom of movement must not be dependent on the chance of birthplace or economic exploitability.
DIE LINKE advocates a comprehensive liberalization of visas as well as an open and solidary immigration law that is no longer based on the criteria of origin or economic usability.
If you really want to fight the causes of flight, you must finally change the conditions that repeatedly force people to flee and make help necessary.
Instead of continuing to systematically export causes of flight such as weapons, environmental and climate destruction and poverty, we therefore want to overcome global injustices,
Democracy
and support social movements from below
and effectively help people in need (see chapter "Social justice worldwide").
Strengthen democracy
Stop right-wing terror and violence
The extreme right has long since crossed the threshold into terror.
The list of right-wing attacks from the last two years alone is long.
We especially remember the attacks in Kassel and Halle in 2019 and Hanau in 2020 with several deaths.
Right-wingers commit assassinations of migrants, people of Jewish and Muslim faith, leftists and other dissidents;
the security authorities repeatedly prove incapable of apprehending the perpetrators.
This has a terrible tradition in the Federal Republic, from the attack on the Munich Oktoberfest to the murders of the NSU.
Germany has had a frightening right-wing terrorist continuity since at least the 1980s.
The perpetrators are encouraged by a social climate in which the value of human life is questioned.
The path to bloodshed begins with agitation in everyday life.
Right-wing groups and parties try to serve people's fears and needs in the face of the consequences of neoliberal policies.
They distract from social struggles for better wages
and redistribution of social wealth and
reinterpret them into ethnic, religious and cultural conflicts,
fight gender equality and sexual diversity.
And they spread anti-Semitic conspiracy theories - especially in view of the corona pandemic.
Because the Office for the Protection of the Constitution gives priority to the protection of informants, it repeatedly obstructs police investigations and legal clarification - and even helps to build up extreme right-wing structures.
Education and resistance against the right is done by others: Most of the time, it is volunteer-organized civil society projects and antifa initiatives that do educational work, make solidarity a practical experience, and go where it hurts.
For this, conservatives call them "nest-destroyers," they are deprived of public funds, and they are criminalized as "left-wing extremists."
The AfD is attempting to undermine unpopular associations and civil society actors.
and even state centers for political education.
Conservatives call for restricting fundamental rights
and (even) more powers for security agencies.
Obviously, however, there is no deficit of information, equipment and authority there - but there is an attitude problem.
DIE LINKE is standing up to it - on the streets, in the workplaces, in the parliaments.
Together with broad alliances, we block Nazi marches and fight against right-wing attacks and for the social ostracism of right-wing ideas.
We oppose every form of misanthropy, whether from the right-wing fringe or from the supposedly respectable center of society.
Civil disobedience is part of democratic protest and must not be criminalized.
With its policies, the grand coalition has prepared the breeding ground on which racism and ideologies of exclusion thrive.
The rise and radicalization of the AfD are the result of these failed policies as well as the successful racist reinterpretation of the causes of social division.
With the AfD gaining strength, there is a danger of the re-emergence of a fascist party with nationwide mass influence.
It is therefore necessary to stop the AfD on the streets and in parliaments.
An effective policy must fight causes and educate: Overcome poverty and low wages,
push back the extreme right,
advance the democratization of society,
create social security,
and defend basic anti-fascist values with all democratic means.
Strengthen the counterforces in civil society!
Protest and education against the right are a condition of democracy
and must no longer be criminalized.
Projects of mobile counseling against right-wing extremism, victim counseling and civil society democracy alliances as well as antifa initiatives must be given stronger and long-term financial support with a genuine Democracy Promotion Act.
There must be no structural distrust and no compulsion to cooperate with the police and the domestic intelligence service.
Civil society associations such as Change.org, Campact and Attac must once again be considered non-profit through a reform of the tax code.
Replace the Office for the Protection of the Constitution with an independent monitoring center!
The Office for the Protection of the Constitution is a domestic intelligence service.
It is not part of the solution, but part of the problem.
It must be replaced by an independent "Observatory on Authoritarianism and Group-Related Misanthropy."
It is to monitor and educate about right-wing extremism, anti-Semitism, antiziganism, racism, religious fundamentalism and other forms of group-based hostility toward people (cf. chapter "Security for all").
The first step must be to uncover and end the domestic intelligence service's V-people system and its entanglements with the extreme right.
Remove the social breeding ground for the right!
The approval of right-wing politics is built on racism and the experience that interests can only be enforced against others.
That the government has given in to right-wing demands on flight and asylum has made the far right stronger, not weaker.
The division of society also strengthens religious fundamentalists.
Against this, a social policy for all people is needed.
With equal rights for all and
massive investment in the public infrastructure that holds a society together - affordable housing, free public transportation, good health care, jobs and education (see chapter on "Solidary Immigration Society").
Disarming the extreme right and investigating right-wing terror!
Investigation priorities at the BKA and the Federal Prosecutor's Office must focus more strongly on the networking of the militant Nazi scene, especially corresponding networks within the police, the Bundeswehr and special units.
They must no longer play down cases of right-wing violence as isolated incidents.
Reichsbürger and neo-Nazis must finally have their weapons permits revoked.
We want the right to stay for the victims of right-wing violence in order to counter the intention of the perpetrators to displace them,
and we condemn the attacks on mosques, synagogues and other sacred or symbolic places.
Left-wing people and structures are also repeatedly targeted by right-wing attacks.
We stand together in solidarity with victims of right-wing violence and their families.
They need better and long-term support.
Democratization of the security authorities!
A scientific investigation of extreme right-wing attitudes and racist practices in the police and the Bundeswehr is needed.
What is needed to combat racism and esprit de corps in the police force is an independent complaint and investigation body at the federal level, mandatory identification, an overhaul of training, and rotation models for closed units.
Racist, anti-Semitic, homophobic, transphobic and sexist views must also be actively combated in the authorities (cf. chapter "Security for all!").
We call for the establishment of a committee of inquiry into right-wing terrorism to continue the investigation and to come to terms with the long history of right-wing terrorist structures in the Federal Republic and the responsibility of state agencies.
All NSU files must finally be made accessible to the public.
We will press ahead with the parliamentary investigation of right-wing terror in the Bundestag, exert pressure for the release of secret service files on the Oktoberfest assassination and the NSU complex, among other things, and continue to support independent research to the best of our ability.
We demand the ban of militant, armed, neo-Nazi organizations.
We are committed to an anti-fascist culture of remembrance to preserve the memory of the victims of that time and today.
May 8, as the day of liberation from fascism, should finally become a national holiday.
We want to strengthen political education in schools and critical social sciences at universities.
Germany has a special responsibility because of the unprecedented crimes of the Germans against Jewish people and against Sinti*zze and Rom*nja because of the unleashing of the Second World War and the crimes against the peoples of Europe - especially against Poland and the peoples of the Soviet Union - against political dissidents, disabled people and homosexuals - and must oppose any kind of misanthropy, anti-Semitism, antiziganism, anti-Muslim and other racism and sexism.
Strengthening the rights of minorities
Danes, Frisians, Sinti*zze and Rom*nja as well as Sorb*innen/Wend*innen have lived in Germany for centuries, the regional language Low German is still spoken today.
The creation of cultural and linguistic diversity therefore includes the promotion of regional and minority languages recognized in accordance with the European Minority Charter (European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages).
We demand federal policy principles for the preservation and further development of the identity, language and culture of ethnic minorities as well as minority protection in the Basic Law.
In the structural support of regions, the needs of ethnic minorities shall be adequately taken into account.
In a very special way, this concerns Lusatia/Łužyca/Łužica, which is once again facing upheaval.
We stand for providing financial support to institutions and projects for the preservation, maintenance and development of minority languages and cultures in accordance with their growing tasks.
We are committed to protecting and promoting the Sinti*zze and Rom*nja.
We are committed to the continuation of the social reappraisal of the history of persecution of the Sinti*zze and Rom*nja during the Nazi era.
We support measures against antiziganism and to strengthen the participation of Sinti*zze and Rom*nja and want to communicate the social contribution of the minority in Germany more comprehensively in order to counteract the structural inequality and the deep-seated rejection towards the minority.
The recommendations of the independent expert commission on antiziganism must be implemented quickly.
We support the Europe-wide efforts to create reliable minority policy instruments at the level of the European Union - the rejection of the Minority Safepack Initiative by the EU Commission must not be the last word.
Security for all instead of a surveillance state
Violent crime has been declining for years.
But the feeling of insecurity is growing.
Every time there is a report on criminal offenses, the government's domestic politicians call for stricter laws and the restriction of basic rights.
This security policy manages the problems instead of solving them.
This has mainly benefited the conservatives' desire for power and the profits of the security industry.
The prevailing security policy is unjust.
It hits people with little money and no lobby harder.
Substitute prison sentences for minor offenses like driving without a ticket send thousands of people to prison each year.
Controls on white-collar crime and tax evasion, on the other hand, are being scaled back - the big ones are being let off the hook.
For many people, the restriction of fundamental rights and the arming of the police mean new insecurities.
Thus, division and aggression are reinforced in everyday life.
All the more so as more and more extreme right-wing networks in the police and judiciary are being uncovered.
The federal government's actions in the corona pandemic also too often met false standards.
The restriction of civil rights and freedom of assembly was severe, and proportionality was often not respected.
Occupational safety at large corporations like Tönnies and Amazon was poorly enforced,
while people in the park were harassed by police.
People with low incomes and in small apartments were particularly affected by this skewing of crisis policy.
Greater security is not achieved by arming the police and intelligence services, but by tackling the social causes of crime, insecurity and violence.
The enforcement of existing law and the prevention of dangers must be guaranteed, as must the protection of civil liberties and civil rights - for everyone!
We therefore want a change in policy - away from a one-sided focus on repressive measures and symbolic policies and toward a comprehensive approach to a democratic security policy that protects fundamental rights, strengthens prevention, expands social security, invests in the public sphere and democratizes the security authorities.
In the long term, we want to reduce state violence as a means of conflict resolution and replace it with civil society prevention and cooperation.
Enforce fundamental rights comprehensively!
A nationally effective anti-discrimination law is needed, modeled on the Berlin anti-discrimination law.
We oppose right-wing campaigns that seek to criminalize minorities and reinterpret social problems as ethnic or cultural conflicts.
More safety through more participation!
We want a security policy that does not have an authoritarian slant but involves all those affected.
In the event of a pandemic, for example, pandemic and health councils will be needed in the future to involve civil society in all its diversity in the implementation and design of infection control measures at the national and local levels.
Maintain proportionality!
Petty offenses such as "driving without a ticket" and "containerizing" as well as victimless offenses such as violations of the Narcotics Act or "illegal entry" must finally be decriminalized.
Substitute prison sentences for fines are socially unjust, they should be abolished!
Strengthen the rule of law!
Secret services are foreign bodies in democracy.
Due to their lack of transparency and the priority given to the protection of informants, they hinder police investigations and legal clarification.
The defense against danger is the task of a democratically controlled police force.
That is why we want to abolish the Office for the Protection of the Constitution and, in the long term, all intelligence services, and replace it with a monitoring center for authoritarianism and group-based misanthropy.
First of all, the use of undercover agents must be stopped (see chapter "Stopping right-wing terror and violence").
Make data protection effective!
We want to safeguard the right to informational self-determination: against data retention, inventory data access and online searches ("state Trojan"), non-individualized radio cell searches, ubiquitous video surveillance, spying and eavesdropping attacks and dragnet searches.
Especially in times of crisis: No lockdown for democracy - civil rights are systemically relevant!
There must be no disempowerment of parliaments, no (self-)empowerment of the executive.
Political activity and meetings must remain possible.
General assembly bans are poison for democracy.
Labor law must not be undermined either.
The right to privacy and informational self-determination also applies to employees.
This starts with protection against video surveillance at the workplace, the use of detectives or the monitoring of e-mail traffic.
In light of new opportunities for digital performance monitoring, we call for an Employee Data Protection Act.
Security is a public task!
We want to prevent or reverse the privatization of security through private security services, "black sheriffs," etc.
It is already difficult enough to monitor state security authorities, but it is impossible with private services.
Stop special criminal law!
The anti-terrorism legislation of the federal governments of the past 20 years should be put to the test in terms of civil rights.
Fighting crime and averting danger is the task of the law enforcement authorities.
This does not require special political criminal law (such as Sections 129 a and 129 b of the German Criminal Code); we want to abolish these sections.
We demand the lifting of the PKK ban.
State and civil organizations must not be militarized.
We want to end civil-military cooperation (ZMZ) in favor of strengthening technical relief and disaster management.
The existing structures of the ZMZ and the structures of the Bundeswehr reserve forces currently being established must be dissolved.
Stop violence - protect victims!
In order to combat violence against women and children, full funding is finally needed for women's counseling centers and emergency services, sufficient places in women's shelters, and prevention programs for violent men (see chapter on "Feminism").
Make gun ownership more difficult!
Weapons and ammunition possession are to be more strictly regulated.
Violent criminals must be consistently banned from carrying weapons.
We want compensation for intrusive measures such as house searches, body searches, telecommunications surveillance and the like if they are subsequently found to be illegal or abusive.
Police under the rule of law
The working conditions for many police officers are characterized by stress and overtime.
This is also due to the fact that they are always being assigned new tasks.
We want to change that and improve working conditions.
In a state governed by the rule of law, the police must not be used as a universal means of dealing with problems; they should be limited to the core tasks of averting concrete dangers and combating crime, in strict compliance with the principle of proportionality.
Documented cases of police discrimination doubled in 2019.
