Every year there are hundreds of cases of unlawful police violence for which no one has to answer - there is hardly any prosecution.
Assaults are rarely reported and even more rarely charged.
In many cases, deployment strategies are used that contradict a democracy.
This creates a police culture that allows and encourages abusive use of force.
A change of direction is needed here!
The exercise of the state's monopoly on the use of force must be better controlled.
Especially for the many police officers who act in accordance with the rule of law and are committed to the protection of all people, the structures must be changed in such a way that they all meet this requirement.
Fewer assaults can only be achieved through a change in police self-image, forms of deployment and police culture.
In addition to streamlining its tasks, the police therefore need a modern, human rights-oriented mission statement based on proportionality, de-escalation and democratic control.
A citizen-oriented police force must protect the rights of migrants and demonstrators as
well as be accessible and approachable for the people.
DIE LINKE stands by all those who oppose police violence and racism and advocate the expansion of fundamental rights and democracy.
The movements against police violence and police law tightening, Black Lives Matter as well as the migrant initiatives and associations are our allies (see chapter "Solidary Immigration Society").
DIE LINKE will not participate in any government that further expands police powers
and dismantles democratic freedoms.
Good working conditions!
Police officers need good and modern training.
In addition, we need a modern staff co-determination system for the police.
Establishment of independent complaint and investigation offices against police violence and discrimination by police officers!
Effective control can only be carried out by an independent body.
It requires a critical eye, institutional independence of the police and the interior administration, and sufficient powers and resources.
Live diversity!
The composition of the police force must reflect the population.
Means for this can be anonymized application procedures or quotas.
Security through traceability!
For the purpose of investigation and prevention of assaults, incident logs and police videos should be kept at trusts.
Transparency now!
An individual labeling obligation must be introduced immediately and everywhere.
It must become a matter of course that police officers face citizens in an individually recognizable manner.
Limitation of powers according to the rule of law!
Police laws in recent years have softened the boundaries.
We want to reverse the tougher penalties for resistance offenses.
We also reject the expansion of the powers of the federal police.
Address problems!
A humanistic view of humanity must be strengthened in the police force and anti-human attitudes must be countered.
These need to be identified, acknowledged, made aware of, and addressed with the help of independent studies.
Create clarity!
Clear rules are needed to prevent racial profiling:
Suspicionless checks based on rubber-stamp paragraphs, as in the Federal Police Act, must be abolished.
No tolerance for intolerance in government service!
Police officers and officials who are found to have engaged in racist, sexist or homophobic behavior must be consistently disciplined, if necessary up to and including dismissal from the service.
De-escalation instead of armament!
We reject the militarization of the police, their increasing equipment with machine guns and "less lethal weapons" such as tasers, the use of rubber bullets or armed SEK against demonstrations.
We want to massively restrict the use of pepper spray by the police;
it should be banned in connection with gatherings, assemblies in public spaces and events.
Training must change!
Most of the police training for the senior service should take place in the general universities.
More critical police research and teaching is needed, as well as ongoing evaluation of police actions.
Give support!
There is a need for mandatory support services such as supervision, training on diversity and non-discriminatory behavior, and psychological support.
The aim is to support civil servants in coming to terms with their experiences
and to prevent discriminatory attitudes from becoming entrenched.
Proximity to citizens instead of barracking!
Officers in closed units should rotate to make it more difficult for esprit de corps to develop.
Overall, we want far fewer closed units
and instead a citizen-oriented police force.
Ensuring the independence of politics
DIE LINKE is the only party in the Bundestag that does not receive donations from corporations, banks, insurance companies or lobbyists.
That's where it stays.
The influence of lobbying on all politics must be pushed back.
Laws must not be written by those who profit from them.
Corruption and bribery, granting and accepting advantages, intransparency and party sponsoring must not be allowed to determine politics.
We want to introduce a binding, machine-readable and transparent lobby register and advocate a ban on the employment of lobbyists in federal ministries and - in the case of full-time parliamentarians - of members of parliament as paid lobbyists for third parties.
We need an independent lobby commissioner to supervise and control the register, elected by the Bundestag.
The federal government's draft legislation must be accompanied by a list of stakeholders and experts whose opinions were taken into account in its preparation and drafting or who otherwise contributed (legislative footprint).
No lobbying at schools!
Insofar as research and institutions or even individual studies are paid for by lobbyists, this must be made transparent.
Subsequent "thank-you donations" and bribery with the aim of enhancing the lobbyist's image must also be punishable without restriction as bribery of members of parliament.
Members of parliament must be prohibited from accepting donations.
The additional income of Members of Parliament must be published promptly in euros and cents.
We want to ban corporate and lobbyist donations to parties as well as party sponsorship such as corporate booths at party conventions and limit donations from private individuals to 25,000 euros per year.
We want to put a stop to the mixing of political and economic interests: Federal ministers and parliamentary state secretaries must wait at least three years after leaving office, or for the duration of their entitlement to transitional benefits, before moving to companies with whose economic interests they were previously politically involved.
We want to expand and strengthen the European Anti-Fraud Authority OLAF.
Democratize democracy!
Democracy is more than casting your vote every four years.
To achieve this, more co-determination and participation must be created at all levels and in all areas - from the European, international and municipal levels to the workplace and the economy.
That is why DIE LINKE has been demanding for years that popular initiatives, referendums and plebiscites must also be possible at the federal level.
We want the privatization of public services to be stopped, as well as all public-private partnerships (PPPs).
Until this is enforced, all privatization projects must be submitted to the citizens for a direct vote by referendum.
Democracy needs freedom of speech and of the press, freedom of assembly and association, and the freedom of citizens from state spying (see "Chapter on Data Security and Data Protection").
We want to introduce popular initiatives, referendums and plebiscites at the federal level.
The expansion of co-determination rights also includes the introduction of referendums, i.e. citizens can veto parliamentary decisions.
We want to set up binding citizens* forums.
Planning approval and regional planning procedures must be designed in such a way that everyone has sufficient time to inform themselves, to check whether their interests are being protected and to participate.
We reject any acceleration of the planning approval process at the expense of citizen participation.
We want to support and promote the instrument of citizens' councils developed by civil society, whereby randomly drawn people from the middle of society design solutions and issues.
We want to further expand the right to petition as a civil right.
We want to strengthen the rights of the opposition in all parliaments, plenary sessions and committees.
Committee meetings should always be open to the public.
DIE LINKE advocates lowering the voting age in all democratic decision-making processes at the European, federal, state and local levels to 14.
This includes the right to vote for migrants living here for a long time (see chapter "Solidary Immigration Society").
Freedom of movement is an essential right that must not be taken away from anyone across the board.
We want to ban parental house arrest.
This is an outdated educational tool that is contrary to the fundamental rights of children and adolescents.
We reject (automatic) membership of children in religious or ideological communities of their parents.
Joining may only be done by oneself and after reaching religious maturity.
People who are under full care must not be excluded from elections.
Accessibility of polling places and voting processes must be ensured.
Youth policy at eye level.
DIE LINKE is committed to a policy that respectfully includes all generations and stands up for the rights of pensioners just as it does for children and young people.
Young people should become responsible citizens.
To achieve this, we want a paradigm shift in youth policy: away from heteronomy and restriction and toward self-determination and serious, value-neutral education at eye level.
Better support for civic engagement
More than 30 million people are involved in this country.
In clubs, initiatives, rescue services, volunteer fire departments and many other places, committed people ensure social cohesion.
Democracy thrives on the critical and participatory involvement of a vibrant civil society.
We want to better support this diverse volunteerism and lower barriers for social groups that are underrepresented in engagement.
Civic engagement must not be misused as a substitute for public services.
Honorary office needs main office.
We want to expand and secure structures that support voluntarily engaged people.
Recognition of volunteerism must be improved.
Together with the states and municipalities, we want to create a uniform nationwide volunteer passport that allows discounts and free use of recreational, cultural, and educational facilities.
Youth Volunteer Services are important educational and orientation programs for young people.
We want to expand them and improve their quality, especially in terms of pedagogical support.
We want to provide better support for socially disadvantaged young people to make it easier for them to participate in voluntary services.
We support the demand of many volunteer service members for free travel for volunteer service members on public transport.
Civil society organizations that bundle commitment and make interests and demands visible are indispensable for a living democracy.
In recent years, obstacles have been placed in the way of many organizations with the non-profit law.
We want to change this and, to this end, reform the non-profit law (see chapter "Reforming income tax fairly").
We would like to focus the newly established German Foundation for Involvement and Volunteering more strongly on promoting existing involvement structures and further strengthening the role of civil society.
The character of voluntary engagement must be preserved.
That is why monetization must be prevented, and engagement must not replace or prevent jobs that are subject to social security contributions.
Volunteering must be given a higher priority in the political debate.
We therefore advocate for a main committee on civic engagement in the German Bundestag.
Culture: crisis-proof, diverse and accessible to all
Culture and art in their many forms are indispensable and relevant to democracy for all of us.
The freedom of art is protected in Article 5, Paragraph 3 of the Basic Law and thus constitutes a fundamental right.
However, art and culture can only be free and fulfill their social tasks if the promotion of culture is not regarded in large parts as a voluntary task of the states and municipalities.
DIE LINKE advocates that the promotion of culture be regarded as a compulsory task, i.e. the state not only protects art and culture, but also promotes them.
Art and culture help us to gain different perspectives on our social interaction and grievances, to explore their causes and to question them
- to enable us to improve conditions for all people in a spirit of solidarity.
Overcoming social inequality
and all cultural oppression is the task of progressive, enlightened culture,
whose content and goal is a humanistic view of man and the comprehensive development of the associated individuals in a spirit of solidarity.
DIE LINKE advocates a diverse, emancipatory and participatory culture that is accessible and affordable to all.
In metropolises as well as in rural areas, in cultural institutions and the independent scene.
Cultural diversity thrives on a broad concept of culture.
This includes participatory open spaces for children and young people, socio-cultural centers, urban club culture, club culture, municipal cinemas and theaters, orchestras, intercultural and transcultural places of cultural education, libraries, as well as spaces for experimental arts, museum facilities and a vibrant culture of commemoration.
We also see the promotion of culture as the promotion of infrastructure.
With this in mind, we want to maintain, develop and expand the cultural infrastructure in the city and the country.
DIE LINKE opposes the economization and privatization of public services.
Culture is primarily the responsibility of the states and municipalities.
Cuts in the cultural sector at the municipal and state level, which are already taking place in many places, are harbingers of distribution struggles that are imminent with the changed budget situation after the Corona crisis.
The Corona crisis confronts state and local governments with significant financial problems that they cannot solve on their own.
Against this backdrop, DIE LINKE is calling for, among other things, a wealth tax and an asset levy to deal with the costs of the crisis and to finance permanent stimulus programs (see the chapter on "Changing course with taxes").
Municipal debt and the need to save money would not only hit culture - as a so-called voluntary task - first, but would also further exacerbate the financial crisis.
That is why culture must become a joint task of the federal, state and local governments.
The federal government's ineffective pandemic response is also being played out on the backs of people working in the cultural sector, who have been in a permanent lockdown for months.
The government has failed to show a social solution for cultural workers.
For one thing, Coronasoforthilfe does not address the realities of life and work for many cultural workers.
On the other hand, many aid programs have major hurdles for small and medium-sized cultural enterprises.
However, the Corona crisis also exacerbates problematic situations that existed before the crisis, because culture is not adequately funded.
We therefore stand for continuous dialog with actors in the cultural scene and support protests by cultural workers and employees in the event industry.
DIE LINKE wants to enable the self-employed, freelancers and the arts, culture, media and creative sectors to resume their activities in good shape.
In this sense, access to a monthly lump sum of at least 1,200 euros - also retroactive from March 2020 - should be made available for the duration of the corona pandemic.
DIE LINKE wants to make culture crisis-proof and is fighting for good, living wage jobs and social security in the cultural sector.
Temporary, low-paid employment contracts and the high proportion of project funding - especially in the independent scene - do not allow for the accumulation of reserves.
The resulting unstable living and working conditions are not very crisis-proof.
The crisis-induced change also offers the opportunity to develop more sustainable,
gender-equitable
and crisis-proof funding systems.
We call for the inclusion of everyone in the statutory social security systems (pension, health, long-term care and unemployment insurance) in order to improve the social security of unsteady employees and the solo self-employed.
The artists' social insurance fund must be opened up to additional professional groups and the federal subsidy must be increased.
We demand binding minimum standards for remuneration in independent artistic and cultural work,
Sector-specific fee floors
and a legally secured exhibition fee for visual artists.
The negotiating position of creators must be strengthened in copyright contract law and their co-determination rights must be expanded vis-à-vis collecting societies.
We reject the trend of universities to increasingly establish collecting societies.
They are non-transparent, difficult to control and orient research towards profit rather than knowledge gain and the common good.
DIE LINKE fights for a science that serves the common good and not profit orientation.
DIE LINKE wants to put federal cultural funding on a new footing and reform funding systems.
Overall, federal cultural funding must be made more sustainable, more process-oriented, less bureaucratic, and less project-oriented.
In this sense, long-term scholarship programs that allow for the accumulation of reserves make sense, as does the continuation of the flexibilization of the law governing the allocation of funding.
Social standards, gender equity and diversity are to be established as criteria in the allocation of federal funding.
We want to equip the cultural promotion funds in line with demand and strengthen them as a central instrument of the independent scene.
The ban on cooperation between the federal and state governments must be ended.
We want culture to be a joint task
and a state goal of culture in the Basic Law in order
to strengthen cooperative cultural federalism.
We want a federal minister of culture with cabinet rank and a ministry of culture to represent the interests of culture more effectively vis-à-vis other ministries and at the European level.
The federal states and local authorities must receive sufficient funding so that they can fulfill their tasks in the preservation and promotion of culture,
to avoid tariff evasion,
and to ensure a wide variety of cultural offerings in the portfolio, along with the necessary investments for them.
DIE LINKE wants to realize "culture for all" and cultural participatory justice.
In order to strengthen equal opportunities, inclusion and diversity, diversity-oriented structural change in the cultural sector must be guided by criteria that are critical of power and discrimination.
Diversity in the cultural sector has an impact on the program, opening up new perspectives and approaches to culture and attracting new visitors.
To this end, anti-discrimination strategies must become effective across the board.
Structural discrimination based on social and ethnic origin, class, gender, sexual identity, disability, religion or belief must be eliminated.
Cultural education creates access to art and culture to enable people to engage creatively with themselves and their environment.
Places of cultural education therefore serve as spaces of self-education and self-empowerment.
For this reason, we want the federal "Kultur macht stark" program to be continued and sustained with increased funding.
Federal regulations should allow urban planners* to increasingly consider "open spaces" that are intended to serve participatory and experimental uses.
Club culture is an important and valuable part of our culture, free spaces where people can enjoy music, dance and party.
That is why we want to promote and preserve the club and festival culture.
Club death is part of the sell-off of cities, we want to stop it.
Clubs are therefore to be recognized as culture and placed on an equal footing with other cultural venues, especially in tax and building law.
"Art in buildings": 3 percent of the costs of public buildings are to be used for works of art.
We insist on compliance with the UNESCO Convention on Cultural Diversity in international trade agreements.
DIE LINKE stands for barrier-free and equal access to culture.
We want to create spaces for dialogue and exchange
and promote a change of perspective.
Admission to federally funded museums and collections must be free of charge in the future, and cultural education staff must be increased.
Cultural institutions must be barrier-free and offer inclusive services.
The experience of cultural institutions and projects with intercultural and transcultural mediation concepts should be utilized and disseminated.
We promote and demand the production and protection of temporary and non-institutional, freely accessible arts, such as street art and art in public spaces, in socio-cultural and self-managed centers.
We advocate for comprehensive cooperation between schools and art institutions as well as independent artists.
DIE LINKE wants to digitally secure cultural assets and make them accessible to all.
To achieve this, we need a nationwide digitalization strategy.
We are committed to an Open Access strategy in the cultural sector as well.
We create opportunities and incentives for cultural institutions to place their digital publications under free licenses.
We want to expand our cooperation with the German Digital Library.
We want to simplify the lending of digital media for public libraries.
We also want to preserve the cinematic heritage permanently and make it accessible.
DIE LINKE stands for a lively and pluralistic history and remembrance policy.
We want to encourage a critical examination of Germany's history in the 19th and 20th centuries, especially the reappraisal of the crimes of National Socialism.
The reappraisal and remembrance of colonialism and the associated slave trade and slavery must become more present.
We want to encourage a critical examination of the history of Germany in the 19th and 20th centuries, especially the reappraisal of the crimes of National Socialism as well as the history of both German societies and states after the Second World War.
The reappraisal and remembrance of colonialism and the associated slave trade and slavery must become more present.
We want to strengthen memorial sites as places of remembrance and learning as well as places of documentation.
Volunteer-led memorial work is to be supported across the board.
The working conditions especially of the pedagogical staff in museums and memorials have to be improved.
Together with local initiatives from civil society, we want to work through and reflect on postcolonial continuities in order to contribute to a democratic, anti-fascist culture, because remembering means acting.
We want to promote a living culture of remembrance that is oriented to the realities of the immigration society.
Halle 2019 and Hanau 2020:
We want to anchor the commemoration and remembrance of the victims of racist and anti-Semitic violence in Germany's recent history more firmly.
A legal basis for the restitution of Nazi looted art is to be created and provenance research expanded.
Likewise, the restitution of unlawfully acquired cultural property from colonial contexts must be regulated by law.
Strengthen media diversity, independent journalism and press freedom
Diverse and independent journalism is a prerequisite for the democratic formation of opinion and will and is therefore indispensable.
Digitization, concentration processes at newspapers and editorial offices, private opinion and market power of platforms such as Facebook and YouTube, the increase in hate messages and fake news: the media world is undergoing radical change.
DIE LINKE wants a diverse media landscape that includes a strong public broadcaster and non-commercial media alongside private providers.
Public broadcasting stands for media participation and basic services.
It must be able to respond to changes in media usage, offer journalistic quality and, in addition to news and information, comprehensive perspectives, education, entertainment and cultural diversity.
DIE LINKE wants a broad social debate to be held both on the reforms and the mission of public broadcasting and on journalistic standards in the media landscape.
Our central concerns regarding public broadcasting are:
We want to compensate and automate the exemptions from contributions for eligible persons with public funds and comprehensively extend them to social institutions and people with disabilities.
The tiresome dunning process should be scaled back.
DIE LINKE wants to preserve the programming autonomy of the broadcasters, which is protected by the freedom of broadcasting, and to ensure that public broadcasting is financed in line with its tasks.
The rights of freelancers and quasi-employees must be strengthened and they must be given secure income and employment prospects.
We want to expand regionality instead of cutting back: New ARD community facilities should also be located in eastern German states.
Strong regional and local coverage by all existing broadcasters must be guaranteed on a permanent basis.
Productions commissioned from third parties should be remunerated appropriately and fairly, and the awarding of contracts to external production companies should be linked to compliance with social standards such as collectively agreed wages, minimum wages and industry-specific minimum fees.
Public service offerings should be expanded in the sense of an independent platform;
fully financed commissioned productions should remain in the media libraries indefinitely,
The diversity of sports must be reflected in programming, because sports are more than soccer, skiing and major events like the Olympics.
Democratize sports rights: Financial proportionality of broadcasting rights and a fairer distribution among the clubs (also gender-equitable!) should be asserted vis-à-vis the rights holders, including the German Soccer League.
We are committed to transparent and non-discriminatory algorithms.
Whether at private or public media companies: for DIE LINKE, the diversity of society must be reflected in the staff structure and in the programming, so that more realities of life are reflected.
Journalism and media work must not become a field of work that you have to be able to afford.
We therefore want good working conditions,
Gender equality
and diversity in the media and film industry.
Media work and education must be inclusive and the media usage options diverse and barrier-free.
Freedom of the press and journalistic work must be guaranteed.
We therefore call for media professionals to be better protected against attacks, persecution and violence.
Journalists as holders of professional secrets as well as their sources must be protected (Whistleblower Protection Act).
Strengthening the public's right to information: DIE LINKE advocates a press information law that safeguards the media's constitutionally guaranteed right to information from federal authorities.
Collective bargaining and fee agreements for the self-employed must be anchored in law;
authors must be anchored in law and must be possible.
The media market is increasingly dominated by monopolies, accelerated by the Corona crisis.
The market and monopoly power of large digital corporations and platforms must be pushed back and democratically controlled, for example, through supervisory structures that are independent of the state (cf. chapter on "Digitization").
While some media companies are benefiting from current developments, others are struggling due to the drastic decline in advertising revenues.
DIE LINKE calls for a nationwide report on the state of media diversity and freedom of the press, which would also regularly examine developments on the media market and derive recommendations for action to safeguard media and opinion diversity.
In order to compensate for competitive disadvantages, DIE LINKE advocates press funding that strengthens journalistic media diversity with good working conditions at the local, regional, statewide and European levels away from the state and supports appropriate research formats of online journalism as well as non-commercial offerings in addition to print media.
DIE LINKE wants to improve youth protection on the Internet.
For us, effective youth protection consists in particular of comprehensive media education programs for parents, teachers, children and young people.
Media education belongs on the agenda of all educational institutions - across generations.
However, the teaching of media skills also plays a central role in old age.
We want to strengthen the role of the state media authorities.
Simplified access to European funding from the economic stimulus programs and investment programs beyond the previous media funding should help to overcome the consequences of the pandemic.
as well as the needs of a democratic media landscape and to increasingly promote non-profit media freedom initiatives.
We defend freedom to and from religion and the separation of church and state
We defend the right to freedom of religion: it is the right of freedom of faith, conscience and freedom of religious and ideological confession.
We support the struggle of people for global social justice, democracy and peace regardless of their worldview and religion.
We advocate the institutional separation of state and religion.
The right to religious freedom is a protection especially for minorities.
That is why we defend Jewish people, Muslims and all other religious minorities when they are discriminated against because of their religion.
Threats, attacks and assaults are directed against Muslim and Jewish people and against synagogues and mosques.
They have become commonplace.
Anti-Semitism and anti-Muslim racism, like any other form of racism, must have no place in society.
We advocate equal treatment of all religions and worldviews with the Christian churches.
DIE LINKE supports the struggle of trade unions
and churches for the work-free Sunday.
We demand the abolition of the special church labor law for employees in the churches, in Diakonie and Caritas.
The human right to the free exercise of religion includes the right to publicly profess a religion.
DIE LINKE defends the right of self-determination of Muslim women, opposes a ban on religiously motivated clothing and rejects a restriction of employee rights on this basis.
We want an ethics class in which all students with their different ideological, cultural and religious backgrounds can discuss ethical issues together.
Schools should continue to impart knowledge about religions as part of their educational mission.
If religious education is offered as an optional subject at schools, all religious communities should be able to participate.
We want to abolish military chaplaincy in its current form.
It is also controversial within the churches.
It must be replaced by a chaplaincy contract for all members of the Bundeswehr that guarantees equal care by all religious and ideological communities.
The church or ideological caregivers are not to be employed or civil servants by the Bundeswehr.
DIE LINKE demands that the churches collect their taxes or contributions independently in the future.
We advocate the constitutional mandate that has existed since 1919 to replace state contributions to the churches.
In an ideologically and religiously diverse society, everyone must have the same opportunities for funding.
DIE LINKE is against a ban on the construction of sacred buildings.
We call for the introduction of state-protected holidays for Jewish and Muslim religious communities.
DIE LINKE advocates the legal equality of all religious and ideological communities.
Sport is not a luxury
Sport is for everyone.
To achieve this, we need to improve the conditions for access to sport.
Being able to play sports should not depend on income and social status.
Sports clubs are also places of successful integration.
We promote inclusive, integrative, nature- and environment-friendly sports.
Sports programs and the promotion of sports must be gender-responsive and take appropriate account of all age groups.
Many sports halls, sports grounds and swimming pools are dilapidated and some are already closed.
The need for remediation amounts to around 31 billion euros.
Our program for the future provides for sufficient investment to make the facilities barrier-free.
and ecologically sensible refurbishment.
Admission prices for swimming pools must be affordable for all.
Recognized sports organizations, schools and universities should be given the right to use public sports facilities free of charge, as regulated in the new Thuringian Sports Promotion Act.
All students should be allowed to participate in swimming lessons.
By the end of primary school, all children should be able to swim safely.
DIE LINKE sees popular sport and elite sport as a reciprocal relationship.
It aims to promote popular sport with its positive social and health effects as well as to support potential sporting careers.
The federal government's top-level sports reform as well as the concept for funding major sports events need to be put to the test.
We want an open discussion about the role of sport in society - also taking into account the consequences of the corona pandemic.
Sport must become a mandatory municipal task.
Athletes' rights must be further strengthened,
existing inequalities in the promotion of sport for people with disabilities are eliminated.
Doping, all forms of violence, corruption and other manipulations must be fought.
The commercialization of sport for the purpose of profit maximization must be pushed back and the teaching of values such as tolerance, respect and fairness must be strengthened.
Maintaining and promoting health must be given greater priority in both popular and competitive sports.
Funding for fan projects, initiatives and projects against extreme rights, discrimination and violence as well as for the integrative impact of sports clubs should be increased and made permanent.
An end to the criminalization of drugs
DIE LINKE advocates a paradigm shift: away from criminal prosecution and towards prevention, counseling and help.
We do not see it as the task of politics to educate people, but to enable them to make informed and risk-conscious consumption decisions.
We do not want to moralize the desire for intoxication.
It is a part of the culture, even if there are risks and possible damages associated with it.
Harm reduction is only possible through good health and social policies.
Banning drugs does not effectively reduce the risks for users and society.
It neither prevents drug trafficking nor does it effectively reduce consumption.
The health hazards of extenders, the financing of organized crime, acquisitive crime, social decline of addicts, concomitant diseases such as HIV/AIDS and hepatitis - many drug-related problems are caused more by repression than by the drugs themselves.
At the same time, repression ties up large amounts of financial resources: several billion euros are spent on criminal prosecution, but only a fraction of this is spent on aid and prevention.
Drugs and addiction are a mirror of society: one can be addicted not only to illegal or legal substances, tobacco or alcohol, but also, for example, to gambling, medications and energy drinks.
Addiction has multiple social and psychological causes and - like other diseases - should not be interpreted as a failure of individuals.
We want to legalize cannabis.
We want to create a primarily non-commercial supply option and allow possession and cultivation for personal use.
As a temporary transitional solution, we propose model projects for legal availability in the federal states with simultaneous nationwide decriminalization of users.
The legal rules for the medical use of cannabis must be changed in the interest of the patients.
Access must be de-bureaucratized.
The use of cannabis as medicine must also be made possible in the case of less severe illnesses and the requirement for approval by the health insurance funds must be abolished.
We want to improve supply security by growing more cannabis as medicine in Germany.
The regulations on driving vehicles with medical use of cannabis must finally be clearly regulated.
Substitution therapy must be open to all opioid addicts.
Access and treatment must be facilitated, especially in prisons.
To do this, we need more substitution physicians, among other things.
Diamorphine-assisted treatment (heroin distribution) and take-home arrangements are also to be expanded.
DIE LINKE is calling for an independent scientific review of whether the repressive drug policy to date has achieved its objectives and what side effects it has had.
We want to end the criminalization of consumers.
To this end, nationwide maximum quantities are to be set for frequently used drugs, the possession of which will not result in prosecution.
In these cases, law enforcement must be replaced with counseling and assistance services.
It also frees up resources to fight organized crime.
n The focus must be on: Reducing damage and saving lives.
That's why we want to expand harm-reduction measures.
We want universal access to drug consumption rooms, sterile consumption paraphernalia, and take-home administration of naloxone, which is life-saving in opioid overdose.
We want analysis-based prevention programs (drug checking) to be explicitly allowed and implemented by the states.
We want to adjust the regulations on drugs in road traffic.
For all drugs, blood concentration limits are set at which impairment of driving ability can be virtually ruled out.
The sobriety requirement should not be affected.
We want to put cannabis- and alcohol-using driving license holders on an equal legal footing.
We want to ban advertising and sponsorship for tobacco and alcohol products in public.
We advocate compliance with the WHO Framework Convention on Tobacco Control.
Tobacco products should be offered in uniform packaging, as in Australia, for example.
We want to further expand the protection of non-smokers and young people.
The use of e-cigarettes should be regarded as a less harmful alternative to tobacco consumption and should therefore be kept more favorable in terms of taxation.
We want to reduce the dangers of gambling addiction.
A state-licensed offer must be introduced for slot machine gaming, with the aim of minimizing the health and social consequences of slot machine gaming.
The same applies to online gambling.
We want a ban on vending machines in catering establishments.
The gambling elements in e-gaming need to be regulated and contained.
Everything is nothing without peace: for peace and disarmament.
Ban arms exports
DIE LINKE defends the principle of peace as a mode of international politics.
The threat of war has not been as great as it is today for decades.
A look at global conditions shows in which directions it can go: Increased competition and authoritarianism, also within the European Union.
Geopolitical rivalries and economic wars are on the rise.
We are committed to a policy of détente
and equitable economic structures.
Respect for international law
and human rights are non-negotiable for us.
That is why there can be no double standards for DIE LINKE on these issues.
"Without justice there can be no peace.
Capitalism carries war within itself like the cloud carries rain." (Jean Jaures)
Yet the German government continues to rely on the unilateral enforcement of economic and geopolitical interests in the competition for locations.
This reinforces global inequality and weakens forms and forums of cross-border cooperation in times of climate catastrophe.
Even with a new president, the U.S. government is continuing its confrontational course to maintain its own supremacy through sanctions and military interventions.
The USA and EU are trying to assert their supremacy against Russia and China.
This threatens to escalate into a new Cold War.
In NATO and EU strategy papers, Russia and China are described as enemy images, and we reject this.
We oppose all forms of imperialism.
NATO's $1.1 trillion in defense spending compares with $61 billion from Russia.
So it's not about security.
But the German government and the European Union are arming themselves - and thus exacerbating the conflicts.
DIE LINKE is aware of the history of German bellicose hegemonic aspirations in Europe and the world.
We are convinced that the Federal Republic of Germany has a special responsibility for peace towards all countries and their people who were victims of these wars as a result of the crimes caused by Nazi Germany in the Second World War.
In the year in which the beginning of the war of robbery and extermination of the fascist Wehrmacht in the East is commemorated for the 80th time, we renew our commitment to Russia and the other countries of the former Soviet Union: Never again fascism, never again war from German soil!
We want a paradigm shift in foreign policy and stand for non-violent conflict resolution and cross-border cooperation, instead of arms exports and foreign deployments of the Bundeswehr.
For peace and stability, we need a binding set of rules in international politics that always applies.
The basis for this is international law.
The German government and its supporting parties, the CDU/CSU and the SPD, have pursued a course of rearmament and confrontation that DIE LINKE rejects.
DIE LINKE is the peace party and the reliable voice of the peace movement in the Bundestag.
We want an immediate stop to all arms exports.
We reject investments in militarization and rearmament.
We stand for fair economic relations,
sustainable development cooperation
and multilateralism based on solidarity.
We will not participate in a government that wages wars and permits combat missions of the Bundeswehr abroad, that promotes rearmament and militarization.
In the long term, we hold to the vision of a world without armies.
No foreign deployments of the Bundeswehr
The Bundeswehr must be withdrawn from all foreign missions.
20 years ago, it was decided for the first time that the German Armed Forces would participate in the war in Afghanistan, and this decision has been extended year after year by every federal government since then.
DIE LINKE has always rejected the deployment of the Bundeswehr in Afghanistan.
The withdrawal from Afghanistan is to be welcomed.
But it reveals the disaster that war has wrought.
Over 200,000 Afghans have lost their lives, including the more than 100 victims of Kunduz.
Millions of people are on the run.
3,600 Western soldiers lost their lives, including 59 Bundeswehr soldiers.
The war was justified by the need to create security, democracy and women's rights.
None of the stated goals were achieved; on the contrary.
The Taliban are stronger than they have been for a long time, and the social and economic situation in the country is catastrophic.
The lesson of the Afghan catastrophe is the same as that of the Syrian, Libyan and Iraqi catastrophes: Democracy and social progress cannot be imposed with wars from outside.
The consequence must be to permanently withdraw foreign troops, special forces and intelligence services.
From Afghanistan, Mali, and all other foreign deployments.
There are currently around 3,000 soldiers on foreign missions with mandates from the German Bundestag.
In addition, more than10000 Bundeswehr soldiers are active abroad without a mandate, currently in Lithuania, for example.
The Bundeswehr must be recalled from all foreign deployments and not sent on new ones.
We want to invest the funds that have so far been spent on foreign missions in a civilian reconstruction program.
and peacekeeping program.
We reject the foreign missions of the Bundeswehr mandated by the Bundestag.
We also oppose the presence of German soldiers abroad under NATO responsibility, such as currently in Lithuania.
We reject training missions for soldiers and security forces.
We demand a ban on the use of military security and mercenary companies.
We do not want to participate in international police and intelligence missions or training missions that serve to support authoritarian regimes.
We reject civil-military cooperation.
Important civilian aid must not be linked to military action.
We demand that civilian structures for international disaster management be established.
Disarming the Bundeswehr instead of rearming - No Bundeswehr as a worldwide deployment army
The German government's spending on armaments and the Bundeswehr is steadily increasing.
The German government continues to head toward NATO's goal of spending 2 percent of gross domestic product on armaments.
We are committed to disarmament, democracy and peaceful foreign policy; spending on armaments must be drastically reduced.
We will reject any increase in military and arms spending.
The military budget of the German government has increased massively in recent years and currently amounts to 47 billion euros, which corresponds to more than 500 euros of taxpayers' money per citizen.
The price for a highly equipped Bundeswehr:
Billions of taxpayers' money are missing from the expansion of the healthcare system,
the social infrastructure,
Education
and climate protection.
The federal defense budget must and can be significantly reduced, because we want to downsize the Bundeswehr and dispense with major armament projects, such as the Future Combat Air System (FCAS) or the Main Ground Combat System (MGCS) for the development of a battle tank.
We call for a 10 percent reduction in military spending in all countries worldwide in the coming year.
If all countries do this at the same time, the relative security for each country remains the same-and it would free up $183 billion in one fell swoop to fund social good like fighting hunger, poverty, and the aftermath of the Corona crisis.
The transformation of the Bundeswehr into a globally operating task force does not serve our security, but rather the interests of large corporations and elites in the global struggle for raw materials, spheres of influence and sales markets.
The rearmament of the Bundeswehr is accompanied by a militarization of society.
We reject the orientation of the Bundeswehr as an operational army.
DIE LINKE is committed to the gradual disarmament of the Bundeswehr.
Material and units designed exclusively for foreign missions must be dismantled first.
The Bundeswehr's cyber and information space must be disbanded.
DIE LINKE strictly rejects the paradigm shift in military technology and strategy to "revolution in military affairs" (RMA) and cyberwar.
Combating cybercrime and protecting critical infrastructure are the responsibility of the domestic security authorities, not the Bundeswehr (see the chapter on "Digitization").
Extreme right-wing, racist and democracy-endangering ideas in the Bundeswehr and in security companies working for the Federal Republic must be uncovered and combated.
For this reason, we are also calling for a study on racism and right-wing ideas in the Bundeswehr (see chapter "Security for all").
We want to disband the Kommando Spezialkräfte (KSK) special forces unit.
It has become public that there are right-wing, neo-Nazi actors and networks in the Bundeswehr and especially in the elite combat unit KSK.
In addition, there were extensive ammunition losses at the KSK.
DIE LINKE has a part to play in clearing up this scandal.
Decisive action must be taken against right-wing actors and networks in the Bundeswehr and other security agencies.
The scandal surrounding right-wing networks in the Bundeswehr shows the danger to democracy posed by the Bundeswehr's orientation toward war missions.
No advertising for dying!
We reject Bundeswehr advertising in job centers, schools, at education and training fairs and in universities, as well as advertising in public.
The Bundeswehr is not allowed to accept minors - not even in the context of the so-called voluntary homeland security.
DIE LINKE rejects voluntary homeland security as a form of militarization of society.
We reject the deployment of the Bundeswehr in Germany.
Civil protection must be better equipped for emergencies, and the Bundeswehr must not be used as scheduled compensation for civil protection.
In particular, the Bundeswehr must never be given police powers.
Stop arms exports: No business with war!
Germany is number four among the world's leading countries in terms of arms exports.
Weapons have even been supplied to warring states, with Turkey and Saudi Arabia waging their wars with weapons from Germany.
We also want to eliminate all the ways in which arms companies seek to circumvent controls in Germany.
Thus, production facilities of German companies abroad must also fall under German arms export controls.
DIE LINKE rejects special cooperation arrangements with friendly states, such as France, to facilitate arms exports, because German weapons could reach the whole world via this detour.
We demand an immediate stop to all arms exports, especially the export of weapons factories, small arms and light weapons, as their final destination cannot be controlled.
We support an Arms Export Control Act for a legal ban on all arms exports.
Arms exports must no longer be supported with taxpayers' money.
We call for an end to Hermes guarantees.
We support the Hamburg popular initiative against arms exports.
European arms companies such as Airbus or Rheinmetall must be forced to stop their arms production for authoritarian regimes.
The same must apply to digital technology that can be used as a weapon in conflicts or that enables the monitoring and control of telecommunications and terminals.
We want to close legal loopholes that allow German companies to circumvent German laws.
Exports of dual-use items that can be used to produce chemical or biological weapons may not be authorized to states that have not ratified the Chemical Weapons Convention or the Biological Weapons Convention.
The ban on biological and chemical weapons must be effectively controlled.
The export of substances suitable for the production of chemical weapons must be more tightly controlled.
Together with social partners from trade unions, the peace movement and churches, we want to develop conversion programs for and with employees in the arms industry in order to create new, civilian jobs.
Funding programs in industry and for research at universities are to serve only civilian production.
No drones for war
The German government plans to arm the German Armed Forces' Heron TP drones.
At the same time, work is underway on the construction and deployment of the so-called Eurodrone, which is intended to drop guided bombs as well as missiles.
Under pressure from civil society, the peace movement and DIE LINKE, the SPD did not agree to the arming of drones during the last legislative period.
Those who let machines fight for them are quicker to decide to use violence and kill people elsewhere.
And they can be deployed anywhere in the world without a declaration of war, as the U.S. has been doing for years.
The arming of the Bundeswehr with combat drones must be prevented.
We say no to combat drones, even after the election!
Germany must take a first step and generally refrain from arming drones and advocate internationally for a binding ban on armed drones under international law.
We want to finally stop the use and control of combat drones from the military base in Ramstein by the US Army.
No drone warfare from German soil!
Ramstein and the other U.S. military bases in Germany must be closed.
Arming drones may be the first step on the road to autonomous weapon systems.
For example, the multibillion-dollar Future Combat Air System (FCAS) defense project plans drone swarms controlled by artificial intelligence.
We reject that.
We call for a global ban on autonomous weapons systems.
The German government must launch an international initiative to this end.
There is to be no more research into autonomous weapons systems in Germany.
For a world free of nuclear weapons
Our goal remains a world without nuclear weapons.
But the nuclear weapons powers are not fulfilling their disarmament obligations under the Non-Proliferation Treaty.
The UN General Assembly voted in favor of a Nuclear Weapons Ban Treaty (NPT), which entered into force in early 2021.
The federal government did not even participate in the negotiations.
That was wrong.
We reject the dangerous concept of nuclear deterrence.
Even though the last-minute extension of the Nuclear Weapons Reduction Treaty by Presidents Biden and Putin has given the world community a brief respite, new initiatives for disarmament and more arms control are urgently needed.
Nuclear weapons are still stored in Germany as part of NATO's nuclear sharing program.
The Ministry of Defense has decided to purchase 138 new fighter aircraft, including 93 Eurofighters and 45 F-18s.
30 of them are to be used for so-called nuclear sharing within NATO.
By "nuclear sharing" is meant that the Bundeswehr provides fighter aircraft as delivery systems for the 20 U.S. nuclear weapons in Büchel, Rhineland-Palatinate.
U.S. nuclear weapons must be withdrawn and destroyed immediately.
No nuclear weapons should be or be stationed in Germany.
The federal government must not provide launchers and pilots for this purpose.
The use of uranium-enriched munitions must be outlawed.
Nuclear sharing within NATO must be ended.
No fighter carrier systems may be made available and newly acquired for this purpose.
Germany must finally sign the UN Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons.
In Germany, more than 700 cities and municipalities - including the three city-states and all state capitals - have joined the Mayors for Peace campaign, which aims to abolish nuclear weapons worldwide.
The German government must take this appeal seriously and press ahead with the worldwide outlawing of nuclear weapons.
Germany should work to ensure that the U.S. rejoins the nuclear agreement with Iran and that all parties abide by the agreement.
Germany should advocate a relaunch of the treaty banning intermediate-range missiles between the U.S. and Russia.
Cooperation instead of confrontation: For an inclusive security system
NATO is a relic of the Cold War and it continues to operate that way today.
For DIE LINKE, war is not a means of politics.
We need a policy of détente with Russia instead of further escalation and troop deployments or maneuvers on its western border.
This is one of the great lessons and obligations of the Second World War.
Confrontation is no basis for security.
The NATO countries' "war on terror" has not created security either - on the contrary.
Time to finally change course.
We call for the dissolution of NATO
and its replacement by a collective security system with Russian participation that has disarmament as a central goal.
We demand to start negotiations on a German-Russian treaty to achieve and perpetuate reconciliation and friendship between Germany and Russia.
Irrespective of a decision on Germany's remaining in NATO, DIE LINKE will advocate in every political constellation that Germany withdraw from the military structures of the military alliance and that the Bundeswehr be withdrawn from NATO's supreme command.
DIE LINKE rejects maneuvers such as Defender 2021.
Against the background of German history, we particularly oppose any presence of German soldiers east of the Oder-Neisse border.
Plans to further expand the Oberlausitz military training area for escalation policy in Eastern Europe and to develop and test autonomous weapons there must be stopped.
Any support for NATO states that - like Turkey under the Erdoğan regime - disregard international law must be stopped immediately.
Instead of stationing another 500 U.S. soldiers at the U.S. Army Europe and Africa headquarters in Wiesbaden, all foreign military bases in Germany must be closed.
Corresponding contracts, including those with the USA under the Stay Treaty and the Supplementary Agreement to the NATO Status of Forces, will be terminated.
A NATO space center is currently being built at the NATO base in Ramstein.
This is not only to defend satellites that have become indispensable to our daily lives, but also to safeguard the military's ability to act and attack.
The seemingly passive component of "defense in space" has an offensive background.
This is intended to safeguard the military's ability to act and attack.
DIE LINKE rejects the militarization of space.
DIE LINKE also rejects the plans of other states for military use of outer space.
The U.S. has waged a drone war with the help of Ramstein Base, breaking international law from German territory.
The consequence can only be to terminate the residence treaty or to establish its de facto breach by the USA.
Civil conflict management and crisis prevention
Peace is more than the absence of war.
Creating and maintaining peace means establishing the conditions in which life in dignity and security is possible.
Yet security encompasses more than the absence of violence.
Security also means that the supply of food is guaranteed and that there is access to medical care, housing, culture, education and training.
We demand a human right to peace.
We want the German government to work within the UN bodies for the implementation of the right to peace in the sense of the Santiago Declaration by anchoring it in a treaty under international law and to implement it consistently in all political action.
DIE LINKE rejects the mixing of civilian and military measures.
International aid must never be part of a military strategy, but must be guided by the imperative to help populations affected by hunger, climate disasters, and war.
The federal government must focus on civilian peace measures such as the involvement of women's initiatives, training programs, surrender of firearms, and civilian mediators.
The funds made available for civil peace service must be systematically increased.
Internationally already proven instruments, such as unarmed civilian peacekeeping, must be promoted in a straightforward manner.
We want to promote these approaches within the framework of development cooperation and strengthen training for them.
We also want to give foreign peacekeepers the opportunity to complete their training in Germany.
We also want to establish corresponding universities and training centers abroad.
Social justice worldwide
The corona pandemic acts like a burning glass: social inequality is on the rise worldwide.
About one percent of humanity owns 45 percent of global wealth.
The poorer half of the world's population has next to nothing, while the rich get richer and richer.
This trend accelerates dramatically in the Corona crisis.
For the first time since 1990, the UN predicted a global increase in poverty.
The German government and the EU are exacerbating international antagonisms and weakening international agreements and institutions with their trade policy and competition between locations.
There has long been a new arms race: Arms exports around the world have reached their highest level since the end of the Cold War.
The militarization of foreign policy has neither fought terror sustainably nor created more security.
The German government likes to invoke democracy and human rights, but in day-to-day political life other goals count: pushing through economic interests or sealing off Europe against refugees.
We want social justice - worldwide!
We want to overcome the crisis not just for Germany or Europe, but globally.
No one is safe until everyone is safe.
We want to overcome neoliberal capitalism, which is characterized by deregulation, privatization and social cuts.
We want to fight the causes of flight and not refugees.
We want to help turn passive displeasure into active resistance.
We want to change the social balance of power.
We are fighting for a system change.
Our foreign policy must promote democracy, human rights and peace, and support civil society, instead of merely serving economic interests and making deals with dictators.
It must become feminist, social and ecological - that is, it must involve women's organizations, trade unions and social movements.
We are fighting for social justice together with partner parties, trade unionists and social movements,
Peace,
Climate protection,
Democracy
and against racism.
Strong movements give us hope, like Fridays for Future or the Black Lives Matter movement in the US.
Together we can change the world.
Socio-ecologically just world economy
Fair trade policies are a prerequisite for a peaceful world
and for global social justice.
German and European foreign economic policy must no longer be characterized by the narrow-minded goal of putting short-term self-interest first: Those who make others poor and let them stay poor cannot win.
And if you really want to fight the causes of flight, you have to stop creating them over and over again - and exporting them.
Partner countries must be able to build their own economies and value chains and achieve the United Nations Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) by 2030.
Where possible, we want to strengthen regional economic cycles in order to push back the sometimes absurd excesses of globalized supply and production chains.
We want trade policy to finally become an instrument of global cooperation,
of socio-ecological progress
and democratization.
We are opposed to a hypocritical policy that simply burdens people and nature in other regions of the world with the costs of "ecological modernization" in this country and mercilessly exploits their environment and raw materials.
In addition to fair trade policies, we need basic global social services.
We can only build and finance these if wealth is redistributed worldwide.
End trade conflicts!
Trade conflicts such as those between the U.S. and China or the EU have caused economic and social damage and intensified locational competition.
Trade policy must no longer be used for political blackmail.
Cooperation instead of free trade agreements!
Economic agreements must contain a set of rules governing production conditions.
In this way, we want to ensure good work and environmental protection along the global production and supply chains.
The European Economic Partnership Agreements (EPAs) cement dependencies of the Global South as a supplier of raw materials and must be replaced by fair trade agreements.
We call for a supply chain law worthy of its name.
The federal government's law leaves too many loopholes.
Companies with 250 or more employees and small and medium-sized enterprises in high-risk sectors must be obliged to exclude human rights violations, child labor and environmental destruction along their entire value chains.
This includes an effective civil liability regime to strengthen the rights of affected persons and improve working conditions.
Independent environmental due diligence,
the inclusion of affected groups of people in decision-making processes,
and measures to achieve gender equality must be promoted much more strongly.
We want to end the import of raw materials that trigger conflicts and serious human rights violations.
We therefore call for a revision of the Conflict Minerals Regulation, its expansion to include other raw materials as well as the entire value chain, and want to close loopholes.
Globalize labor law!
We support the agreement (UN treaty), which obliges companies to respect the rights and dignity of employees.
This gives employees the opportunity to sue for their rights anywhere in the world at the place where they work.
Fair trade should become the normal form of trade, internationally as well as at local weekly markets.
The UN Migration Pact aims to strengthen the rights of refugees and migrant workers.
As the country with the world's largest surplus in trade in goods and capital, Germany must support the legally binding nature of the international ILO Convention on the Protection of Global Migrant Workers.
We demand that global labor migration recruitment agencies must only operate under license, their fees and contracts must be transparent, and recruitment fees must be borne by employers.
Secure jobs worldwide!
We demand uniform and globally valid minimum requirements to protect workers in the workplace.
Collapsing factory buildings, the use of hazardous chemicals without proper protective equipment, and other life-threatening working conditions must be avoided.
In order for the super-rich to become even richer, people produce at the risk of their lives.
We demand an end to this dangerous cheap production!
Sustainable economic policy instead of national location competition!
There is a need for an international equalization mechanism that commits countries with export surpluses to balanced trade accounts.
Thus, the economy is more focused on demand in the interior.
This requires an end to the cutback policy that promotes the low-wage sector and keeps wages in Europe artificially low.
This exports poverty worldwide and is harmful to the national economy.
Not again!
Hundreds of thousands opposed the planned free trade agreement with the USA, TTIP, because it primarily served the interests of export-oriented companies on both sides of the Atlantic.
We want TTIP to be abandoned for good.
We also reject the agreement with Canada (CETA) and with South American countries (Mercosur).
Ecological and social standards must no longer be neglected.
We reject special rights of action that subordinate democracy and fundamental rights to profit interests.
We want to stop the Energy Charter Treaty, because it prevents the energy transition: Fossil fuel companies use it to sue states when they want to get out of coal, oil and gas.
Across Europe, nearly 350 billion euros of fossil investments are protected by the treaty.
This fuels climate change and makes the cost of combating it extremely high.
Currently, there is a chance to get out of the contract.
Italy already left in 2016, and France and Spain are considering leaving.
Access to universal and public health care and strengthening the human right to health!
Drugs developed through taxpayer-funded research must be made available for post-production royalty-free.
We want to expand research and development to combat the deadliest infectious diseases and frequently neglected diseases such as HIV/AIDS, malaria and tuberculosis.
We call for the development of a global primary health care system with access to the best available therapies.
We demand a solidarity-based pandemic response for all people instead of vaccination nationalism and favoritism of the Global North!
The development of vaccines can only be a joint effort and must not be carried out by pharmaceutical companies to maximize profits.
or only at national level.
The World Health Organization (WHO) must be provided with a broad financial base.
We need vaccines that can be used everywhere, that can be produced quickly, and that are not backed by economic interests - this requires the worldwide development of public vaccine production (see chapter "Breaking the power of the pharmaceutical industry!").
n Ban speculation with food!
Since 2014, the number of hungry people worldwide has been rising again, and this crisis has been exacerbated by the corona pandemic.
Our goal is: Right to food and food sovereignty for all and a ban on patents on seeds!
Food trade should no longer be the responsibility of the World Trade Organization, but of the UN Food and Agriculture Organization.
Overcoming hunger and poverty means securing the livelihoods of farmers and farm workers worldwide!
We want to support regions in not practicing agriculture primarily for export.
There must be an end to food markets being flooded with food from outside - as in the case of food subsidized in the EU.
We want to promote organic production around the world and agree on international systems to protect against price erosion.
Fight land grabbing effectively!
We want to put a stop to large agricultural corporations that make a lot of money from factory farming or the cultivation of monocultures.
We want to ban the import of food produced on stolen land.
We demand an international reappraisal and a ban on land grabbing.
Stolen land must be returned to the original owners.
To promote organic and regional agriculture, German corporations and their international partners involved in land grabbing are to pay compensation.
The raw materials strategy presented by the German government primarily follows the interests of industry.
What is needed, however, is a reduction in the consumption of raw materials.
To this end, we are calling for a new European raw materials strategy.
The dependence of the countries of the South on raw material exports must be ended.
Enable independent development!
International cooperation can help overcome poverty through technology transfer and targeted local business development.
Raw materials should be processed where they are extracted from the earth.
There is no entitlement of European corporations to access to raw materials.
Value creation must be enabled and promoted in the countries of the Global South.
We want data protection and transparency worldwide!
In all areas of technology, we need global cooperation to create a set of rules that establishes binding data protection rules for robotics, data flows and artificial intelligence and makes algorithms transparent.
We support transnational organizations of workers and the formation of international trade union cooperation with the aim of significantly improving the situation of workers.
We reject the efforts of large digital corporations to enshrine their interests in international trade agreements on e-commerce or within the framework of the WTO.
This is intended to deprive states of the ability to regulate and tax the activities of corporations.
We want to secure regulatory and taxation options and enforce minimum standards.
Development through justice
Inequality is increasing worldwide - despite decades of Western "development policy" - and is hampering economic and social development.
Past development policies have not simply failed.
It is an instrument of (post-)colonial oppression and exploitation.
Development cooperation must finally put dignity and solidarity at the center, not own economic interests, - and break the destructive dynamics of boundless capital exploitation.
To this end, we want to strengthen public and civil society structures.
Development cooperation must be geared to the goals of the partner countries and their societies and support them in pursuing independent development paths.
The unequal integration of countries into the world market exacerbates economic crises and also weakens the countries of the Global South politically.
Our plan for development work in solidarity:
Strengthen women's and girls' rights - health and education for all worldwide!
We want to make universal access to effective, high-quality and needs-based health care, including access to one's sexual and reproductive rights, a goal of German and European development cooperation.
We want comprehensive public, free and high-quality basic education for all people.
Right to food and clean water for all!
Food sovereignty and social security are the foundation of security and stability.
This requires strengthening local food markets and agroecological farming practices that preserve farm diversity and protect plant and animal life.
The abuse of agricultural development programs by transnational corporations must be stopped.
The export of highly hazardous pesticides must be banned.
An end to exploitation in the guise of development cooperation!
Development funds must no longer be misused as investment incentives for German or international capital.
We want to discontinue initiatives such as the Marshall Plan with Africa or Compact with Africa.
Development financing from the public sector!
The money for development cooperation must come from public funds.
We want to end the undemocratic influence of private foundations and large investors, as well as public-private partnerships.
We want to strengthen the instrument of budget support.
We want to increase the funds for development cooperation to the amounts pledged.
Not only more, but different!
We want development cooperation to be oriented towards the needs of the people in poorer countries - instead of continuing to serve primarily the interests of European companies!
We reject the interlocking of development and security policy in the sense of so-called border protection and migration control.
Segregation is not a development policy!
Money is to be made available to the countries of the Global South to enable independent development.
We criticize the discontinuation of development cooperation with Cuba and advocate for its resumption.
Climate justice global
The countries of the Global South are particularly affected by climate and environmental degradation, although the main polluters are in the Global North.
According to Oxfam, the richest 10 percent of the world's population produce just as many CO2 emissions as the poorer 50 percent.
The global consequences of climate change are already catastrophic.
Women and children are particularly affected, often lacking the legal or financial resources to protect themselves against climate impacts.
Women are far more affected than average by environmental disasters.
Water shortages, droughts, and floods deprive people of their livelihoods, resulting in distribution struggles over dwindling resources that force more and more people to flee.
This must be brought to an end: The rich must be held accountable.
We need a change of course in trade policy and in the consumption of raw materials.
The Paris climate agreement was a minimal consensus among nations.
However, the reduction volumes pledged so far by the individual countries are nowhere near sufficient to achieve these targets (see chapter "Climate").
Germany, too, must step up its game and - as one of the main contributors to climate change - provide more funding for the Global South so that it can shape its development in a climate-neutral and equitable way.
At UN level, we want to set up a compensation fund for the consequences of climate change and colonialism, financed by the industrialized countries.
Former colonial powers should pay more into this fund than other states.
We want to increase the corresponding climate finance transfers each year.
As long as the countries in the Global South cannot cover their own needs from green electricity, we therefore reject hydrogen imports from these countries (see chapter "Energy transition").
Climate justice instead of greenwashing and selling indulgences!
Increasingly, industrialized countries are outsourcing climate and environmental protection measures, such as forest conservation initiatives, to the Global South, thus shirking their responsibilities.
The deliberate destruction of natural resources such as oceans, rainforests and climate continues to be largely without legal consequences.
DIE LINKE wants to bring the destroyers of the environment, climate and biodiversity to justice.
For this we want the introduction of the offense of ecocide as a crime into German criminal law and into the Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court into international law.
Climate refugees must not be further denied the right to asylum.
In order to live up to the historical responsibility of Western states as the main emitters of climate-damaging greenhouse gases, we also want the EU to offer climate passports to the inhabitants of threatened states that will become uninhabitable as a result of the climate crisis.
They are to be established in addition to, not as an alternative to, existing initiatives and requirements.
Fair taxes worldwide
The rich and corporations must share in the global costs of crises and climate change.
A fair international tax system with a financial transaction tax is needed.
Tax havens must be drained in order to finally give transnational corporations a greater share in the development of the countries from whose exploitation and resources they profit (see chapter on "Fair taxes" and chapter on "Banks and finance").
Double taxation agreements that Germany has signed with many countries in the Global South often prevent fair local taxation, and most of the money flows to Germany.
This must be stopped!
We call for a debt cut and a sustainable debt relief initiative for all countries in the Global South whose debt burden is unsustainable.
Private creditors must be forced to participate in this debt initiative.
We call for the introduction of a sovereign insolvency procedure.
Strengthen UN and international cooperation
A system of stronger cooperation is needed at the international level, but multilateralism is in crisis.
There is an ice age in international relations.
The U.S. and its allies on one side, China and Russia on the other, have blocked the Security Council and the United Nations (UN) in recent years.
The foundations of the UN include peacekeeping and the prevention of conflicts, the protection of human rights, the promotion of social progress and social development as well as international cooperation.
Promoting the goals of the United Nations means ensuring the peaceful settlement of all disputes and renunciation of the use of force, and respecting the equality and national sovereignty of all states.
The UN is supposed to provide the framework for states by setting the rules.
Its 17 development goals (SDGs), including poverty reduction, gender equality, education and health, are to be achieved by 2030.
But the world is far from that today.
Poverty and hunger are growing rapidly due to the corona pandemic: According to UN estimates, up to 235 million people will not have sufficient access to food and drinking water in 2021.
While wealth is piling up on the financial markets, the UN is short of money everywhere.
This makes them dependent on support from private companies and foundations, which primarily pursue their own interests.
The independence and neutrality of the UN is thus undermined.
Recalling the Charter of the United Nations:
"The Organization is founded on the principle of the sovereign equality of all its members.(...)
Every State has the right freely to choose and develop its political, social, economic and cultural order.(...)
All members shall refrain in their international relations from any threat or use of force against the territorial integrity or political independence of any State or otherwise inconsistent with the purposes of the United Nations."
Strengthen and democratize the UN!
The General Assembly must be strengthened vis-à-vis the Security Council.
We therefore reject the demand for a permanent seat for Germany on the Security Council.
The countries of the Global South need more influence!
Social and economic policy competencies, as in the UN Economic and Social Council (ECOSOC), must be strengthened.
Exclusive forums such as the G 7 are to be absorbed into it.
