The United Nations Conference on Trade and Development (UNCTAD) is to be strengthened vis-à-vis the World Trade Organization (WTO) in order to enhance the interests of the Global South in trade and development policy.
The UN's specialized agencies, such as the World Food Program (WFP), the World Health Organization (WHO), the International Labor Organization (ILO), or the Refugee Agency (UNHCR), are unable to adequately address the crises due to underfunding.
The rich member states must finally meet their payment obligations and close the financing gap.
In the case of the UNHCR, we are talking about just under 4 billion euros, only a fraction of German arms spending.
To push back the influence of private players, we want to raise the basic contributions.
UN spending on military operations must be reallocated in favor of funding for hunger relief, peaceful conflict management and civilian crisis prevention.
We support the appeal of UN Secretary General António Guterres for a global ceasefire.
Economic sanctions primarily affect the ordinary population and must be ended.
Unilateral sanctions by the U.S. and EU, such as those against Iran, Cuba, Syria or Russia, are contrary to international law and continue to escalate the situation.
We condemn the blockade of Cuba by the Biden administration and all attempts by the U.S. and the EU to bulldoze away disagreeable governments in Latin America, such as in Venezuela and Bolivia, and to destabilize them through economic sanctions.
In the case of Cuba, an entire country is blocked in its economic development.
Even the German government regularly votes against the U.S. blockade in the UN.
We therefore demand that a new German government finally backs up its words with action and consistently implements the EU blocking regulation of 1996.
DIE LINKE supports the proposal to award the Nobel Peace Prize to the Cuban medical missions.
So far, they have treated 260,000 patients in 40 countries and provided medical care for the population in poor countries - also against Corona and other viruses.
We advocate a peaceful solution to the Middle East conflict based on two independent states of Israel and Palestine and the 1967 borders.
We want to strengthen cooperation with organizations and associations of states in the Global South that are working for people's social concerns, equitable economic development, indigenous rights, peaceful cooperation and regional integration through political cooperation.
Enforce human rights
Human rights are universal and oblige political action.
All human rights are equally important to us: social, economic, cultural and political.
We as the LEFT criticize the violation of human rights everywhere.
We oppose the federal government's double standards.
We want to enforce human rights globally, and international jurisdiction must be strengthened to achieve this.
Peace is a sine qua non for the realization of human rights and comprehensive human development.
We want international law to enshrine the right to peace.
Human rights must not be instrumentalized for warfare.
We want the federal government to sign the Additional Protocol to the International Covenant on Human Rights so that individuals have the option of appealing to the UN.
Basic rights should apply to all people living in Germany and should not be dependent on the German passport.
We want the forces for democracy,
Equal rights
and social justice,
instead of making deals with dictators!
That is why we support the progressive social movements from Kurdistan to Western Sahara to Colombia in their struggle.
Germany must actively support the release of political prisoners.
We want to end the arbitrary criminalization of progressive movements, including by NATO allies and authorities here at home.
We stand in solidarity with persecuted whistleblowers like Chelsea Manning or Edward Snowden and journalists like Julian Assange, who have made public war crimes and millions of illegal worldwide surveillance by the US and are therefore persecuted.
Human rights are fought for as a whole and are indivisible.
As this unity, they must also be realized.
The right to work and to equal pay for equal work must be filled with life.
Right to clean drinking water and to a healthy ecosystem must be understood as human rights.
Let's improve human rights together.
Reappraise German and European colonialism
DIE LINKE demands that German colonialism and its impact in international relations be dealt with until today.
Colonialism must finally be recognized as the rule of injustice.
We want a public debate within federal German institutions as well as support for the anti-colonial culture of remembrance in the former colonies.
To this end, we call for the establishment of a Bundestag Commission of Inquiry and support the initiative to erect a central memorial to the victims of German colonialism at the site of the so-called Africa Conference in Berlin.
The federal government is to establish an institution for the history of colonialism with the involvement of scholars from the former colonies.
In particular, it should shed light on the German role in the African, Asian and South Pacific colonies.
n The German government and the Bundestag must fully recognize the genocide of the Herero and Nama as genocide.
The request for an apology for the genocide in the former German colony of Southwest Africa, announced in May 2021, is only a first step in coming to terms with the past.
The reconstruction and development program announced over a period of 30 years is not compensation, but must be evaluated as technical development assistance.
It is no substitute for a policy of reconciliation and compensation for the suffering of generations of Herero and Nama.
In addition to the Namibian government, the representatives of the affected communities in Namibia must be included in the dialogue on an equal footing on how to deal with the guilt and on compensation.
Culture and natural objects must be returned to the countries of origin.
Only after official approval may artifacts be exhibited as loans in the Federal Republic.
Mortal remains must be returned to the communities of origin.
Research on unlawfully acquired collections must be stopped.
For a Europe based on solidarity!
We are fighting for a social, democratic and peaceful Europe, for another European Union in which everyone can live and work well.
A Europe of solidarity in which all people are protected from poverty.
In which democracy and solidarity, not location competition and profit, come first.
A Europe in which corporations and the rich finally pay their share to finance the common good.
For an EU that does not make deals with dictators
and multinational corporations,
which outlaws war as a means of politics
and prevents people from drowning in the Mediterranean.
We want a Union that finally advances climate protection and an energy and transport turnaround instead of blocking them.
We want a peaceful Europe without an arms race.
We demand minimum social standards,
good health care
and education for all.
We must meet the ecological challenges
with a response to social problems.
But the EU Commission has imposed a "Green Deal" with which the EU is not even able to achieve its climate targets.
That is why we want to change course - with a socio-ecological system change in Europe.
The must create the transformation of the economy with massive public investment in good jobs, innovation for climate-neutral production and infrastructure.
The natural foundations of life and common goods such as water, energy, air, a clean environment and our health must no longer be subordinated to the profit interests of a few.
We argue for a sensible regionalization of the flow of goods.
Europe finally needs higher taxes for the rich and corporations.
Money from the EU budget must be reallocated: Instead of military rearmament, it
must be invested in solidarity-based and ecological projects for the future.
Because we need a historic show of force to stop the climate catastrophe
and at the same time bring all people with us.
We are fighting for the redistribution of wealth,
for gender equality
and democracy,
for a new industrial strategy
and a sustainable public infrastructure in Europe -
for a good future for all.
For the EU, the corona pandemic is the second severe shock after the financial crisis.
For countless people, it once again means loss of income, existential angst and destroyed life plans.
Member countries have tried to keep the crisis at bay and cushion it socially through economic measures.
The EU Commission suspended the deficit restrictions of the EU's Stability and Growth Pact.
However, as a result of the cutback policies of recent years, public services are underfunded.
Banks were bailed out with billions, but hospitals were cut to the bone.
Hundreds of thousands of people have died, partly because they could not be adequately treated.
The split between Northern and Southern, Eastern and Western Europe is growing.
Germany's policy of low wages and export success at any price has helped cause the crisis and has also increased inequality and competition within the EU.
Austerity, privatization, social cuts and deindustrialization have destroyed jobs,
created poverty and
thus boosted right-wing populism.
No country can meet the challenges of climate change and global social justice alone.
We need to find cross-border - global - solutions.
All this shows: It is high time for a social and solidary Europe!
Unlike in the financial crisis of 2008/2009, the EU has not yet reacted to the crisis with a dictate of cutbacks.
But there is a great danger that the EU will fall back into the old policy of cuts after the crisis.
Because the dictate of the black zero is only suspended.
It is therefore clear that we need a paradigm shift, away from cuts, free trade agreements and market radicalism, towards public investment, cross-border cooperation and solidarity.
Away from rearmament
and toward sensible investments and a consistent policy of détente and peace.
This policy change must begin in Berlin.
We want an EU that is committed to a system of international cooperation on an equal footing.
We want an EU whose foreign policy is characterized by peaceful cooperation and not by the violent enforcement of economic interests.
The Maastricht and Lisbon Treaties inscribed neoliberalism into the foundations of the Union.
We want new treaties to make the EU more social,
fairer
and more ecological.
This is the only way the Union has a common future.
We are working for this future together with social movements, with trade unions, with the European Left and other parties.
Trade unions and movements, the commitment for the climate, for democracy and women's rights and against racism everywhere show: Together we can change Europe.
Investing instead of blocking the future!
The EU budget and reconstruction and aid funds fall far short of what would be needed to address the consequences of the pandemic and redirect for a just and carbon-neutral future.
Parts of the EU budget are hidden subsidies for large corporations.
It was mainly the rich who profited from this.
It is particularly negligent that investments and health spending were cut from the reconstruction package.
For the economy is crippled,
many countries are plagued by mass unemployment,
and the infrastructure has long been driven to wear and tear.
We want money for investments in the future instead of for rearmament.
What might be too much for individual states to handle is quite feasible for the European community of states as a whole, because with its great economic power and the European Central Bank (ECB) behind it, it has sufficient economic strength.
The Stability and Growth Pact curtails democracy in the individual member states and locks them into a neoliberal fiscal policy.
We want to change that: The EU needs an investment offensive without handbrakes.
Deficit and debt rules need to be adjusted.
For the EU to have a future, we need to address the deficits that really matter:
The investment backlog in the welfare state,
in education,
the infrastructure,
on the labor market
and climate protection.
In view of the challenges posed by Corona and climate catastrophe, the EU budget must be expanded by issuing European bonds.
In view of the biggest slump in the global economy in decades, a volume of 1 to 2 trillion euros is required for the European investment and spending program.
A socio-ecological investment program is needed!
The EU's financial resources must be expanded and used in a targeted manner for the economically weaker countries, regions, sectors and for future tasks such as a socio-ecological industrial policy, healthcare, digital infrastructure, education and research as well as the energy and transport turnaround.
Troika and austerity are expressions for the unsolidary EU.
The competencies of the EU Commission to control and steer the allocation of funds must be limited and the European Parliament must be more involved.
Democratic control of the use of EU funds must take place at the European level.
In the process, no more cutbacks may be imposed, such as the dismantling of labor rights.
We call for debt cuts and meaningful investment programs for the poorer regions of Europe.
We reject the fact that the allocation of funds from the EU Reconstruction Fund is tied to conditions that in effect turn the recommendations of the EU Commission within the framework of the European Semester into regulations.
Without compensatory measures, the euro, as a common currency of very different economic areas, increases the imbalance between the rich states in Northern and Western Europe vis-à-vis the states in Southern Europe.
We need to build a fair and common European economy instead of continuing the competition.
Europe-wide: Distributing wealth from top to bottom
Investments for the future cost money.
But the good news is: money is there - it's just misallocated.
After all, the companies that make the biggest profits still pay the least taxes in Europe.
Even large fortunes are hardly taxed.
Tax avoidance and tax havens are booming.
The result: While the rich are getting richer and richer, especially in the Corona crisis, the poverty of the majority of people is growing.
Enough of this!
There needs to be an EU-wide minimum tax rate for companies with broad and uniform tax bases.
We call for common minimum standards for the taxation of large assets and top incomes.
The fight against tax evasion must be stepped up.
We will revoke the licenses of banks that operate in tax havens.
European own resources are needed, for example from a financial transaction tax.
Digital corporations like Google and Amazon make billions in profits and pay hardly any taxes.
We will finally make them pay!
Democratically controlling the European Central Bank and using it socially and ecologically
The European Central Bank (ECB) must finally be oriented toward the common good instead of the criterion of competitiveness.
The ECB must enable socio-ecological investments by member states and make them independent of the goodwill of the financial markets.
For this, it would already suffice if the ECB guaranteed the solvency of the member states by being obliged to be the lender of last resort.
There is no inflationary risk because the ECB remains committed to its inflation target.
The EU treaties must be amended to allow the ECB to finance the state.
We want the ECB to be democratically controlled by the European Parliament - instead of continuing to be at the mercy of the influence of financial lobbyists.
The ECB must not continue to buy bonds from companies with high CO2 emissions and thereby undermine climate protection.
It needs strong social and environmental standards.
This also applies to corona aids.
Transforming the economy
We must not carry on as before after the crisis.
We want to make Europe fairer
and advance a socio-ecological system change.
We want social-ecological transformation to be possible in all member states.
Our goal is to make power generation, industry, transport, buildings and agriculture climate-neutral without leaving people or regions behind (see chapter "For a socio-ecological system change").
The recent increase in the EU's greenhouse gas reduction target from 40 to 55 percent compared to 1990 is still too low to meet the goals of the Paris climate agreement.
We want to make the EU climate-neutral by 2035 at the latest.
Investments: The EU has squeezed the programs for equitable restructuring from 40 billion euros to 17.5 billion euros - restructuring cannot succeed like this.
We want to strengthen the Just Transition Fund.
It is intended to provide social security for people working in areas such as mining and climate-damaging industries, especially in disadvantaged regions, and to open up new career prospects for them.
To combat mass unemployment, poverty and a lack of prospects, a consistent European full employment policy and a genuine industrial strategy are needed.
It must aim for climate neutrality and, above all, give de-industrialized regions a future.
Energy transition: The coal phase-out must begin immediately throughout Europe and be completed by 2030.
We don't want new fossil fuel infrastructure.
Renewable energies must be expanded
- close to the people
and in public or cooperative ownership.
We advocate the establishment of an alternative "European Community for the Promotion of Renewable Energies and Energy Saving".
We reject nuclear power and fracking.
Transport turnaround: A European mobility revolution is needed.
This can be done if we expand bus and rail services and drastically reduce prices, create networked mobility and promote short distances.
Instead of air routes, we want to expand rail connections.
A large proportion of freight traffic and intra-European air traffic must be shifted to rail.
Agricultural turnaround: We focus on sustainable agriculture and regional cycles instead of long transport routes and industrial mass production.
The system of EU agricultural subsidies is not sustainable, we want to orient subsidies to social and ecological criteria and no longer to the area.
We want to end export subsidies for agricultural products.
Social security and good work
All people must be able to live from their work.
But politics in the EU puts corporate interests ahead of those of most people.
The result is poverty, wage dumping and exploitation.
The rise in youth unemployment is dramatic; in Spain and Greece it threatens to rise to 40 percent as a result of the Corona crisis.
Almost every second young person looking for a job comes up empty.
Corporate profits must no longer take precedence over workers' labor rights and people's basic social rights.
We demand for all citizens in the EU social rights and minimum wages that secure the existence.
The principle of "equal pay for equal work in the same place" must be enshrined in law to prevent wage dumping.
Seasonal workers can work in Germany without social security for 100 days.
We want all people working in Germany and Europe to be well insured and want social insurance for everyone and from day one.
We want statutory minimum wages of at least 60 percent of the median wage in the respective country.
In addition, minimum regulations are needed to protect and promote collective agreements and trade union rights.
We want co-determination rights and the rights of trade unions and employees to be restored and expanded.
We therefore join with the European Trade Union Confederation in calling for the introduction of a European framework directive to safeguard corporate codetermination.
Enforce social security!
We want social security with binding minimum social security and minimum social standards - in case of doubt, the better standard applies (favorability clause).
Freedom of movement for all!
Unequal living conditions force young people in particular to migrate.
No one should be excluded from social benefits because of this,
human rights are indivisible,
and the subsistence level is non-negotiable.
We want to help people find Good Work.
Democracy instead of lobbyist rule
We need more democracy in Europe.
Many people have turned away from the EU in disappointment in recent years.
There is a lack of trust; for many people, the EU is far away.
Because democracy is more than an election every five years.
We want a European Union that takes fundamental rights seriously and defends them.
Democracy must no longer be subordinated to the financial markets.
We reject all attacks on democracy in Europe, for example by establishing rights of penetration over national budgets.
We need a peaceful, social, democratic and ecological EU - with new treaties, new structures, new hopes.
This means a strong European Parliament and extensive opportunities for participation.
That's why we want a new constitution for Europe that citizens can help shape and on which they can decide simultaneously in referendums in all EU member states.
We want the European Parliament to have the right of initiative and to be able to introduce its own legislative proposals.
Fundamental decisions must be made by the European Parliament - rather than by executive bodies such as the Commission, Eurogroup or Council.
In addition, MEPs should be able to elect and vote out the Commission President and Commissioners.
The European Council plays a decisive role in determining the legislative process in the EU, but its work is not transparent; as a result, national governments often act without democratic control.
We want to finally commit the Council to transparency.
We want decisions to be made at the levels that are most affected: local affairs in the municipalities, federal affairs in the national parliaments, European affairs in the EU Parliament.
No limits for democracy!
The high hurdles for European citizens' initiatives must be lowered:
We want to enable EU-wide referendums and plebiscites.
All people should have the same rights in the EU countries in which they live.
We want the state of democracy, the rule of law and fundamental rights in the EU to be regularly evaluated and violations to be sanctioned.
There needs to be more commitment to democracy
and human rights in all member states.
We want current and future EU accession candidates to commit to democracy without reservation.
and human rights.
This applies in particular to the accession candidate Turkey.
The current government of Turkey must implement the rulings of the European Court of Human Rights, guarantee democracy and freedom of expression, end the persecution of the democratic opposition and release all imprisoned parliamentarians and mayors of the opposition Kurdish party HDP.
We want the EU to accede to the European Convention on Human Rights.
The common foreign and security policy must also be controlled by the European Court of Human Rights.
Fundamental social rights must become enforceable for individuals before the European Court of Justice.
We want all decisions and the processes leading to them to be made transparent.
So far, lobbyists often influence political decisions in the EU without citizens being able to find out about it.
We call for an EU transparency register and a transparency regulation.
European policy of détente instead of rearmament
The EU's response to the crises is, of all things, to rearm.
Economic development is practiced as arms promotion.
Dictators are business partners in arms deals and are glorified as anchors of stability.
The expansion of a "military union", the creation of an additional European army and arms exports, however, do not lead to more security for the people.
The so-called Permanent Structured (Military) Cooperation (PESCO for short) is supposed to ensure that billions are spent on armaments while there is an enormous lack of arms control and civil conflict management.
The participating states are committed to a steady increase in their defense budgets and investments, participation in large-scale armament projects and the establishment of European troop formations.
With the European Peace Facility (EFF), the European Union itself becomes a supplier of arms and ammunition.
We want a peaceful Europe and a Union of disarmament
that promotes democracy instead of doing business with dictators.
We advocate a European policy of peace and détente
and want to end the militarization of the EU.
Security is only possible with a consistent peace policy
and promoting global justice instead of competition between locations.
We want to abolish the EU arms agency and advocate an EU-wide ban on arms exports.
Exports to authoritarian regimes like Egypt and Turkey must be stopped immediately.
We reject the plans for a European defense union and cooperation between the EU and NATO.
The expansion of a "defense union" or "military union" with an independent military policy, a European army and other projects of militarization do not lead to more security for the people in Europe, but only secure corporate interests militarily.
We want to dissolve the Euratom Treaty and detach it from the treaty foundations of the EU, because it blocks a sustainable, socially and democratically designed energy transition.
We reject the European Defense Fund.
It is intended to channel billions from the joint EU budget into defense research and development.
This only benefits the arms industry and promotes neither security nor peace.
Instead of a planned expansion through the participation of third countries, we call for the termination of PESCO and all military-related EU programs and funds, such as the European Peace Facility (EFF).
We want to invest the money in social cohesion,
Climate protection
and global justice.
Human rights instead of Fortress Europe
The EU Commission wants to push through a "migration pact" that further aims at closure, deportation and disenfranchisement.
The German government supports this approach.
We oppose it.
It is not compatible with a solidary and humane Europe that thousands of people drown on the run in the Mediterranean Sea or are imprisoned in lawless spaces in reception camps and deportation centers at and in front of the borders of the EU.
We oppose cooperation for the purpose of sealing off the EU with authoritarian regimes, as in the inhumane EU-Turkey deal or the agreement with the Libyan coast guard: they are not part of the solution, but part of the problem.
DIE LINKE wants to save people, clear escape routes and fight the causes of flight (see chapter "Solidary Immigration Society"):
Without the border protection agency and coast guard Frontex, with legal escape routes.
With legal certainty and enforcement of the Refugee Convention, the Convention on the Rights of the Child and the European Convention on Human Rights.
Without deprivation of liberty and pushbacks into torture and death (see chapter "Defending Humanity").
How we change the country
DIE LINKE fights for social justice
and peace,
we fight for a restructuring of economy and society that puts the people all over the world in the center: the employees, pensioners, the unemployed - and the people of tomorrow, our children and grandchildren.
We want to hand over to them a livable, inclusive and climate-just society.
With a well-equipped public service, in which what is there for everyone also belongs to everyone.
With places that promote democratic exchange,
make social cohesion tangible,
and open up access and participation in social wealth to all.
On a viable planet, with good air to breathe.
We will do everything in our power to achieve the goal of limiting global warming to 1.5 degrees
- and to change the economy and society in a socially and climate-friendly way.
We want to encourage people.
We want to win social majorities for five points.
They are realistic and radical.
They improve the lives of the majority - and at the same time set the course for a different society.
These are decisive steps towards a social
and ecological future.
We will only participate in a government that is measured by the following:
1.There was much applause in the pandemic, but little change in wages.
What is needed are higher wages and secure rather than precarious work.
To combat the low-wage sector, we need a minimum wage that protects against poverty now and in old age,
the conversion of mini-jobs into socially insured work,
and nationwide collective agreements.
The statutory pension must be designed in such a way that no one has to live below the poverty line, and the retirement age must be lowered again.
Hartz IV must be free of poverty and sanctions.
Without taxing millionaires, there can be no policy change.
Without a wealth tax, the necessary investments in affordable housing, educational equality and climate protection cannot be financed fairly.
2. instead of warm words, the colleagues in the care sector finally get better pay, more staff and a statutory needs-oriented staffing level.
Hospitals and care facilities must be returned to public and community-oriented ownership throughout the country.
The flat rates per case must be abolished.
The rent cap in Berlin has shown that rents do not have to keep rising.
The rent cap was cashed because the Federal Constitutional Court is of the opinion that this is not the task of a federal state, but of the Federal Parliament for the entire country.
We see that as a mission.
With us, there will be a rent cap for all municipalities with a tight housing market.
A program for the construction of permanently affordable housing is also needed
- in public and cooperative hands.
4 For us, consistent climate protection
and social justice together - because it is precisely the poor who will suffer most from climate change.
A turnaround is needed toward investing in the future for a climate-neutral economy
and good jobs for all.
Hundreds of thousands of well-paid, future-proof jobs can be created in schools, daycare centers, health care, through the energy turnaround and the socio-ecological restructuring of industry.
We will massively increase investment in buses and trains and make tickets significantly cheaper.
The spiral of rearmament devours taxpayers' money that is needed for social welfare and climate protection and further fuels the danger of new wars.
We need a change in peace policy: Away from the 2 percent target of the NATO countries, toward a policy of détente.
Arms spending must be reduced, arms exports stopped and the Bundeswehr's foreign deployments ended.
We will fight the causes of flight, not the refugees.
All people who live here permanently should receive the same social rights.
We want change for social security,
Peace
and climate justice.
We will drive this change as a rebellious part of a center-left government or from the opposition to set the political agenda.
DIE LINKE wants to make this federal election a decision on direction.
At last, a majority for a progressive government in Germany seems possible.
This majority and all the improvements it promises are only possible with the LEFT.
We are ready for that.
We want to take responsibility for a socio-ecological policy change in Germany.
We want to govern to change!
A different policy is not significantly made in the parliament.
It needs pressure from society, from trade unions, social and climate movements, NGOs, social and environmental associations and the peace movement.
Pressure from below and pressure from the street.
DIE LINKE is anchored in these movements.
Together, we can shift the balance of power in society to the left.
We are the address in parliament that is free of corporate and lobby interests.
We give a voice to those who are overheard by the other parties.
We promise: DIE LINKE accepts no corporate donations, no party sponsorship and no large private donations.
The deputies of the LEFT stand for the goals and projects presented here.
They declare that they do not accept donations or gifts from lobby groups or large corporations.
Citizens' will and the common good take precedence over individual interests!
All additional income is disclosed;
that they do not cooperate with secret services
and against the dismantling of democracy;
that they use information and knowledge from their parliamentary activities in the general interest.
We are not a backroom party.
Freedom of information instead of secrecy!
that they make the resources and infrastructure of MPs' offices available to the local population, social movements or solidarity and aid projects.
climate protection in all policy areas
and social justice together and prioritize them.
The members of parliament will work to ensure that in the future they, along with the self-employed and civil servants, pay into the statutory pension fund and into a solidarity-based comprehensive health and long-term care insurance scheme, and that the contribution assessment limits - insofar as they are constitutionally permissible - are abolished.
Fridays for Future has called for climate justice and economic transformation worldwide.
The nurses' protests have put the nursing emergency on the agenda.
Employees organize themselves under adverse conditions and strike for their interests, for good work that fits in with life, and a future that can be planned.
In many places, tenants are fighting against rising rents and housing shortages.
These concerns are our program.
We want to enforce improvements in the everyday lives of the vast majority of people and join them on the path to a social,
climate-friendly society.
Let's change the country together.
Give the LEFT party your vote: Together we are strong to assert the interests of the many against the profit interests of the few.
Let's fight together for new social majorities.
For a social,
ecological
and peace policy awakening!
